Witness Requirements for Eid al-Adha: The Hanafi Dispute
Dispute over witness requirements for Eid al-Adha crescent.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the relied-upon Hanafi position on the number of witnesses required for the crescent of Eid al-Adha and evaluate the conflicting narration from Abu Hanifa.

Core Idea
Eid al-Adha requires two witnesses or one man and two women because the benefit is attached to the servant.

In this lesson, we examine a subtle dispute within the Hanafi school regarding the crescent of Eid al-Adha. While Eid al-Fitr clearly requires two male witnesses or one male and two females when the sky is cloudy, the ruling for Eid al-Adha is contested. The relied-upon view equates it to Eid al-Fitr, but a narration from Imam Abu Hanifa suggests a single witness suffices. Understanding the basis of this ikhtilaf sharpens your ability to weigh evidence within the madhhab.

Guided Path
1
State the two conflicting positions
Identify the Zahir al-Riwayah position (two men or one man and two women) and the narrated view from Abu Hanifa (single witness).
The dispute is only for cloudy skies.
2
Examine the basis for each position
Zahir al-Riwayah views the benefit (naf‘) as individual, thus analogizing to private rights. Abu Hanifa's narration sees collective benefit, similar to Ramadan.
The key distinction is between naf‘ al-‘abd (individual benefit) and maslahah ‘ammah (collective benefit).
3
Identify the tarjih mechanism
Zahir al-Riwayah is the most authoritative transmission (al-asahh) and is mufta bihi.
This is a classic example of preferring the zahir al-riwayah over a solitary narration.
4
Apply the thamarah al-khilaf
If a single witness reports, according to the relied-upon view, testimony is rejected and fasting continues; according to the other narration, fasting ends.
This practical difference affects the day of Eid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِذَا كَانَ بِالسَّمَاءِ عِلَّةٌ لَمْ تُقْبَلُ فِي هِلَالِ الْفِطْرِ إِلَّا شَهَادَةُ رَجُلَيْنِ أَوْ رَجُلٍ وَامْرَأَتَيْنِ لِأَنَّهُ تَعَلَّقَ بِهِ نَفْعُ الْعَبْدِ وَهُوَ الْفِطَرُ فَاشْبَهَ سَائِرَ حُقُوقِهِ وَالْأضْحَى كَالْفِطْرِ فِى هَذَا فِى ظَاهِرِ الرّوَايَةِ وَهُوَ الْاصَحُ خِلَافًا لِمَا رُوِيَ عَنْ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ أَنَّهُ كَهَلَالِ رَمَضَانَ لِأَنَّهُ تَعَلَّقَ بِهِ نَفْعُ الْعِبَادِ وَهُوَ التَّوَسُّعُ بِلُحُومِ الْأَضَاحِي
And when there is a cloud in the sky, the testimony is not accepted regarding the crescent of al-Fitr except the testimony of two men or one man and two women, because the benefit of the servant is attached to it, which is breaking the fast, so it resembles the rest of his rights. And al-Adha is like al-Fitr in this regard in the apparent narration (Zahir al-Riwayah), and this is the most correct, contrary to what has been narrated from Abu Hanifa that it is like the crescent of Ramadan, because the benefit of the servants is attached to it, which is expansion through the meat of sacrifices.
Source pages p. 202

Commentary
This passage addresses the required number of witnesses for establishing the crescent of Eid al-Fitr when the sky is cloudy. The ruling is that testimony from two men or one man and two women is accepted. The rationale is that Eid al-Fitr involves a right of the servant (the benefit of breaking the fast), so it is analogized to other financial rights and contracts. The witnesses must be free and not previously convicted of slander (qadhf), and they must explicitly use the word 'shahadah'. The passage then discusses Eid al-Adha: according to Zahir al-Riwayah (the relied-upon transmission), the same rule applies as for Eid al-Fitr – two men or one man and two women. This is considered the correct position (al-asahh). However, there is a narration from Imam Abu Hanifa that Eid al-Adha is like Ramadan, meaning a single witness is sufficient because the benefit is collective (expansion through meat). The Zahir al-Riwayah position is preferred because the benefit is still attached to individual rights to some extent.

Key Terms
نفع العبد (naf‘ al-‘abd): A personal benefit or right belonging to an individual, as opposed to purely divine rights
ظاهر الرواية (Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah): The most authoritative transmission in the Hanafi school, attributed to Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani's six books
الأصح (al-asahh): The most correct position in the school, often used to prefer one view over another

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon view (Zahir al-Riwayah), which of the following testimonies is sufficient for establishing the crescent of Eid al-Adha when the sky is cloudy?
A) One man
B) Two women
C) One man and one woman
D) One man and two women

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position equates Eid al-Adha with Eid al-Fitr regarding witness requirements: two men or one man and two women.

Moon Sighting on a Clear Sky: Requirement of a Large Group
Ruling on moon sighting in clear conditions with intra-Hanafi dissent.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on moon sighting when the sky is clear and explain the exception according to Imam Tahawi.

Core Idea
In clear conditions, certainty requires a crowd; one or two witnesses do not suffice.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a critical question: how many witnesses are needed to establish the sighting of the Ramadan moon when the sky is clear? Unlike cloudy conditions where a single just witness may be accepted, a clear sky demands a large group to produce certainty. The author draws an analogy from the law of oaths in murder cases. A significant intra-Hanafi difference is also noted, showing the school's internal diversity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being ruled upon (moon sighting for Ramadan/Eid) and the ruling (wajib to base fasting on a report that yields certainty). When sky is clear, a large group is required.
2
Locate the analogy (qiyas)
The author draws an analogy from the case of fifty oaths in murder: just as certainty about the killer requires fifty oaths, so certainty about the moon requires a large group.
This is a qiyas jali, comparing one type of certainty to another.
3
Identify the condition
The key condition is that the sky is clear (mutla saaf) – no clouds, dust, or smoke. If the sky is clear, obstacles to sighting are minimal, so a higher standard of proof is needed.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Imam Tahawi holds that one witness from outside the city suffices because there are fewer obstacles. He also allows one witness from inside the city if they saw from a high place.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The majority view (Al-Marghinani and others) requires a large group for clear skies. This is the relied-upon position for fatwa.
Imam Tahawi's view is noted but not adopted as the operative ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد سوم
كتاب الصوم
یہاں پچاس افراد کی قسم سے قاتل کے بارے میں لاعلمی کا یقین ہو جاتا ہے اسی طرح چاند کے بارے میں بھی پچاس افراد کے دیکھنے سے رؤیت ثابت ہو جائے گی۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر مطلع صاف ہو تو ایک دو آدمی کی گواہی قبول نہ ہوگی جب تک جماعت کثیرہ نہ ہو اب وہ گواہی دینے والے حضرات وہ ہوں جنہوں نے شہر اور آبادی میں چاند دیکھا ہے یا وہ ہوں جو شہر کے باہر دیکھ کر آتے ہیں بہر صورت مطلع صاف ہونے کی صورت میں جماعت کثیرہ کا دیکھنا شرط ہے۔ امام طحاوی نے فرمایا کہ چاند دیکھ کر آنے والا اگر آبادی کے باہر سے دیکھ کر آیا ہے تو ایک آدمی کی شہادت بھی قبول کر لی جائے گی کیونکہ شہر سے باہر موانع رؤیت کم ہیں یعنی شہر کے اندر تو دھواں ، گرد وغبار ہوتا ہے لیکن باہر کچھ نہیں ہوتا اس لئے اس کا قول قبول کر لیا جائے گا کتاب الاستحسان میں اسی قول کی طرف اشارہ ملتا ہے اور امام طحاوی کے نزدیک اس طرح اگر کسی نے شہر کے اندر کسی بلند جگہ کھڑے ہو کر چاند دیکھا ہو تو ایک آدمی کی گواہی قبول کر لی جائے گی ۔ عید کے چاند میں ایک عادل کی گواہی معتبر نہیں
(Beginning of book of fasting) Here, with an oath of fifty individuals, certainty of ignorance about the killer is achieved. Similarly, for the moon, sighting is established by fifty individuals seeing it. The author of Hidayah says: If the horizon is clear, the testimony of one or two people will not be accepted until there is a large group. Now those witnesses are either those who saw the moon inside the city and settlement, or those who come after seeing it outside the city. In any case, when the sky is clear, seeing by a large group is a condition. Imam Tahawi said: If the one who saw the moon came from outside the settlement, then the testimony of one person will also be accepted because outside the city there are fewer obstacles to sighting—that is, inside the city there is smoke, dust, etc., but outside there is none. Therefore, his statement will be accepted. In Kitab al-Istihsan, there is an indication of this opinion. According to Imam Tahawi, similarly, if someone saw the moon standing in a high place inside the city, the testimony of one person will be accepted. For the moon of Eid, the testimony of a single just person is not valid.
Source pages p. 202

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on moon sighting for Ramadan and Eid when the sky is clear. The author explains that when there are no obstructions, a single witness is insufficient; a large group whose report produces certainty is required. This is analogous to testimony in murder cases where fifty oaths are needed. The passage then mentions a difference: Imam Tahawi holds that if the moon is seen outside the city, one witness suffices because obstacles are fewer. Inside the city, unless from a high place, one witness is not enough. The ruling is based on precaution (ihtiyat) to avoid error. The Hanafi school generally requires multiple witnesses for moon sighting in clear conditions, but exceptions exist for witnesses from outside the city.

Key Terms
مطلع صاف (mutla saaf): Clear horizon without clouds, dust, or smoke.
جماعت کثیرہ (jamaat kathirah): A large group whose report gives certainty of knowledge.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When the sky is clear, what is required for moon sighting to establish the start of Ramadan?
A) One just witness
B) Two just witnesses
C) A large group whose report gives certainty
D) Fifty witnesses

Key Takeaway
When the sky is clear, the Hanafi school requires a large group for moon sighting to ensure certainty, though Imam Tahawi allows a single witness from outside the city.

One Person Seeing Eid Crescent Must Not Break Fast
Ruling on individual who sees Eid moon alone

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for a lone individual who sights the Eid crescent, apply the principle of ihtiyat (precaution), and distinguish it from the Ramadan moon-sighting rule.

Core Idea
A lone moon-sighting for Eid does not permit breaking fast; precaution keeps the obligation intact.

Imagine you are alone on a hilltop and you see the new moon of Eid al-Fitr. Do you break your fast immediately? The Hanafi school says no—you must continue fasting out of precaution. This ruling, based on ihtiyat, protects the integrity of worship while resolving doubt. Let's examine the exact ruling, its proof, and how it differs from the case of Ramadan.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its subject
The act in question is breaking the fast (iftar) upon sighting the Eid crescent. The subject is a single individual who sees the moon alone, with no other witnesses.
Note that the ruling applies whether the sky is clear or not—no distinction is made.
2
State the Hanafi ruling
The ruling: such a person must NOT break his fast. If he does break, qada (make-up) becomes wajib, but no kaffarah (expiation) is required. The precaution (ihtiyat) is to avoid terminating an act of worship on uncertain grounds.
This is the mufta bihi (operative) position from Zahir al-Riwayah.
3
Understand the dalil (proof)
The proof is the general principle of ihtiyat in worship: when evidence is doubtful, the safer path is chosen. For exiting an obligation, stronger evidence is needed than for entering it.
This is a zanni (probative) dalil, not a direct nass.
4
Contrast with Ramadan moon-sighting
For the start of Ramadan, one reliable witness suffices to make fasting obligatory for others. The ihtiyat here is towards obligation, not towards continuation. The difference lies in the nature of the benefit: for Eid, the benefit is worldly (breaking the fast), so caution requires more evidence to terminate; for Ramadan, the benefit is religious (observing the fast), so caution requires less evidence to begin.
This distinction is a key nuance in Hanafi fiqh.
5
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Now apply: if you see the Eid moon alone and break your fast, what must you do? You must make up one day (qada), but you do not owe kaffarah. The fast itself remains valid until the point you broke it? Actually, the ruling teaches that the original fast must be completed, so breaking it is a sin (though the text doesn't explicitly say sin, but the wajib of qada indicates a deficiency).
Practice: state the ruling for a similar scenario, e.g., seeing the moon of Eid through a telescope alone.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَنْ رَأَى هِلَالَ الْفِطْرِ وَحْدَهُ لَمْ يُفْطِرُ احْتِيَاطًا وَ فِي الصَّوْمِ الْاِحْتِيَاطُ فِي الْإِيجَابِ ترجمہ اور جس شخص نے اکیلے عید کا چاند دیکھا تو وہ احتیاطاً افطار نہ کرے اور بلال صوم کی صورت میں احتیاط روزہ واجب کرنے میں ہے۔
تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی نے عید کا چاند دیکھا خواہ مطلع صاف ہو یا مطلع صاف نہ ہو تو وہ شخص احتیاطاً افطار نہ کرے اور اگر افطار کر لیا تو اس پر قضا واجب ہوگی اور روزہ توڑنے سے کفارہ واجب نہ ہوگا اور رمضان کے چاند کی صورت میں احتیاط روزہ واجب کرنے میں ہے چنانچہ رمضان کا چاند تنہا ایک آدمی کے دیکھنے کی گواہی پر روزہ واجب کیا گیا ہے۔
And whoever sees the crescent of Fitr alone does not break his fast out of precaution, and in fasting, precaution is in making it obligatory. Translation: And the person who saw the moon of Eid alone, he should not break his fast out of precaution, and in the case of Ramadan, precaution is in making the fast obligatory. Explanation: The matter is that if someone saw the moon of Eid, whether the horizon is clear or not, that person should not break his fast out of precaution. And if he broke his fast, then qada (make-up) becomes obligatory on him, and expiation (kaffarah) is not obligatory for breaking the fast. And in the case of the moon of Ramadan, precaution is in making the fast obligatory. Thus, the moon of Ramadan is made obligatory on the testimony of a single person seeing it.
Source pages p. 202

Commentary
This passage is a ruling about a lone individual who sees the crescent of Eid al-Fitr. The ruling states that such a person should not break his fast out of precaution (ihtiyat). Even if he sees it alone, he must continue fasting until the end of the day. If he breaks the fast, he must make it up (qada) but no expiation is required. This is because the benefit (manfa'ah) in Eid is personal? Actually, the precaution is to avoid error. In contrast, for Ramadan, one witness is sufficient to make fasting obligatory for others, as precaution is in obligating the fast. The commentary explains the difference: for Eid, the benefit is worldly (breaking the fast), so more caution is needed in terminating the obligation; for Ramadan, the benefit is religious (observing the fast), so less evidence is needed to start.

Key Terms
احتیاط (ihtiyat): Precaution; choosing the safer option to avoid error in worship.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person alone sees the moon of Eid al-Fitr, what must he do?
A) Break his fast immediately
B) Continue fasting and break if others confirm
C) Continue fasting and not break, even if certain
D) Break and make up later

Key Takeaway
A lone sighting of the Eid crescent does not permit breaking the fast; precaution demands continuation until official confirmation.

Witness Requirements for Moon Sighting: Eid al-Adha on Cloudy Nights
Intra-Hanafi dispute on moon sighting for Eid al-Adha when cloudy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on moon sighting for Eid al-Adha when cloudy, distinguish between Zahir al-Riwayah and Nawadir, and apply the reasoning to determine the mufta bihi.

Core Idea
The nature of the benefit (worldly vs. religious) determines if one witness suffices or complete testimony is required.

When the sky is cloudy on the 29th of the Islamic month, the standard leniency for Ramadan moon sighting (one witness) does not automatically apply to the Eids. This passage from Al-Hidayah examines an intra-Hanafi dispute: should Eid al-Adha be treated like Eid al-Fitr (requiring two men or one man and two women) or like Ramadan (requiring only one just man)? The answer hinges on whether the attached benefit is worldly or religious. Understanding this distinction is essential for muftis determining Islamic dates.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core issue
The dispute is about the number and composition of witnesses needed to confirm the moon of Eid al-Adha when the sky is cloudy. Note that for Eid al-Fitr, the ruling is settled: complete testimony (two men or one man and two women) is required. The question is whether Eid al-Adha follows the same rule or is treated like Ramadan (one witness).
The sky condition triggers the need for fewer witnesses? No, for Ramadan one witness suffices even when clear; for cloudy it's the same. So the leniency is not weather-dependent but occasion-dependent.
2
State the Zahir al-Riwayah position
According to the relied-upon books of Imam Muhammad (Zahir al-Riwayah), Eid al-Adha is treated exactly like Eid al-Fitr: when the sky is cloudy, only the testimony of two men or one man and two women is accepted. This is the position that the author of Al-Hidayah declares as 'al-asahh' (the most correct).
This ruling applies provided the witnesses are free, just, Muslim, not hadd-punished for qadhf, and testify using the word 'shahada'.
3
Identify the Nawadir counter-position
In the Nawadir (rare transmissions), Imam Abu Hanifa is reported to hold that Eid al-Adha is like Ramadan: the moon is established by the testimony of a single just man. The basis is that the benefit attached is religious (appearance of Hajj time), similar to Ramadan's benefit of worshipping through fasting.
The Nawadir view is not the relied-upon position for fatwa.
4
Analyze the proofs: qiyas on benefit
Both sides use qiyas (analogy). Zahir al-Riwayah argues: the benefit of Eid al-Adha is worldly (expansion through meat), so it resembles rights of servants (huquq al-‘ibad), requiring complete testimony. Nawadir argues: the benefit is religious (Hajj time), so it resembles rights of Allah (huquq Allah), requiring only one witness. Identify which benefit the text weighs more heavily.
The Hanafi school considers the dharurah (necessity) of verifying dates carefully; worldly benefits require stronger proof.
5
Determine the tarjih (preference)
The author of Al-Hidayah rules that the Zahir al-Riwayah position is 'al-asahh' and the mufta bihi (operative for fatwa). The worldly benefit of meat distribution is deemed more apparent, so complete testimony is required. This is the standard Hanafi practice.
Remember: the disagreement is legitimate ikhtilaf within the school, but the mufti must follow the preferred view.

Source Text

مطلع ابر آلود ہو نیکی صورت میں دو مرد یا ایک مرد اور دو عورتوں کی گواہی معتبر ہوگی
وَإِذَا كَانَ بِالسَّمَاءِ عِلَّةٌ لَمْ تُقْبَلُ فِي هِلَالِ الْفِطْرِ إِلَّا شَهَادَةُ رَجُلَيْنِ أَوْ رَجُلٍ وَامْرَأَتَيْنِ لِأَنَّهُ تَعَلَّقَ بِهِ نَفْعُ الْعَبْدِ وَهُوَ الْفِطَرُ فَاشْبَهَ سَائِرَ حُقُوقِهِ وَالْأضْحَى كَالْفِطْرِ فِى هَذَا فِى ظَاهِرِ الرّوَايَةِ وَهُوَ الْاصَحُ خِلَافًا لِمَا رُوِيَ عَنْ بِي حَنِيفَةَ أَنَّهُ كَهَلَالِ رَمَضَانَ لِأَنَّهُ تَعَلَّقَ بِهِ نَفْعُ الْعِبَادِ وَهُوَ التَّوَسُّعُ بِلُحُومِ الْأَصَاحِي ترجمہ اور جب آسمان میں علت ہو تو عید الفطر کے چاند میں قبول نہ ہوگی مگر دو مردوں یا ایک مرد اور دو عورتوں کی گواہی کیونکہ اس کے ساتھ بندے کا نفع متعلق ہے اور وہ فطر ہے اسلئے تمام حقوق بندہ کے مشابہ ہو گیا اور عید الاضحی کے چاند دیکھنے کا حکم ظاہر الروایہ کے مطابق عید الفطر کے مانند ہے اور یہی صحیح ہے برخلاف اس کے جوابوحنیفہ سے روایت کیا گیا ہے کہ عید الاضحی کا چاند رمضان کے چاند کے مانند ہے کیونکہ اس کے ساتھ بھی بندوں کا نفع متعلق ہوتا ہے اور وہ نفع قربانیوں کے گوشت سے توسیع کا حصول ہے۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ۲۹ رمضان کو اگر آسمان پر ابر یا غبار وغیرہ ہو تو عید الفطر کے چاند کے ثبوت میں دو مردوں یا ایک مرد اور دو عورتوں کی شہادت ضروری ہے ایک آدمی کی شہادت کافی نہ ہوگی اور گواہوں کا آزاد ہونا اور محدود فی القذف نہ ہونا بھی ضروری ہے محدود فى القذف اگر تو بہ کر چکا ہو تب بھی عید الفطر کے چاند دیکھنے میں اس کی شہادت معتبر نہ ہو گی اسی طرح اس گواہی کا لفظ شہادت کے ساتھ ہونا ضروری ہے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ عید الفطر کے چاند کے ساتھ بندوں کا نفع متعلق ہے اور وہ نفع فطر ہے یعنی رمضان میں کھانے پینے کی جو پابندیاں تھیں عید کے چاند سے وہ سب ختم ہو گئیں اور ظاہر ہے کہ اس میں بندوں کا نفع ہے اور جب اس میں بندوں کا نفع ہے تو یہ محض دینی امر نہ رہا بلکہ حقوق العباد کے مشابہ ہو گیا اور حقوق العباد کو ثابت کرنے کے لئے شہادت کا ملہ ضروری ہوتی ہے یعنی دو مرد یا ایک مرد اور دو عورتیں گواہی دیں بشرطیکہ وہ آزاد ہوں مسلمان ہوں اور عادل ہوں ، محدود فی القذف نہ ہوں اور لفظ شہادت کے ساتھ گواہی دی ہو پس جب عید الفطر کے چاند کا معاملہ بھی حقوق العباد کے قبیل سے ہے تو اس کو ثابت کرنے کے لئے بھی شہادت کا ملہ ضروری ہے ایک آدمی کی گواہی کافی نہ ہوگی ۔
صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ عیدالاضحی کے چاند کا حکم بھی عید الفطر کے چاند کے مانند ہے یعنی عید الاضحی کے چاند کا ثبوت بھی ایک آدمی کی گواہی سے نہ ہوگا بلکہ دو مرد یا ایک مرد اور دو عورتوں کا ہونا ضروری ہے بشرطیکہ مذکورہ تمام شرطیں موجود ہوں یہ حکم ظاہر الرویہ کے مطابق ہے اور یہ صیح قول ہے البتہ نوادر میں امام ابوحنیفہ سے اس کے خلاف روایت ہے نوارد کی روایت کے مطابق عید الاضحی کا چاند، رمضان کے چاند کے مانند ہے۔ یعنی رمضان کے چاند کی طرح ایک آدمی کی گواہی سے ثابت ہو جائے گا بشر طیکہ آسمان غبار آلود یعنی مطلع صاف نہ ہو۔
نوادر کی روایت کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ عید الاضحی کے چاند کے ساتھ ایک امر دینی متعلق ہوتا ہے یعنی حج کے وقت کا ظہور، اور امور دینیہ ثابت کرنے کے لئے ایک عادل آدمی کی گواہی کافی ہے لہذا رمضان کی طرح عیدالانی کے چاند کے ثبوت میں ایک عادل آدمی کی گواہی کافی ہوگی ۔ اور ظاہر الروایہ کی دلیل یہ ہےکہ عید الاضحی کے چاند سے بندوں کا نفع متعلق ہے یعنی عید الاضحی کے ایام میں بندے اپنے خدا کے مہمان ہوتے ہیں اور قربانی کے گوشت کی بڑی ریل پیل رہتی ہے اور ظاہر ہے کہ گوشت کے اندر توسع کا حصول بندوں کا نفع ہے پس یہ بھی حقوق العباد کے مشابہ ہو گیا اور حقوق العباد کو ثابت کرنے کے لئے ایک آدمی کی گواہی نا کافی ہوتی ہے اس لئے عید الاضحی کے چاند کو ثابت کرنے کے لئے بھی ایک آدمی کی گواہی کافی نہ ہوگی بلکہ عید الفطر کے چاند کی طرح عیدالانی کے چاند کے لئے بھی شہادت کاملہ کا ہونا ضروری ہے۔
When the sky is cloudy, the testimony of two men or one man and two women will be considered valid. And when there is an obstruction in the sky, for the moon of Fitr, only the testimony of two men or one man and two women is accepted, because the benefit of the servant is attached to it, which is breaking the fast, so it becomes similar to his other rights. And Adha is like Fitr in this in Zahir al-Riwayah, and this is the most correct, contrary to what was narrated from [Abu] Hanifa that it is like the moon of Ramadan, because the benefit of the servants is attached to it, which is obtaining expansion through the meat of sacrifices. Translation: And when there is an obstruction in the sky, for the moon of Eid al-Fitr, only the testimony of two men or one man and two women will be accepted, because the benefit of the servant is attached to it, and that is breaking the fast, so it resembles all his rights. And the moon of Eid al-Adha is like Fitr in this in Zahir al-Riwayah, and this is the correct opinion, contrary to what was narrated from [Abu] Hanifa that it is like the moon of Ramadan, because the benefit of the servants is attached to it, and that benefit is obtaining expansion through the meat of sacrifices. Explanation: The matter is that on the 29th of Ramadan, if there is cloud or dust etc. in the sky, then for establishing the moon of Eid al-Fitr, the testimony of two men or one man and two women is necessary. The testimony of one person will not suffice. And it is also necessary that the witnesses be free and not be hadd-punished for qadhf. Even if a person hadd-punished for qadhf has repented, his testimony for seeing the moon of Eid al-Fitr is not valid. Similarly, the testimony must be given with the word 'shahada'. The evidence is that the benefit of the servants is attached to the moon of Eid al-Fitr, and that benefit is breaking the fast, i.e., the restrictions on eating and drinking in Ramadan are all lifted with the moon of Eid. It is obvious that there is benefit for the servants in this. And when there is benefit for the servants, it is no longer purely a religious matter but resembles rights of the servants. And for establishing rights of the servants, complete testimony is required, i.e., two men or one man and two women give testimony, provided they are free, Muslims, just, not hadd-punished for qadhf, and have testified with the word 'shahada'. So, since the matter of the moon of Eid al-Fitr is of the category of rights of the servants, complete testimony is required to establish it; one person's testimony is not enough. The author of Hidayah says that the ruling for the moon of Eid al-Adha is also like that of Eid al-Fitr. That is, the moon of Eid al-Adha will not be established by one person's testimony; rather, two men or one man and two women are necessary, provided all the aforementioned conditions exist. This ruling is according to Zahir al-Riwayah, and this is the correct view. However, in Nawadir, there is a narration from Imam Abu Hanifa contrary to this. According to the Nawadir narration, the moon of Eid al-Adha is like the moon of Ramadan, i.e., it will be established by one person's testimony, provided the sky is dusty, i.e., not clear. The evidence of the Nawadir narration is that a religious matter is attached to the moon of Eid al-Adha, i.e., the appearance of the time of Hajj. And for establishing religious matters, the testimony of one just person is sufficient. Hence, like Ramadan, one just person's testimony is enough to establish the moon of Eid al-Adha. And the evidence of Zahir al-Riwayah is that the benefit of the servants is attached to the moon of Eid al-Adha, i.e., during the days of Eid al-Adha, the servants are guests of their God, and there is a great abundance of sacrifice meat. It is obvious that obtaining expansion through meat is a benefit for the servants. So this also resembles rights of the servants. And for establishing rights of the servants, one person's testimony is insufficient. Therefore, for establishing the moon of Eid al-Adha, one person's testimony is not enough; rather, like the moon of Eid al-Fitr, complete testimony is necessary.
Source pages p. 203

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute within the Hanafi school regarding moon sighting for Eid al-Adha when the sky is cloudy. The main ruling for Eid al-Fitr: when sky is cloudy, two men or one man and two women are required because breaking the fast is considered a right of the servant (haqq al-‘abd), similar to financial claims. The same ruling applies to Eid al-Adha in Zahir al-Riwayah (the relied-upon position) because the benefit of sacrificial meat is seen as worldly. However, in Nawadir (rare transmissions), Abu Hanifa is reported to equate Eid al-Adha with Ramadan, where one witness suffices, because the moon marks a religious occasion (Hajj time). The commentary explains the reasoning: the benefit in Eid al-Fitr is worldly (breaking the fast), so rigorous testimony is needed; in Ramadan, the benefit is religious (obligating the fast), so leniency applies. For Eid al-Adha, Zahir al-Riwayah weighs the worldly benefit (meat distribution), while Nawadir emphasizes the religious aspect (Hajj). The text declares the Zahir al-Riwayah position as the correct one (al-asahh).

Key Terms
شہادت کاملہ (shahadat kamilah): Complete testimony consisting of two men or one man and two women, fulfilling conditions of freedom, justice, etc.
محدود فی القذف (mahrur fi al-qadhf): A person who has received the hadd punishment for false accusation of adultery (qadhf).
ظاہر الروایہ (Zahir al-Riwayah): The six core books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani that form the canonical basis of Hanafi fiqh.
نوادر (Nawadir): Rare or singular transmissions from the early Hanafi imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) that are not part of Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Zahir al-Riwayah, how many witnesses are needed for the moon of Eid al-Adha when the sky is cloudy?
A) One just man
B) Two men or one man and two women
C) One man and two women only
D) Only two men

Key Takeaway
For moon sighting when cloudy, Eid al-Adha requires complete testimony (two men or one man and two women) because the worldly benefit of meat distribution outweighs the religious aspect, following the Zahir al-Riwayah position.

Time of Fasting: From Dawn to Sunset
Ruling on the time of fasting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the exact time of fasting in the Hanafi school and identify the Quranic proof that defines it.

Core Idea
Fasting begins at true dawn (fajr sadiq) and ends at sunset.

The time of fasting is a fundamental condition for observing the fast correctly. This lesson establishes the precise boundary: it begins at the second dawn (al-fajr al-thani) and ends at sunset. The proof is direct from the Quran, and the Hanafi school emphasizes the distinction between the true and false dawn to avoid error.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Recognize that this passage states the time of fasting as a legal condition (shart) for the validity of the fast.
The time condition is external to the act itself but necessary for correct observance.
2
Note the start and end points
The start is 'the rising of the second dawn' (al-fajr al-thani), not the false dawn. The end is 'the setting of the sun' (ghurub al-shams).
The second dawn is the horizontal light spread; the first dawn is vertical and not used for fasting.
3
Distinguish between the two dawns
Understand that the false dawn (fajr awwal) appears as a vertical pillar of light but disappears; the true dawn (fajr thani) spreads horizontally across the horizon and persists.
This distinction is crucial: beginning the fast at the false dawn would mean eating/drinking after the real start, invalidating the fast.
4
Connect to the Quranic proof
The verse (Surah al-Baqarah 2:187) uses 'white thread from black thread' as a metaphor for dawn and night, clearly marking the boundaries.
The Hanafi school considers this proof qat'i (definitive) in both transmission and meaning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَوَقْتُ الصَّوْمِ مِن حِيْنَ طُلُوعِ الْفَجْرِ الثَّانِي إِلَى غُرُوبِ الشَّمْسِ لِقَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى كُلُوا وَاشْرَبُوا حَتَّى يَتَبَيَّنَ لَكُمُ الْخَيْطُ الْأَبْيَضُ مِنَ الْخَيْطِ الْأَسْوَدِ مِنَ الْفَجْرِ ثُمَّ أَتِمُّوا الصِّيَامَ إِلَى اللَّيْلِ
And the time of fasting is from the rising of the second dawn until the setting of the sun, due to His saying, the Exalted: 'Eat and drink until the white thread becomes distinct to you from the black thread of dawn; then complete the fast until night.'
Source pages p. 203

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement establishing the time for fasting. The beginning is at true dawn (al-fajr al-thani), which is the horizontal light spread across the horizon, not the false dawn (al-fajr al-awwal) which rises vertically. The end is at sunset. The proof is from the Quran (Surah al-Baqarah 2:187), which uses the analogy of white and black threads to distinguish between day and night. The Hanafi school insists on the second dawn (fajr sadiq) because the first dawn is not a reliable marker for commencing the fast. The time of fasting is thus clearly defined, and any food or drink after true dawn invalidates the fast.

Key Terms
الفجر الثاني (al-fajr al-thani): The true dawn; the horizontal spread of light along the horizon after the false dawn.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what marks the beginning of the fasting time?
A) The first dawn (fajr awwal)
B) The second dawn (fajr thani)
C) Sunrise
D) Midday

Key Takeaway
The time of fasting is precisely defined as from true dawn to sunset, based on a clear Quranic verse, and the Hanafi school emphasizes the distinction between true and false dawn.

Testimony for the Crescent of Eid al-Adha: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on testimony for Eid al-Adha crescent

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on the testimony required for the Eid al-Adha crescent, explain the reasoning behind each, and identify which is the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Eid al-Adha's crescent requires complete testimony like Eid al-Fitr, not one witness like Ramadan.

The crescent of Eid al-Adha marks the beginning of the days of sacrifice. But what kind of testimony establishes it? This lesson explores a unique intra-Hanafi dispute: while the relied-upon position (Zahir al-Riwayah) demands complete testimony (two men or one man and two women), a rare narration from Imam Abu Hanifah himself accepts a single upright witness. The dispute hinges on whether the crescent is closer to a religious matter (like Ramadan) or a matter of people's rights (like Eid al-Fitr).

Guided Path
1
State the two positions
What does Zahir al-Riwayah require? What does the Nawadir narration require? Be precise about the number and conditions of witnesses.
Both positions agree that if the sky is clear, a large group giving certainty is needed, but under cloudiness they differ.
2
Identify the common foundation
Both sides agree on the base rulings: Ramadan crescent requires one upright witness (when cloudy); Eid al-Fitr requires complete testimony. The dispute is which analogy applies to Eid al-Adha.
This shows the dispute is not about the basic rules but about categorizing Eid al-Adha.
3
Trace the reasoning behind each position
For Zahir al-Riwayah: Eid al-Adha brings worldly benefit (abundance of meat) → resembles rights of people → complete testimony. For Nawadir: Eid al-Adha is linked to Hajj (religious matter) → like Ramadan → one witness suffices.
Each side highlights a different aspect of the crescent: worldly benefit vs. religious significance.
4
Evaluate the tarjih (preference)
The text declares Zahir al-Riwayah as 'the correct statement' (asahh). Why? Because the benefit aspect is predominant over the religious connection. Also, Zahir al-Riwayah is the stronger transmission.
The mufta bihi position is complete testimony.
5
Note the additional rule for clear sky
When the sky is clear (no obstruction), the threshold is higher: only a large group whose report yields certainty is accepted, regardless of the dispute.
This rule applies to all crescents and is not part of the internal dispute.

Source Text

کتاب الصوم
۲۰۲
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد سوم
کے ساتھ ہونا ضروری ہے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ عید الفطر کے چاند کے ساتھ بندوں کا نفع متعلق ہے اور وہ نفع فطر ہے یعنی رمضان میں کھانے پینے کی جو پابندیاں تھیں عید کے چاند سے وہ سب ختم ہو گئیں اور ظاہر ہے کہ اس میں بندوں کا نفع ہے اور جب اس میں بندوں کا نفع ہے تو یہ محض دینی امر نہ رہا بلکہ حقوق العباد کے مشابہ ہو گیا اور حقوق العباد کو ثابت کرنے کے لئے شہادت کاملہ ضروری ہوتی ہے یعنی دو مرد یا ایک مرد اور دو عورتیں گواہی دیں بشرطیکہ وہ آزاد ہوں مسلمان ہوں اور عادل ہوں ، محدود فی القذف نہ ہوں اور لفظ شہادت کے ساتھ گواہی دی ہو پس جب عید الفطر کے چاند کا معاملہ بھی حقوق العباد کے قبیل سے ہے تو اس کو ثابت کرنے کے لئے بھی شہادت کاملہ ضروری ہے ایک آدمی کی گواہی کافی نہ ہوگی ۔
صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ عیدالاضحی کے چاند کا حکم بھی عید الفطر کے چاند کے مانند ہے یعنی عید الاضحی کے چاند کا ثبوت بھی ایک آدمی کی گواہی سے نہ ہوگا بلکہ دو مرد یا ایک مرد اور دو عورتوں کا ہونا ضروری ہے بشرطیکہ مذکورہ تمام شرطیں موجود ہوں یہ حکم ظاہر الرویہ کے مطابق ہے اور یہ صحیح قول ہے البتہ نوادر میں امام ابوحنیفہ سے اس کے خلاف روایت ہے نوادر کی روایت کے مطابق عید الاضحی کا چاند، رمضان کے چاند کے مانند ہے۔ یعنی رمضان کے چاند کی طرح ایک آدمی کی گواہی سے ثابت ہو جائے گا بشرطیکہ آسمان غبار آلود یعنی مطلع صاف نہ ہو۔
نوادر کی روایت کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ عید الاضحی کے چاند کے ساتھ ایک امر دینی متعلق ہوتا ہے یعنی حج کے وقت کا ظہور، اور امور دینیہ ثابت کرنے کے لئے ایک عادل آدمی کی گواہی کافی ہے لہذا رمضان کی طرح عیدالاضحی کے چاند کے ثبوت میں ایک عادل آدمی کی گواہی کافی ہوگی ۔ اور ظاہر الروایہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ عید الاضحی کے چاند سے بندوں کا نفع متعلق ہے یعنی عید الاضحی کے ایام میں بندے اپنے خدا کے مہمان ہوتے ہیں اور قربانی کے گوشت کی بڑی ریل پیل رہتی ہے اور ظاہر ہے کہ گوشت کے اندر توسع کا حصول بندوں کا نفع ہے پس یہ بھی حقوق العباد کے مشابہ ہو گیا اور حقوق العباد کو ثابت کرنے کے لئے ایک آدمی کی گواہی ناکافی ہوتی ہے اس لئے عید الاضحی کے چاند کو ثابت کرنے کے لئے بھی ایک آدمی کی گواہی کافی نہ ہوگی بلکہ عید الفطر کے چاند کی طرح عیدالاضحی کے چاند کے لئے بھی شہادت کاملہ کا ہونا ضروری ہے۔
مطلع صاف ہو تو ایک کثیر جماعت کی گواہی معتبر ہوگی
وَإِنْ لَمْ يَكُن بِالسَّمَاءِ عِلَّةً لَمْ تُقْبَلُ إِلَّا شَهَادَةُ جَمَاعَةٍ يَقَعُ الْعِلْمُ بِخَبَرِهِمْ كَمَا ذَكَرْنَا ترجمہ . اگر آسمان پر علت نہ ہو تو امام قبول نہ کرے مگر ایسی جماعت کی شہادت جسکی خبر سے یقین حاصل ہو جائے جیسا کہ ہم نے ذکر کیا ہے۔
Book of Fasting. 202. Ashraf al-Hidayah Sharh Urdu Hidayah Volume Three. It is necessary to be with. The proof is that with the crescent of Eid al-Fitr is connected the benefit of the servants, and that benefit is fitr, i.e., the restrictions of eating and drinking in Ramadan are all removed by the crescent of Eid, and it is apparent that in this is the benefit of the servants. And when in this is the benefit of the servants, then it is no longer a purely religious matter but becomes similar to the rights of the servants. And for establishing the rights of the servants, complete testimony is necessary, i.e., two men or one man and two women testify, provided they are free, Muslim, and upright, not hadd-ul-qadhf, and they testify with the word shahadah. So when the matter of the crescent of Eid al-Fitr is also of the category of rights of the servants, then to establish it also complete testimony is necessary; one person's testimony will not suffice. The author of Hidayah says that the ruling of the crescent of Eid al-Adha is like that of the crescent of Eid al-Fitr, i.e., the proof of the crescent of Eid al-Adha will also not be established by one person's testimony, rather two men or one man and two women are necessary, provided all the mentioned conditions exist. This ruling is according to Zahir al-Riwayah, and this is the correct statement. However, in Nawadir, there is a narration from Imam Abu Hanifah contrary to this. According to the Nawadir narration, the crescent of Eid al-Adha is like the crescent of Ramadan, i.e., like the Ramadan crescent, it will be established by one person's testimony, provided the sky is dusty, i.e., the horizon is not clear. The proof of the Nawadir narration is that with the crescent of Eid al-Adha is connected a religious matter, i.e., the appearance of the time of Hajj, and for establishing religious matters, the testimony of one upright person suffices. Therefore, like Ramadan, for establishing the crescent of Eid al-Adha, the testimony of one upright person suffices. And the proof of Zahir al-Riwayah is that with the crescent of Eid al-Adha is connected the benefit of the servants, i.e., in the days of Eid al-Adha, the servants are guests of their Lord, and there is great abundance of sacrificial meat, and it is apparent that obtaining abundance in meat is the benefit of the servants. So this also becomes similar to the rights of the servants, and for establishing the rights of the servants, one person's testimony is insufficient. Therefore, for establishing the crescent of Eid al-Adha, one person's testimony will not suffice; rather, like the crescent of Eid al-Fitr, for the crescent of Eid al-Adha, complete testimony is necessary. If the horizon is clear, then the testimony of a large group that gives certainty is accepted. And if there is no obstruction in the sky, testimony is not accepted except from a group whose report gives certainty, as we have mentioned.
Source pages p. 203

Commentary
This passage discusses the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the testimony required for establishing the crescent of Eid al-Adha. The text begins by explaining the ruling for Eid al-Fitr: because the crescent brings benefit to people (removal of fasting restrictions), it resembles rights of people (huquq al-‘ibad), which require complete testimony (two men or one man and two women). For Eid al-Adha, the author of Al-Hidayah states the ruling is the same according to Zahir al-Riwayah (the relied-upon position). The reasoning is that Eid al-Adha also involves benefit (abundance of meat), so it also resembles rights of people, thus requiring complete testimony. However, there is a narration in Nawadir (rare transmissions) from Imam Abu Hanifa that considers Eid al-Adha like Ramadan: since it is linked to a religious matter (Hajj timing), one upright witness suffices, provided the sky is not clear (i.e., cloudy). The text then adds a further rule: if the sky is clear, testimony is accepted only from a group whose report gives certainty, not just one or two witnesses. This passage is an expansion probe by the commentator, detailing the proofs for both positions.

Key Terms
شهادة كاملة (shahadah kamilah): Complete testimony: two men or one man and two women, meeting conditions of freedom, Islam, and uprightness, using the word 'shahadah'.
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwayah): The well-known transmitted corpus from Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani's six books, considered the most authoritative source of Hanafi rulings.
نوادر (nawadir): Rare or less widely transmitted narrations within the Hanafi school, carrying less weight than Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Zahir al-Riwayah, what testimony is required to establish the crescent of Eid al-Adha when the sky is cloudy?
A) One upright male witness
B) Two men or one man and two women with conditions
C) A large group giving certainty
D) Two women only

Key Takeaway
Eid al-Adha's crescent requires complete testimony (two men or one man and two women) according to the relied-upon Hanafi position, because its worldly benefit overrides the religious link to Hajj.

Sawm — Fasting
beginner

Time of Fasting: From Dawn to Sunset
Ruling with Qur'anic proof for the time of fasting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the precise time boundaries for fasting according to the Hanafi school and identify the Qur'anic proof that establishes them.

Core Idea
Fasting begins at true dawn and ends at sunset — determined by the Qur'anic metaphor of the white and black threads.

One of the first things a fasting person must know is when to start and stop. This passage, drawn from a Hanafi text, lays down the exact timing using a clear Qur'anic verse. Understanding this foundation is essential for the validity of your fast.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its time boundaries
The passage states that the time of fasting is from the rising of the second dawn (true dawn) to the setting of the sun. Note the precision: not the first dawn, but the second.
The second dawn is also called the true dawn (fajr sadiq).
2
Locate the Qur'anic proof
The author cites Surah al-Baqarah 2:187: 'Eat and drink until the white thread becomes distinct to you from the black thread... Then complete the fast until the night.' Identify the operative words: 'until the white thread becomes distinct' and 'until the night'.
The verse itself uses metaphorical language.
3
Understand the metaphorical language
The commentator explains that the 'white thread' is the light of dawn and the 'black thread' is the darkness of night. This imagery helps visualize the transition from night to day and back.
This is a common tafsir understood across madhhabs.
4
Apply the ruling to practice
Fasting commences at true dawn, so one must stop eating before that moment. It ends at sunset, so one may break the fast immediately after the sun has set. Use reliable prayer timetables or direct observation.
The ruling is agreed upon and forms the basis for all fasting timings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
روزہ کا وقت ابتداء وانتہاء
وَوَقْتُ الصَّوْمِ مِنْ حِينَ طُلُوعِ الْفَجْرِ الثَّانِي إِلَى غُرُوبِ الشَّمْسِ لِقَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى كُلُوا وَاشْرَبُوا حَتَّى يَتَبَيَّنَ لَكُمُ الْخَيْطُ الْأَبْيَضُ مِنَ الْخَيْطِ الْأَسْوَدِ إِلَى أَنْ قَالَ ثُمَّ أَتِمُوا الْقِيَامَ إِلَى اللَّيْلِ وَالْخَيْطَانِ بَيَاضُ النَّهَارِ وَسَوَادُ اللَّيْلِ ترجمہ اور روزہ کا وقت فجر ثانی کے طلوع ہونے کے وقت سے آفتاب غروب ہونے تک ہے کیونکہ باری تعالیٰ نے فرمایا ہے کہ کھاؤ، پیو یہاں تک کہ ظاہر ہو جائے تمہارے واسطے فجر کے سیاہ ڈورے سے سفید ڈورا، یہاں تک کہ اللہ تعالیٰ نے فرمایا پھر تم تمام کرو روزے کو رات تک اور دونوں ڈورے دن کی سفیدی اور رات کی سیاہی ہیں۔ تشریح اس عبارت میں روزے کا اول اور آخر بیان کیا ہے چنانچہ فرمایا کہ روزے کا وقت صبح صادق طلوع ہونے کے وقت سے لے کر آفتاب غروب ہونے تک ہے۔ دلیل باری تعالیٰ کا یہ قول ہے حَتَّى يَتَبَيَّنَ لَكُمُ الْخَيْطُ الْأَبْيَضُ مِنَ الْخَيْطِ الْأَسْوَدِ اور اس کے بعد فرمایا ثُمَّ أَتِمُّوا الْقِيَامَ إِلَى اللَّيْلِ (البقرہ ۱۸۷) آیت میں خیط ابیض سے مراد صبح کی روشنی ہے اور خیط اسود سے مراد رات کی تاریکی ہے پس اس آیت میں رات کی تاریکی کو سیاہ خط اور صبح کی روشنی کو سفید خط کی مثال سے جتلا کر روزہ شروع ہونے اور کھانا پینا حرام ہو جانے کا صحیح وقت متعین فرمایا ہے۔
The time of fasting: beginning and end. And the time of fasting is from the rising of the second dawn to the setting of the sun, because of His saying, the Most High: 'Eat and drink until the white thread becomes distinct to you from the black thread' until He said 'Then complete the fast until the night.' And the two threads are the whiteness of the day and the blackness of the night. Translation: And the time of fasting is from the time of the rising of the true dawn to the setting of the sun, because Allah the Exalted has said: 'Eat and drink until the white thread becomes distinct to you from the black thread' until Allah said 'Then complete the fast to the night.' And the two threads are the whiteness of the day and the blackness of the night. Explanation: In this passage, the beginning and end of the fast are stated. Thus it says that the time of fasting is from the rising of the true dawn to the setting of the sun. The proof is the saying of Allah the Exalted: 'until the white thread becomes distinct to you from the black thread' and after that He said 'Then complete the fast to the night.' In the verse, 'white thread' refers to the light of dawn, and 'black thread' refers to the darkness of night. So in this verse, by likening the darkness of night to a black line and the light of dawn to a white line, the correct time for the start of fasting and the prohibition of eating and drinking is determined.
Source pages p. 204

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement with proof (istidlal) for the time of fasting. It explicitly defines the beginning (fajr sadiq, the true dawn) and the end (sunset). The proof is directly from the Qur'an, Surah al-Baqarah 2:187. The commentator explains that the 'white thread' is the light of dawn and the 'black thread' is the darkness of night, emphasizing that the metaphorical language establishes the precise legal timing. The ruling is clear: fasting obligates abstention from dawn to sunset.

Key Terms
الفجر الثاني (al-fajr al-thani): The true dawn, which is the second dawn, characterized by light spreading horizontally along the horizon. This is the start time for fasting.
غروب الشمس (ghurub al-shams): The setting of the sun, marking the end of the fasting time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) At the beginning of night (maghrib)
B) At sunset (ghurub al-shams)
C) At the disappearance of twilight
D) At midnight

Key Takeaway
The time of fasting is precisely defined: from the rising of the true dawn to the setting of the sun, based on the Qur'anic verse.

Sawm — Fasting
intermediate

Legal Definition of Fasting (Sawm)
Definition of sawm with linguistic and legal components

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi legal definition of fasting and identify its essential components: linguistic meaning, added intention, daytime specification, and condition for women.

Core Idea
Fasting is not just abstaining; intention transforms abstention into worship.

This lesson unpacks the legal definition of fasting (sawm) as presented in the Hanafi tradition. The definition is not merely linguistic; it incorporates intention and temporal restrictions that elevate abstention from a habit to an act of worship. Understanding this layered definition is essential for correctly applying the rulings of fasting, especially regarding validity and conditions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the linguistic core
Recognize that the word 'sawm' in Arabic means abstention (imsaak) from anything, as seen in pre-Islamic usage. This is the raw material of the definition.
Linguistic meaning is general; legal meaning adds restrictions.
2
Add the legal element: intention
Note that Islamic law adds intention (niyyah) to abstention. This distinguishes worship from mere habit. Without intention, abstention is not considered fasting in the legal sense.
Intention is a condition (shart) for validity.
3
Restrict to daytime
Understand why fasting is limited to daytime (dawn to sunset) using the Qur'anic verse (2:187) and rational reasoning: continuous day-and-night fasting is impossible, so daytime is specified to make it distinct from ordinary habit.
The verse instructs eating/drinking until dawn and completing fast until night.
4
Identify the condition for women
Recognize that purity from menstruation and postnatal bleeding is a condition (shart) for the validity of a woman's fast. If fasting during these states, it is invalid and must be made up later.
This is a unique condition for female fasting.
5
Synthesize the full definition
Combine all elements: 'Fasting is abstention from eating, drinking, and sexual intercourse during the daytime with intention, and for women, freedom from menses/postnatal bleeding.' This is the complete Hanafi definition.
Each component is necessary for validity.

وَالصَّوْمُ هُوَ الْإِمْسَاكُ عَنِ الْأَكْلِ وَالشُّرْبِ وَالْجِمَاعِ نَهَارًا مَعَ النِّيَةِ فِي الشَّرْعِ لِأَنَّ الصَّوْمَ فِي حَقِيقَةِ اللُّغَةِ هُوَ الْإِمْسَاكُ لِوُرُودِ الِاسْتِعْمَالِ فِيهِ إِلَّا أَنَّهُ زِيدَ عَلَيْهِ النِّيَةُ فِي الشَّرْعِ لِيَتَمَيَّزَ بِهَا الْعِبَادَةُ مِنَ الْعَادَةِ وَاخْتَصَّ بِالنَّهَارِ لِمَا تَلَوْنَا وَلِأَنَّهُ لَمَّا تَعَذَّرَ الْوِصَالُ كَانَ تَعَيُّنُ النَّهَارِ أَوْلَى لِيَكُونَ عَلَى خِلَافِ الْعَادَةِ وَعَلَيْهِ مَبْنَى الْعِبَادَةِ وَالطَّهَارَةُ عَنِ الْحَيْضِ وَالنِّفَاسِ شَرْطٌ لِتَحَقُّقِ الْأَدَاءِ فِي حَقِّ النِّسَاءِ ترجمہ اور روزہ شریعت کے اندر نیت کے ساتھ دن بھر کھانے پینے اور جماع سے رکنے کا نام ہے کیونکہ لفظ صوم حقیقت لغویٰ میں امساک کا نام ہے کیونکہ لفظ صوم اس معنی میں مستعمل ہوا ہے مگر یہ کہ شریعت میں اس پر نیت کا اضافہ کر دیا گیا تا کہ نیت کی وجہ سے عبادت کا عادت سے امتیاز ہو جائے۔ اور شرعی روزہ کا اختصاص دن کے ساتھ اس آیت کی وجہ سے ہوا جو ہم نے تلاوت کی ہے اور اس لئے کہ جب وصال متعذر ہو تو دن ہی کا متعین کرنا اولیٰ ہوگا تا کہ عادت کے خلاف ہو جائے۔ اور عبادت کی بنیاد اسی پر ہے اور حیض و نفاس سے پاک ہونا شرط ہے عورتوں کے حق میں ادا متحقق ہونے کے لئے۔ تشریح یہاں روزہ کی تعریف کی گئی ہے چنانچہ فرمایا کہ شریعت میں روزہ نیت کے ساتھ کھانے پینے اور جماع سے رکنے کا نام ہے کیونکہ لغت میں صوم کا لفظ مطلقاً امساک کے معنی میں ہے اس لئے کہ اسلام سے پہلے بھی یہ لفظ امساک کے معنی میں استعمال ہوتا تھا البتہ شریعت میں اس پر نیت کا اضافہ کر دیا گیا تا کہ نیت کی وجہ سے امساک بطور عبادت اور امساک بطور عادت کے درمیان امتیاز ہو جائے اور شرعی صوم دن کے ساتھ مختص ہے باری تعالیٰ کے قول كُلُوا وَاشْرَبُوا حَتَّى يَتَبَيَّنَ لَكُمُ الْخَيْطُ الْأَبْيَضُ مِنَ الْخَيْطِ الْأَسْوَدِ اور أَتِمُّوا الْقِيَامَ إِلَى اللَّيْلِ کی وجہ سے کیونکہ اس آیت میں صوم کے طلوع فجر سے رات تک ہونے کو بیان کیا گیا ہے۔ اور عقلی دلیل یہ ہے صوم وصال یعنی رات و دن کا روزہ رکھنا تو متعذر ہے اس لئے کہ مسلسل ایک ماہ رات و دن نہ کھانے پینے سے
The legal definition of fasting. And fasting in law is abstention from eating, drinking, and sexual intercourse during the daytime with intention, because the word 'sawm' in its literal reality is abstention, due to its usage in that meaning. However, intention was added to it in law to distinguish worship from habit. And it is specifically during the daytime because of what we have recited (the verse), and because when continuous fasting (wisal) is not possible, specifying the daytime is more appropriate so that it is contrary to habit, and upon this is based worship. And purity from menstruation and post-natal bleeding is a condition for the validity of performance in the case of women. Translation: And fasting in law is the name for abstaining from eating, drinking, and sexual intercourse during the day with intention, because the word sawm in its literal meaning is abstention, because the word sawm has been used in this meaning. However, intention was added to it in law so that by intention worship is distinguished from habit. And legal fasting is specifically associated with the day because of the verse we have recited, and because when continuous fasting (wisal) is impossible, specifying the day is more appropriate so that it is contrary to habit, and upon this is based worship. And purity from menstruation and post-natal bleeding is a condition for the validity of performance in the case of women. Explanation: Here the definition of fasting is given. Thus it says that in law, fasting is the name for abstaining from eating, drinking, and sexual intercourse with intention, because in language the word sawm means absolute abstention, because before Islam this word was used in the meaning of abstention. However, in law, intention was added to it so that by intention abstention as worship and abstention as habit are distinguished. And legal fasting is specific to the day because of the saying of Allah the Exalted: 'Eat and drink until the white thread becomes distinct to you from the black thread' and 'Complete the fast to the night', because in this verse it is stated that fasting is from dawn to night. And the rational proof is that continuous fasting (day and night) is impossible because continuous not eating and drinking for a month...
Source pages p. 204

Commentary
This passage provides the legal definition (ta'rif) of fasting (sawm) in the Hanafi school. It breaks down the components: linguistic meaning (imsaak: abstention), the added condition of intention (niyyah) to distinguish worship from mere habit, the specification of daytime (nahar) based on Qur'anic evidence and rational consideration (since continuous day-and-night fasting is impossible, daytime is chosen to make it distinct from ordinary habit), and finally the condition for women that they must be free from menstruation and postnatal bleeding (hayd and nifas) for the fast to be validly performed. The commentary explains each element, emphasizing that intention is what transforms a mere act of abstention into an act of worship. The definition is comprehensive, covering the physical acts (eating, drinking, sex), the time (daytime), the mental component (intention), and a special condition for women (purity from menses).

Key Terms
الإمساك (al-imsaak): Abstention; the linguistic and legal core meaning of sawm.
النية (an-niyyah): Intention; a necessary component added in law to distinguish fasting as an act of worship from mere abstention.
الطهارة عن الحيض والنفاس (at-taharah an al-hayd wan-nafas): Purity from menstruation and postnatal bleeding; a condition (shart) for the validity of a woman's fast.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why was intention added to the definition of fasting in Islamic law?
A) To increase the reward
B) To distinguish worship from habit
C) To make fasting more difficult
D) Because the Quran commanded it

Key Takeaway
Fasting in Hanafi law is abstention from eating, drinking, and sexual intercourse during the daytime with intention, with purity from menses as a condition for women.

Sawm — Fasting
beginner
6 min
The Hanafi Definition of Sawm (Fasting)
Defines sawm as abstention with intention and specifies condition of purity for women

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of sawm and identify its essential elements: abstention, intention, daytime, and the condition of purity for women.

Core Idea
Fasting is not just abstaining; intention and daytime distinguish worship from habit.

This passage lays out the foundational definition of sawm (fasting) in the Hanafi school. It clarifies that while the word sawm means 'abstention' in Arabic, the Shari'ah adds specific conditions to transform a mere physical restraint into an act of worship. Understanding this definition is essential before exploring the detailed rulings of fasting.

Guided Path
1
Identify the linguistic and Shar'i definitions
First, note that in language, sawm simply means 'to abstain' (imsak). The Shari'ah defines it more narrowly: abstention from eating, drinking, and intercourse, coupled with intention, during the daylight hours.
This contrast is key: the Shar'i definition adds the conditions of intention and daytime.
2
Recognize the role of intention (niyyah)
Intention is added to distinguish worship from habit. Without intention, mere abstention is not a valid Islamic fast. In Hanafi fiqh, intention is a condition (shart) for validity.
Intention must be made each night for the next day's fast in Ramadan.
3
Understand why fasting is restricted to daytime
The Quranic verse (2:187) and rational reasoning justify this: continuous fasting (wisal) is impossible because it leads to harm. Therefore, fasting is prescribed for daytime, which runs contrary to natural habit, emphasizing the worship aspect.
The daytime is specified to align with the spirit of worship—opposing one's habits.
4
Note the condition of purity for women
For a woman, purity from menstruation (hayd) and postnatal bleeding (nifas) is a condition for valid performance. If a fast is observed during such states, it is invalid and must be made up (qada) later.
This condition applies to all schools of thought.
5
Distinguish rukn and shurut
The rukn (pillar) of fasting is the abstention itself. The shurut (conditions) include intention, daytime, and, for women, purity. Omission of a rukn invalidates the act; omission of a shart also invalidates it.
In Hanafi fiqh, the absence of any condition makes the fast batil (void).

اضافہ کر دیا گیا تا کہ نیت کی وجہ سے عبادت کا عادت سے امتیاز ہو جائے۔ اور شرعی روزہ کا اختصاص دن کے ساتھ اس آیت کی وجہ سے ہوا جو ہم نے تلاوت کی ہے اور اس لئے کہ جب وصال مستعد رہو ا تو دن ہی کا متعین نفاس سے پاک ہونا شرط ہے پس بحالت حیض و نفاس ادائے صوم تو صحیح نہ ہوگا البتہ نفس وجوب کی وجہ سے پاک ہونے کے بعد قضاء واجب ہوگی۔ واللہ اعلم بالصواب تجمیل احمد عفی عنہ
Definition of sawm in Shari'ah: 'And sawm in the Shari'ah is abstention from eating, drinking, and intercourse during the day with the intention, because the literal meaning of sawm is abstention, due to usage, except that in the Shari'ah the intention is added to it to distinguish worship from habit, and it is specific to the day because of what we recited, and because continuous fasting is impossible, so specifying the day is most appropriate to be contrary to habit, and worship is based on that. And purity from menstruation and post-natal bleeding is a condition for the validity of performance in the case of women.' Translation: And fasting in the Shari'ah is the name for refraining from eating, drinking, and intercourse with intention during the day because the word sawm literally means abstention as it was used in this meaning. However, in the Shari'ah, intention was added to it so that worship is distinguished from habit. And the specificity of the day is due to the verse we recited and because continuous fasting (al-wisal) is difficult, so specifying the day is preferable so that it is contrary to habit, and worship is based on that. And purity from menstruation and post-natal bleeding is a condition for the validity of the performance for women. Explanation: Here the definition of fasting is given. Thus it is said that in the Shari'ah, fasting is the name for refraining from eating, drinking, and intimacy with intention, because in the language the word sawm literally means abstention, as it was used before Islam in the meaning of abstention. However, in the Shari'ah, intention was added so that there is a distinction between abstention as worship and abstention as habit. And the Shari'ah fast is specific to the day due to the saying of Allah Almighty: 'Eat and drink until the white thread becomes distinct from the black thread' and 'then complete the fast until the night', because this verse indicates that fasting is from dawn to night. And the rational proof is that continuous fasting (day and night) is impossible because continuously not eating and drinking for a month would likely lead to death; therefore, it is necessary to specify one of the day or night for fasting. According to reason, specifying the day is better so that refraining from eating and drinking in the day is contrary to habit, and worship is based on opposing habit and desires. And for women, for the valid performance of fasting, their purity from menstruation and post-natal bleeding is a condition. So in the state of menstruation, the performance of fasting is not valid; however, due to the obligation itself, after becoming pure, qada' becomes obligatory. And Allah knows best what is correct. (Signature: Tajmil Ahmad, may he be forgiven.)
Source pages p. 204

Commentary
This passage provides the legal definition of sawm (fasting) in the Hanafi school. It begins with the formal definition: sawm is abstention (imsak) from food, drink, and sexual intercourse during daylight hours, coupled with intention (niyyah). The commentary explains that in the Arabic language, sawm simply means 'to abstain' in general. The Shari'ah added the requirement of intention to differentiate worship from mere habit. The restriction to daytime is based on the Quranic verse (2:187) and rational reasoning: continuous fasting (wisal) is impossible because it would lead to harm; therefore, fasting is prescribed for the daytime, which runs contrary to natural habit, thus emphasizing the worship aspect. The passage also states that for women, purity from menstruation (hayd) and postnatal bleeding (nifas) is a condition for the correct performance (ada') of fasting. If a woman is in menstruation, her fast is not valid, but she must make up the missed days (qada') after purification. This reflects the Hanafi position on the condition of purity for valid fasting.

Key Terms
صوم (sawm): Shari'ah definition: abstention from food, drink, and intercourse with intention during the day.
إمساك (imsak): Literally: abstention. In this context, refraining from nullifiers of fasting.
النية (al-niyyah): Intention to fast, required to distinguish worship from habit.
حيض و نفاس (hayd wa nifas): Menstruation and postnatal bleeding; purity from these is a condition for valid fasting for women.

Key Terms from Source Passage

According to the Hanafi school, what distinguishes the Shari'ah definition of sawm from its linguistic meaning?
A) The addition of intention (niyyah)
B) The abstention from food and drink
C) The specification of the month of Ramadan
D) The requirement of purity

Key Takeaway
Sawm in the Hanafi school is abstention from nullifiers with intention during the daytime, and for women, purity from hayd and nifas is a condition for valid performance.

Sawm — Fasting
intermediate

Ruling on Forgetting While Fasting: Eating, Drinking, or Intercourse
Hanafi ruling: forgetful eating/drinking/intercourse does not break the fast, using istihsan over qiyas.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that forgetful eating, drinking, or intercourse does not break the fast, and evaluate the Maliki counter-argument based on qiyas.

Core Idea
A hadith overrides qiyas: the fast remains valid if you forget—Allah fed you, complete your fast.

This lesson examines a classic dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam Malik regarding the effect of forgetful eating, drinking, or intercourse during fasting. While qiyas (analogical reasoning) suggests the fast should break, the Hanafi school relies on a direct prophetic command and the principle of istihsan (juristic preference) to preserve the fast's validity. Understanding this ruling clarifies how the Hanafi school prioritizes textual evidence over pure analogy.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Determine the ruling according to the Hanafi school: what happens to the fast if a person forgetfully eats, drinks, or has intercourse?
The fast remains valid; it is not broken.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Which school or scholar disagrees, and what do they hold?
Imam Malik holds that the fast is broken based on qiyas.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Trace the qiyas argument: what is the original case (asl), its ruling, and the shared effective cause (illa)?
Asl: speaking forgetfully in prayer (invalidates prayer). Illa: both are acts contrary to the act's purpose.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
How does the Hanafi school rebut the qiyas? What evidence do they bring? Identify the role of istihsan.
They cite the hadith 'Complete your fast, for Allah fed you and gave you drink' and distinguish prayer from fasting due to the absence of a reminder in fasting.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
What is the practical difference between the two positions?
Hanafi: no qada/kaffarah; Maliki: qada required (and possibly kaffarah).

بَابُ مَا يُرْجِبُ الْقَضَاءَ وَالْكَفَّارَةَ ترجمہ یہ باب ان چیزوں کے بیان میں ہے جو قضاء اور کفارہ کو واجب کرتی ہیں تشریح روزے کی انواع اور اقسام سے فراغت پا کر اب ان صورتوں کو بیان کریں گے جن میں روزہ فاسد ہو جاتا ہے اور فساد کی کس صورت میں قضاء اور کفارہ دونوں واجب ہوتے ہیں اور کس صورت میں فقط قضاء واجب ہوتی ہے۔ بھول کر کھانے پینے سے روزہ نہیں ٹوٹتا إذا أكل الصَّائِمُ أَو شَرِبَ أَوْ جَامَعَ لَا يَا لَمْ يُفْطِرُ وَالْقِيَاسُ أنْ يُفْطِرَ وَهُوَ قَولُ مَالِك لِوُجُودِ مَا يُضَادُ الصَّومُ فَصَارَ كَالْكَلَام نَاسِيَّا فِي الصَّلوةِ وَوَجْهُ الْاِسْتِحْسَانِ قَوْلُهُ عَلَيْهِ الصَّلوةَ وَالسَّلَامُ لِلَّذِى أَكَلَ وَ شَرِبَ نَاسِيَّاتِمْ عَلَى صَوْمِكَ فَإِنَّمَا اَطْعَمَكَ اللهُ وَ سَقَاكَ وَإِذَا ثَبَتَ هَذَا فِي حَقِّ الْأَكْلِ وَالشَّرْبِ ثَبَتَ فِى الْوَقَاعِ لِلْإِسْتِوَاءِ الرُّكْنِيَّةِ بِخِلَافِ الصَّلوةِ لِأَنَّ هَيَأةَ الصَّلَاةِ مُذَكِّرَةً فَلَا يَغْلَبُ النِّسَانُ وَلَا مُذَكِّرَ فِي الصَّوْمِ فَيَغْلِبُ وَلَا فَرْقَ بينَ الفَرْضِ وَالنفل لأَنَّ النَّصَّ لَمْ يفصل ترجمہ اور جب روزہ دار نے بھولے سے کھایا یا پیا با جماع کیا تو افطار نہیں ہوا اور قیاس یہ ہے کہ افطار ہو جائے ، اور یہی قول امام مالک کا ہے کیونکہ روزے کی ضد پائی گئی پس یہ نماز میں بھول کر کلام کرنے کے مانند ہو گیا۔ اور وجہ استحسان یہ ہے کہ حضور اقدس صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے اس شخص کے حق میں فرمایا ہے جس نے بھول کر کھایا پیا تھا، تو اپنا روزہ پورا کر اس لئے کہ تجھ کو اللہ نے کھلا یا اور پلایا اور جب یہ حکم کھانے اور پینے میں ثابت ہو گیا تو جماع کے حق میں بھی ثابت ہو گیا کیونکہ رکن ہونے میں سب برابر میں بر خلاف نماز کے، کیونکہ نماز کی حالت خود یا دلانے والی ہے تو نسیان غالب نہ ہوگا اور روزے میں کوئی چیز یاد دلانے والی نہیں ہے پس نسیان غالب ہو جائے گا اور فرض اور نفل کے روزے میں کوئی فرق نہیں ہے کیونکہ نص (حدیث) نے کوئی تفصیل نہیں فرمائی ہے۔ تشریح مسئلہ اگر روزہ دار بھول کر کھالے یا پی لے یا جماع کرلے تو اس کا روزہ نہیں ٹوٹے گا اور قیاس کا تقاضا یہ ہے کہ روزہ ٹوٹ جائے یہی امام مالک کا قول ہے قیاس کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ کھانا، پینا اور جماع کرنا روزے کی ضد ہے اور شئی کی ضدشئی کو معدوم کر دیتی ہے کیونکہ بیک وقت ضدین کا پایا جانا محال ہے پس جب روزے کی ضد یعنی کھا لینا وغیرہ پایا گیا تو روزہ معدوم ہو گیا اور یہ ایسا ہو گیا جیسا کہ نماز میں بھول کر کلام کرنا پس جس طرح جھول کر نماز میں کلام کرنا، نماز کو فاسد کر دیتا ہے اسی طرح بھول کر کھانا پینا روزہ کو فاسد کر دیگا۔ وجہ استحسان یہ حدیث ہے کہ ایک شخص نے بحالت صوم بھول کر کچھ کھا پی لیا تو اس سے حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ تو اپنا روزہ پورا کر، اس لئے کہ اللہ
Chapter on what necessitates qada' and kaffarah. Translation: This chapter is about things that make qada' and kaffarah obligatory. Explanation: After finishing the types and categories of fasting, we will now mention the cases in which the fast becomes invalid, and in which case both qada' and kaffarah are obligatory, and in which case only qada' is obligatory. The fast does not break by forgetting eating/drinking: 'When a fasting person eats or drinks or has intercourse forgetfully, he does not break his fast. By qiyas, he would break it, and that is the view of Malik because he did something contrary to fasting, so it is like speaking forgetfully in prayer. The basis of istihsan is his (peace be upon him) statement to the one who ate and drank forgetfully: "Complete your fast, for Allah fed you and gave you drink." And when this is established regarding eating and drinking, it is also established regarding intercourse because of the equality in being a pillar. Unlike prayer, because the posture of prayer is a reminder, so forgetfulness does not prevail, whereas there is no reminder in fasting, so forgetfulness prevails. And there is no difference between obligatory and supererogatory fasts because the text did not differentiate.' Translation: And when a fasting person eats or drinks or has intercourse forgetfully, then he does not break his fast. According to qiyas, he would break it, and that is the view of Imam Malik because the opposite of fasting is found, so it becomes like speaking forgetfully in prayer. The basis of istihsan is that the Holy Prophet (peace be upon him) said to the person who ate and drank forgetfully: 'Complete your fast, for Allah fed you and gave you drink.' And when this ruling is established regarding eating and drinking, it is also established regarding intercourse because they are equal in being a pillar. This is contrary to prayer, because the state of prayer is itself a reminder, so forgetfulness does not prevail, whereas in fasting there is no reminder, so forgetfulness prevails. And there is no difference between obligatory and supererogatory fasts because the text did not differentiate. Explanation: The ruling is that if a fasting person eats, drinks, or has intercourse forgetfully, his fast does not break. Qiyas requires that the fast breaks, and that is the view of Imam Malik. The reason for qiyas is that eating, drinking, and intercourse are opposites of fasting, and opposites eliminate each other. So when the opposite is found, the fast is eliminated, like speaking forgetfully in prayer invalidates prayer. The basis of istihsan is the hadith that a person ate and drank forgetfully while fasting, and the Prophet (peace be upon him) told him to complete his fast because Allah fed him and gave him drink. Then from this, the ruling extends to intercourse because they are the same in being pillars. Unlike prayer, because the form of prayer is a reminder, so forgetfulness does not overcome, but in fasting there is no reminder, so forgetfulness overcomes. There is no distinction between obligatory and voluntary fasts because the text did not distinguish.
Source pages p. 204

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam Malik regarding fasting. The ruling is that if a fasting person eats, drinks, or has intercourse forgetfully, his fast is not invalidated. This is the Hanafi position. The opposing view (Imam Malik) says that it does invalidate the fast based on qiyas: since these actions oppose fasting, they should break it, similar to speaking forgetfully in prayer which invalidates prayer. The Hanafi response uses istihsan (juristic preference) based on a sahih hadith: the Prophet (peace be upon him) told a man who ate and drank forgetfully to complete his fast, because Allah had fed and watered him. This hadith provides a specific textual exception to the qiyas. The author then extends the same ruling to forgetful intercourse by analogy (qiyas al-musawi) since all three are part of the same rukn (abstention). The author distinguishes prayer from fasting: prayer has a formal structure (hay'ah) that constantly reminds the person of the act, so forgetfulness is rare and the prayer breaks if one speaks forgetfully. In fasting, there is no such constant reminder, so forgetfulness can easily occur. The ruling applies to both fard and nafl fasts, as the hadith does not differentiate. This is the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
القياس (al-qiyas): Analogical reasoning that would invalidate the fast due to opposition.
الاستحسان (al-istihsan): Juristic preference that prefers the hadith over qiyas in this case.
ناسياً (nasiyan): Forgetfully, meaning the person had no intention to break the fast.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary evidence for the Hanafi ruling that forgetful eating does not break the fast?
A) Qiyas upon speaking in prayer
B) The hadith 'Complete your fast, for Allah fed you and gave you drink'
C) The Quranic verse about the white and black thread
D) Consensus of the Companions

Key Takeaway
Forgetful eating, drinking, or intercourse does not invalidate the fast because the hadith provides a specific exception over qiyas.

Sawm — Fasting
intermediate
8 min
Forgetful Consumption Does Not Break the Fast: The Hanafi Ruling and Its Proof
Hanafi ruling with proof from hadith and istihsan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on forgetful eating, drinking, or intercourse during fasting and explain the proof from hadith and istihsan.

Core Idea
The fast remains valid; forgetfulness is excused because of the hadith: 'Complete your fast, for Allah fed you.'

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a common scenario: what happens if a fasting person forgetfully eats, drinks, or has intercourse? While analogy might suggest the fast is broken, the Hanafi school relies on a specific prophetic hadith and the principle of istihsan to rule that the fast remains valid. We will unpack the proof, the reasoning behind it, and the distinction from prayer.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi ruling and its scope
Identify the exact ruling: the fast is not invalidated by forgetful eating, drinking, or intercourse. Note that this applies to both obligatory and voluntary fasts.
The ruling covers all three acts equally, as they are all integral (rukn) to the fast.
2
Identify the conflicting qiyas and the opposing school
Understand that qiyas (analogy) would suggest the fast is broken because the act contradicts the essence of fasting. This is the position of Imam Malik, who analogizes to speaking forgetfully in prayer.
The opposing school is Maliki. The Hanafi response relies on a stronger textual evidence.
3
Locate the primary dalil: the hadith
The Prophet (peace be upon him) told a man who forgetfully ate and drank: 'Complete your fast, for Allah fed you and gave you drink.' This is the basis for istihsan overriding qiyas.
The hadith is narrated by al-Bukhari, Muslim, and al-Daraqutni.
4
Understand how istihsan overrides qiyas
Istihsan (juristic preference) gives priority to this specific textual evidence over general analogy. The hadith explicitly instructs completion, implying the fast is valid.
Hanafis use istihsan as a source; other schools generally reject it.
5
Analyze the distinction from prayer
The analogy with prayer is rejected because prayer has a reminding posture (e.g., standing, bowing) that makes forgetfulness rare. Fasting has no such outward reminder, so forgetfulness is more likely and thus excused.
This explains why forgetful speaking invalidates prayer but forgetful eating does not invalidate fasting.
