بَابُ مَا يُرْجِبُ الْقَضَاءَ وَالْكَفَّارَةَ
إذا أكل الصائم أو شرب أو جامع لا ياً لم يفطر والقياس أن يفطر وهو قول مالك لوجود ما يضاد الصوم فصار كالكلام ناسيا في الصلاة ووجه الاستحسان قوله عليه الصلاة والسلام للذى أكل و شرب ناسيا أتم على صومك فإنما أطعمك الله و سقاك وإذا ثبت هذا في حق الأكل والشرب ثبت في الوقاع للإستواء الركنية بخلاف الصلاة لأن هيأة الصلاة مذكرة فلا يغلب النسيان ولا مذكر في الصوم فيغلب ولا فرق بين الفرض والنفل لأن النص لم يفصل
ترجمہ یہ باب ان چیزوں کے بیان میں ہے جو قضاء اور کفارہ کو واجب کرتی ہیں
تشریح روزے کی انواع اور اقسام سے فراغت پا کر اب ان صورتوں کو بیان کریں گے جن میں روزہ فاسد ہو جاتا ہے اور فساد کی کس صورت میں قضاء اور کفارہ دونوں واجب ہوتے ہیں اور کس صورت میں فقط قضاء واجب ہوتی ہے۔
بھول کر کھانے پینے سے روزہ نہیں ٹوٹتا
إذا أكل الصَّائِمُ أَو شَرِبَ أَوْ جَامَعَ لَا يَا لَمْ يُفْطِرُ وَالْقِيَاسُ أنْ يُفْطِرَ وَهُوَ قَولُ مَالِك لِوُجُودِ مَا يُضَادُ الصَّومُ فَصَارَ كَالْكَلَام نَاسِيَّا فِي الصَّلوةِ وَوَجْهُ الْاِسْتِحْسَانِ قَوْلُهُ عَلَيْهِ الصَّلوةَ وَالسَّلَامُ لِلَّذِى أَكَلَ وَ شَرِبَ نَاسِيَّاتِمْ عَلَى صَوْمِكَ فَإِنَّمَا اَطْعَمَكَ اللهُ وَ سَقَاكَ وَإِذَا ثَبَتَ هَذَا فِي حَقِّ الْأَكْلِ وَالشَّرْبِ ثَبَتَ فِى الْوَقَاعِ لِلْإِسْتِوَاءِ الرُّكْنِيَّةِ بِخِلَافِ الصَّلوةِ لِأَنَّ هَيَأةَ الصَّلَاةِ مُذَكِّرَةً فَلَا يَغْلَبُ النِّسَانُ وَلَا مُذَكِّرَ فِي الصَّوْمِ فَيَغْلِبُ وَلَا فَرْقَ بينَ الفَرْضِ وَالنفل لأَنَّ النَّصَّ لَمْ يفصل
ترجمہ اور جب روزہ دار نے بھولے سے کھایا یا پیا با جماع کیا تو افطار نہیں ہوا اور قیاس یہ ہے کہ افطار ہو جائے ، اور یہی قول امام مالک کا ہے کیونکہ روزے کی ضد پائی گئی پس یہ نماز میں بھول کر کلام کرنے کے مانند ہو گیا۔ اور وجہ استحسان یہ ہے کہ حضور اقدس صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے اس شخص کے حق میں فرمایا ہے جس نے بھول کر کھایا پیا تھا، تو اپنا روزہ پورا کر اس لئے کہ تجھ کو اللہ نے کھلا یا اور پلایا اور جب یہ حکم کھانے اور پینے میں ثابت ہو گیا تو جماع کے حق میں بھی ثابت ہو گیا کیونکہ رکن ہونے میں سب برابر میں بر خلاف نماز کے، کیونکہ نماز کی حالت خود یا دلانے والی ہے تو نسیان غالب نہ ہوگا اور روزے میں کوئی چیز یاد دلانے والی نہیں ہے پس نسیان غالب ہو جائے گا اور فرض اور نفل کے روزے میں کوئی فرق نہیں ہے کیونکہ نص (حدیث) نے کوئی تفصیل نہیں فرمائی ہے۔ تشریح مسئلہ اگر روزہ دار بھول کر کھالے یا پی لے یا جماع کرلے تو اس کا روزہ نہیں ٹوٹے گا اور قیاس کا تقاضا یہ ہے کہ روزہ ٹوٹ جائے یہی امام مالک کا قول ہے قیاس کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ کھانا، پینا اور جماع کرنا روزے کی ضد ہے اور شئی کی ضدشئی کو معدوم کر دیتی ہے کیونکہ بیک وقت ضدین کا پایا جانا محال ہے پس جب روزے کی ضد یعنی کھا لینا وغیرہ پایا گیا تو روزہ معدوم ہو گیا اور یہ ایسا ہو گیا جیسا کہ نماز میں بھول کر کلام کرنا پس جس طرح جھول کر نماز میں کلام کرنا، نماز کو فاسد کر دیتا ہے اسی طرح بھول کر کھانا پینا روزہ کو فاسد کر دیگا۔ وجہ استحسان یہ حدیث ہے کہ ایک شخص نے بحالت صوم بھول کر کچھ کھا پی لیا تو اس سے حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ تو اپنا روزہ پورا کر، اس لئے کہ اللہ نے تجھ کو کھلایا اور پلایا ہے۔ اعتراض: رہا یہ اعتراض کہ یہ حدیث کتاب اللہ کے معارض ہے کیونکہ کتاب اللہ میں ہے " أَتِمُوا الصّيام " اور صیام اور سلام کے معنی امساک کے ہیں یعنی رکھنا، اور بھول کر کھانے پینے کی صورت میں امساک پایا نہیں گیا پس بھول کر کھانے پینے کی صورت میں آیت دلالت کرتی ہے بطلان صوم پر اور حدیث دلالت کرتی ہے بقائے صوم پر ۔ جواب: اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ کتاب اللہ میں نسیان کے معاف ہونے پر دلالت ہے چنانچہ ارشاد ہے رَبَّنَا لَا تُوا خِذْنَا إِن نَّسِينَا أَوْ أَخْطَانَا (البقرة :۲۸۶) پس جب نسیان معاف ہے تو حدیث اور کتاب اللہ میں کوئی تعارض باقی نہیں رہا۔ ہمارے مذہب کی تائید اس حدیث سے بھی ہوتی ہے جس کو شیخین نے روایت کیا ہے حدیث یہ ہے عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَ ةٌ عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَالَ مَنْ نَسِيَ وَهُوَ صَائِمٌ فَاكَلَ اوْشَرِبَ فَلْيُتِمَّ صَوْمَهُ فَإِنَّمَا أَطْعَمَهُ اللهُ وَسَقَاهُ یعنی رسول اکرم صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے فرمایا ہے جو شخص بھول گیا حالانکہ وہ روزہ دار ہے پھر اس نے کھایا پیا تو وہ اپنا روزہ پورا کرے، اس لئے کہ اللہ نے اس کو کھلایا اور پلایا ہے اور دار قطنی میں ہے رَجُلا سَأَلَ رَسُولَ اللهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ فَقَالَ إِنِّي كُنتُ صَائِمًا فَأَكَلْتُ وَ شَربُتُ نَاسِبًا فَقَالَ عَلَيْهِ السَّلامُ رَتِمُ صَوْمَكَ فَإِنَّ اللهَ أَطْعَمَك وَسَقَاكَ یعنی ایک آدمی نے رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم سے دریافت کیا اور کہا کہ میں روزے سے تھا میں نے بھول کر کھا پی لیا تو رسول خدا صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ تو اپنا روزہ پورا کر، اس لئے کہ اللہ نے تجھ کو کھلایا اور پلایا ہے نیز ایک حدیث میں ہے ان مَنْ أَقْطَرَ فِي شَهْرِ رَمَضَانَ نَاسِي فَلا قَضَاءَ عَلَيْهِ وَلَا كَفَّارَةَ یعنی جس نے رمضان کے مہینہ میں بھول کر افطار کر لیا تو اس پر نہ قضاء ہے اور نہ کفارہ بہر حال یہ تمام حدیثیں اس بات پر دلالت کرتی ہیں کہ بھول کر کھانے پینے سے روزہ نہیں ٹو تھا۔ وَاذَاثَبَتَ هَذَا فِى حَقِّ الاكل ... الخ سے سوال کا جواب ہے۔ سوال یہ ہے کہ بھول کر کھانے پینے سے روزے کا نہ ٹو شنا خلاف قیاس نص (حدیث) سے ثابت ہے اور جو چیز خلاف قیاس ثابت ہو وہ غیر کی طرف متعدی نہیں ہوتی لہذا یہ روزہ فاسد نہ ہونے کا حکم بھول کر جماع کرنے کی طرف متعدی نہ ہونا چاہئے یعنی بھول کر جماع کرنے سے روزہ ٹوٹ جانا چاہئے حالانکہ آپ نے بھول کر جماع کرنے کو بھول کر کھانے پینے پر قیاس کر کے اس پر بھی روزہ نہ ٹوٹنے کا حکم لگایا ہے۔ جواب: اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ بھول کر جماع کرنے سے روزہ کا نہ ٹو تنا قیاس سے ثابت نہیں ہے بلکہ دلالت النص سے ثابت ہے بایں طور کہ کھانے ، پینے اور جماع کرنے سے رکنا روزے کا رکن ہونے میں سب برابر ہیں لہذا جماع ، کھانے پینے کی نظیر ہوا اور چونکہ نص (حدیث) کی وجہ سے نسیانا اکل وشرب کے حق میں عدم فساد صوم کا حکم ثابت ہے لہذا انسیا نا جماع کے حق میں بھی دلالہ عدم فساد وصوم کا حکم ثابت ہو گا“۔
بخِلافِ الصَّلوۃ سے امام مالک کے قیاس علی الصلوۃ کا جواب ہے: جواب کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ روزے کو نماز پر قیاس کرنا قیاس مع الفارق ہے بایں طور کہ نماز کی حالت حالت مذکرہ ہے یعنی نماز کی حالت میں ہمہ وقت یہ یادر ہتا ہے کہ میں نماز میں ہوں کیونکہ نماز کی حالت غیر نماز کی حالت کے بالکل مختلف ہوتی ہے پس نماز کی حالت میں نسیان اور بھول کا غلبہ نہیں ہو سکے گا اس کے برخلاف روزہ کہ روزہ دار اور غیر روزہ دار دونوں کی حالت برابر ہوتی ہے کیونکہ روزہ کا تعلق باطن سے ہے نہ کہ ظاہر سے پس چونکہ روزہ دار کی ظاہری حالت عام انسانوں کی طرح ہوتی ہے اس لئے اس پر نسیان کا غالب آنا المکن اور اکثر ہے اب آپ ملاحظہ فرمائیں کہ اس قدر فرق کے ہوتے ہوئے روزے کو نماز پر قیاس کرنا کس طرح درست ہوگا۔ صاحب ہدایہ کہتے ہیں کہ روزہ نقلی ہو یا فرض ہو دونوں صورتوں میں بھول کر کھانا پینا اور جماع کرنا روزہ کو فاسد نہیں کرتا کیونکہ حدیث میں صوم فرش اور صوم نفل کی کوئی تفصیل بیان نہیں کی گئی ہے۔
Chapter on what necessitates qada and kaffarah. When a fasting person eats or drinks or has intercourse forgetfully, he does not break his fast. Analogy (qiyas) would be that he does break it, and this is the opinion of Malik, because something that contradicts fasting occurred, so it becomes like speaking forgetfully in prayer. The basis of istihsan is his statement (peace be upon him) to the one who ate and drank forgetfully: 'Complete your fast, for Allah fed you and gave you drink.' When this is established regarding eating and drinking, it is established regarding intercourse because of equality in being integral (rukn), contrary to prayer, because the state of prayer is a reminder, so forgetfulness does not overcome, and there is no reminder in fasting, so forgetfulness overcomes. There is no difference between obligatory and voluntary fasts because the text did not differentiate.
Source pages p. 205

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on what necessitates qada and kaffarah in fasting. The author first states the Hanafi ruling: if a fasting person eats, drinks, or has intercourse forgetfully, the fast is not broken. This is contrary to qiyas (analogy) that would declare the fast invalid because the action contradicts the essence of fasting (imsak). Imam Malik held that view, comparing it to speaking forgetfully in prayer, which invalidates prayer. However, the Hanafi school adopts istihsan (juristic preference) based on the authentic hadith where the Prophet (peace be upon him) told a man who forgetfully ate and drank to complete his fast because Allah fed him. The same ruling applies to intercourse because both eating/drinking and intercourse are equally integral acts (rukn) of the fast. The passage then distinguishes fasting from prayer: in prayer, the physical posture constantly reminds the worshipper of their state, so forgetfulness rarely overcomes; in fasting, there is no such outward reminder, so forgetfulness is expected to dominate. Finally, the ruling applies equally to both obligatory (fard) and voluntary (nafl) fasts because the hadith does not distinguish between them. This is the relied-upon Hanafi position.

Key Terms
القياس (al-qiyas): Analogical reasoning that would suggest the fast is broken because the act contradicts the essence of fasting.
الإستحسان (al-istihsan): Juristic preference that overrides qiyas based on a stronger evidence (here, the hadith) leading to the ruling that the fast is not broken.
النسيان (al-nisyan): Forgetfulness that excuses the act; in this ruling, it is not attributed to the person intentionally.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a fasting person forgetfully eats and drinks, what is the ruling on his fast?
A) The fast is invalid and must be made up (qada).
B) The fast is invalid and requires both qada and kaffarah.
C) The fast remains valid and no qada or kaffarah is required.
D) The fast is invalid but no qada is needed because of forgetfulness.

Key Takeaway
Forgetful consumption does not break the fast; the hadith and istihsan override analogy.

Breaking Fast by Mistake or Coercion: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Explains ruling and Shafi'i disagreement on qada for mistaken or coerced eating

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school requires qada (make-up fast) for a person who breaks the fast by mistake or coercion, and distinguish this from the Shafi'i position based on the frequency and source of the excuse.

Core Idea
Mistake and coercion require qada; forgetfulness does not — the analogy fails because forgetfulness is common and from Allah.

This lesson examines a classic Hanafi-Shafi'i dispute: when a fasting person eats or drinks by mistake or under coercion, must they make up the fast? The Hanafi school answers yes, while Imam al-Shafi'i analogizes to forgetfulness and says no. The passage you will read gives the Hanafi proof for this distinction.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi ruling
Identify that qada is wajib (obligatory) for both mistake (khat'a) and coercion (ikrah) in fasting.
This is the position from Zahir al-Riwayah.
2
Identify the opposing view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that qada is not required; he analogizes mistake/coercion to forgetfulness (nisyan), where the pen is lifted.
See the hadith: 'The pen is lifted from the forgetful...'
3
Examine the first Hanafi proof
Mistake and coercion are rare (ghayr ghalib), while forgetfulness is predominant (ghalib). The analogy is invalid due to difference in frequency.
Qiyas ma'a al-fariq – analogizing two things that differ in essential attribute.
4
Examine the second Hanafi proof
Forgetfulness comes from Allah (the Owner of the right), while coercion comes from another person. Therefore, the cases are distinct.
The source of the excuse determines the ruling.
5
Understand the prayer analogy
A chained person (muqayyad) who prays sitting must repeat after release (like coercion). A sick person (marid) does not repeat (like forgetfulness).
This analogy reinforces the distinction based on the source of the hindrance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَوْ كَانَ مُخْطِيًا أَوْ مَكْرَهَا فَعَلَيْهِ الْقَضَاءُ خِلافًا لِلشَّافِعِي فَإِنَّهُ يَعْتَبِرُهُ بِالنَّاسِى وَلَنَا أَنَّهُ لَا يَغْلِبُ وُجُودُهُ وَعُدْرُ النِّسْيَانِ غَالِبٌ وَلَأنَّ البَيَانَ مِنْ قِبَلِ مَنْ لَهُ الْحَقُّ وَالإِكْرَاهُ مِنْ قَبْلِ غَيْرِهِ فَيَفْتَرِقَان كَالْمُقَيِّدِ وَالْمَرِيضِ فِي قَضَاءِ الصَّلوة
And if he is mistaken or coerced, then qada is obligatory upon him, contrary to al-Shafi'i, for he analogizes him to the forgetful one. And for us (the Hanafis), his occurrence is not predominant, while the excuse of forgetfulness is predominant. And because forgetfulness comes from the One who has the right, while coercion comes from another, so they differ, like the chained person and the sick person regarding qada of prayer.
Source pages p. 207

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute. The author states the Hanafi ruling: if a fasting person eats or drinks by mistake (khat'a) or under coercion (ikrah), qada (make-up fast) is obligatory. Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees, as he analogizes this situation to forgetfulness (nisyan), where qada is not required. The Hanafi proof is twofold: first, the occurrence of mistake/coercion is rare, while forgetfulness is common (so analogy is invalid due to difference in frequency); second, forgetfulness originates from Allah (the One who has the right to the fast), whereas coercion comes from another person, making the two cases distinct. The author gives an analogy: a chained person (mulaqqad) who prays sitting due to being bound must repeat the prayer after release, while a sick person who prays sitting does not repeat, because sickness comes from Allah while chains come from others. Thus, the Shafi'i analogy is rejected.

Key Terms
خطاء (khat'a): A mistake where one intends to eat but forgets the fast, or accidentally swallows water while rinsing.
إكراه (ikrah): Coercion: being forced by another to eat or drink against one's will.
نسیان (nisyan): Forgetfulness: one forgets they are fasting and eats intentionally but without recalling the fast.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on qada if a fasting person is forced to eat under coercion?
A) Qada is not required.
B) Qada is required.
C) The fast becomes invalid but no qada.
D) The fast remains valid.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the distinction between predominant and rare excuses, and between divine and human source of the excuse, determines whether qada is required.

Wet Dream Does Not Break the Fast
States ruling and proof that wet dream does not nullify fast

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on wet dream during fasting and explain the two proofs (hadith and rational) that support it.

Core Idea
Involuntary ejaculation in sleep does not invalidate the fast.

A common question for fasting individuals is what breaks the fast. The Hanafi school distinguishes between voluntary and involuntary acts. In this lesson, we examine a clear ruling: a wet dream (ihtilam) does not nullify the fast. The proof combines a direct prophetic hadith and a rational analysis of the act's form and meaning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The passage begins with a conditional: if a fasting person sleeps and has a wet dream, then he does not break his fast. Identify the act (wet dream) and the ruling (fast remains valid).
The act is involuntary.
2
Examine the hadith proof
The passage cites a hadith: 'Three things do not break the fast: vomit, cupping, and wet dream.' Locate this hadith and note that it is an explicit textual proof (dalil naqli).
The hadith is ahad, but its meaning is clear (qati' al-dalalah) on this point.
3
Understand the rational proof
The passage adds a rational proof: wet dream lacks both the form (surah) of intercourse (actual penetration) and the meaning (ma'na) of intercourse (ejaculation with desire through direct physical contact). Since both are absent, the fast is not invalidated.
This addresses the underlying principle that only intentional, direct acts break the fast.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَإِن نَامَ فَاحْتَلَمَ لَمْ يُفْطِرُ لِقَوْلِهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ ثَلاثَ لَا يُفْطِرُنَ الصِّيَامُ الْقَيْءُ وَالْحَجَامَةُ وَالْإِحْتِلامُ وَلَانَّهُ لَمْ يُوجَدُ صُوْرَةُ الْجِمَاعِ وَلَا مَعْنَى وَهُوَ الْإِنْزَالُ عَنْ شَهْوَةِ بِالْمُبَاشِرَةِ
For if he sleeps and has a wet dream, he does not break his fast, because of his statement, peace be upon him: 'Three things do not break the fast: vomit, cupping, and wet dream.' And because neither the form of intercourse nor its meaning is found, and its meaning is ejaculation due to desire by direct contact.
Source pages p. 208

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling with proof. The ruling: if a fasting person sleeps and experiences a wet dream (ihtilam), his fast remains valid and is not nullified. The proof is twofold: first, a hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him) explicitly stating that three things do not break the fast: vomiting (involuntary), cupping (hijamah), and wet dream (ihtilam). Second, a rational proof: wet dream lacks both the form (surah) and meaning (ma'na) of sexual intercourse. The form of intercourse is actual penetration; the meaning is ejaculation with desire through direct physical contact. Since neither occurs in a dream, the fast is not invalidated.

Key Terms
احتلام (ihtilam): Wet dream: involuntary ejaculation during sleep.
صورۃ الجماع (surat al-jima'): The form of intercourse: actual penetration.
معنى الجماع (ma'na al-jima'): The meaning of intercourse: ejaculation with desire due to direct physical contact.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT mentioned in the hadith as not breaking the fast?
A) Vomit
B) Cupping
C) Wet dream
D) Intercourse

Key Takeaway
A wet dream (ihtilam) during sleep does not break the fast, based on direct hadith and the absence of the form and meaning of intercourse.

Looking at a Woman During Fast: Ruling and Analogy
Ruling that looking at a woman causing mani does not break fast, with analogies

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for looking at a woman with desire during fasting and apply the analogy to distinguish between actions that invalidate the fast and those that do not.

Core Idea
Looking without contact does not break the fast; only direct physical contact invalidates.

The text extends the previous ruling on thinking to looking. The key principle is that ejaculation without direct physical contact does not nullify the fast. However, there is an intra-Hanafi difference on masturbation with the hand, which some analogize to thinking but others treat differently.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling for looking
State clearly that if a fasting person looks at a woman with desire and emits semen, the fast remains valid.
This is the primary ruling presented.
2
Compare to the case of thinking
The text analogizes looking to thinking (al-mutafakkir). Both involve mental stimulation without physical contact.
The absence of direct contact is the key common element.
3
Identify the illa (effective cause)
The reason the fast is not broken is the absence of direct physical contact (mubasharah) that leads to ejaculation with desire.
The illa is 'absence of mubasharah'.
4
Apply to masturbation (istimna')
Some Hanafi scholars analogize masturbation to thinking/looking, saying the fast is not broken. Others disagree because masturbation involves intentional direct contact.
This is a point of ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi disagreement
The text says 'according to what they said' (عَلَى مَا قَالُوا), indicating a view of some mashayikh. The mufta bihi position is that masturbation by hand requires qada.
This is a legitimate difference; later fatwa collections favor qada.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَكَذَا إِذَا نَظَرَ إِلَى امْرَأَةٍ فَأَمُنى لِمَابَيْنَا وَصَارَ كَالْمُتَفَكَّرِ إِذَا أمنى وَكَالْمُسْتَمْنِي بِالْيَدِ عَلَى مَا قَالُوا
And likewise, if he looks at a woman and emits mani (semen), for what we have mentioned, and it becomes like the one who thinks (and emits mani) and like the one who masturbates with his hand, according to what they said.
Source pages p. 208

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling extended from the previous one. The ruling: if a fasting person looks at a woman (or her private parts) and semen is emitted (amana), the fast is not nullified. The reason is that neither the form nor the meaning of sexual intercourse is present. The author analogizes this to two cases: first, someone who merely thinks vividly about a woman and emits semen (mutafakkir), where the fast remains valid; second, someone who masturbates with the hand (istimna' bi al-yad), where according to some Hanafi scholars (mashayikh), the fast is also not nullified. However, there is an intra-Hanafi difference: other scholars hold that masturbation with the hand does require qada because the 'meaning' of intercourse (intentional ejaculation with desire) is present. The text notes that the permissibility of masturbation for a non-fasting person is discussed separately: if done to satisfy desire, it is forbidden based on Quranic verses about guarding private parts.

Key Terms
نظر (nazar): Looking, specifically with desire at a woman or her private parts.
إنزال (inzal): Emission of semen (mani).
استمناء باليد (istimna' bi al-yad): Masturbation using the hand.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what makes the case of looking at a woman analogous to thinking about her in terms of the fast?
A) Both involve intentional desire.
B) Both involve the absence of direct physical contact.
C) Both result in ejaculation.
D) Both are prohibited outside of fasting.

Key Takeaway
The fast remains valid when semen emission results from looking without direct contact; only direct physical contact with ejaculation nullifies the fast.

Wet Dream Does Not Break the Fast
Ruling with proof from hadith and rational argument

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a wet dream does not break the fast and explain the two proofs: the prophetic hadith and the rational argument based on absence of form and meaning of intercourse.

Core Idea
A wet dream does not break the fast because it is involuntary and lacks the form or meaning of intercourse.

This lesson addresses a common concern among fasting individuals: what if a wet dream occurs during sleep? The Hanafi school, relying on both textual and rational evidence, rules that the fast remains valid. We will examine the primary proof from a hadith and the secondary rational proof that distinguishes involuntary emission from voluntary acts that invalidate the fast.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act in question is ihtilam (wet dream) occurring while fasting. State the ruling: the fast is not broken and remains valid (sahih).
2
Examine the primary proof (hadith)
The Prophet ﷺ said: 'Three things do not break the fast: vomiting, cupping, and a wet dream.' Analyse how this hadith directly exempts wet dream from being a mufsid (invalidator).
The hadith is ahad but its meaning is clear and uncontested.
3
Examine the rational proof
The text argues that invalidating acts require either the 'form' (actual intercourse) or the 'meaning' (voluntary sexual contact with desire leading to emission). In a wet dream, neither occurs because there is no direct physical contact and the emission is involuntary.
This rational proof reinforces the hadith and addresses any potential doubt.
4
Summarize the legal conclusion
Combine both proofs to confirm that ihtilam does not break the fast. Note that this ruling is unanimous among Hanafi authorities and consistent with the principle that involuntary acts do not invalidate worship.
A common misunderstanding is that any emission breaks the fast; this lesson clarifies the distinction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَإِن نَامَ فَاحْتَلَمَ لَمْ يُفْطِرُ لِقَوْلِهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ ثَلاثَ لَا يُفْطِرُنَ الصِّيَامُ الْقَيْءُ وَالْحَجَامَةُ وَالْإِحْتِلامُ وَلَانَّهُ لَمْ يُوجَدُ صُوْرَةُ الْجِمَاعِ وَلَا مَعْنَى وَهُوَ الْإِنْزَالُ عَنْ شَهْوَةِ بِالْمُبَاشِرَةِ

احتلام سے روزہ نہیں ٹوٹتا

ترجمہ: پھر اگر روزہ دار سو گیا اور اس کو احتلام ہو گیا تو اس کا روزہ افطار نہیں ہوا کیونکہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ تین چیزیں روزہ کو افطار نہیں کرتیں قے، پچھنا لگوانا اور احتلام، اور اس لئے کہ نہ صورتاً جماع پایا گیا اور نہ معناً جماع اور معنی جماع شہوت کے ساتھ مباشرت کر کے انزال کا ہوتا ہے۔

تشریح: مسئلہ اگر روزہ دار سو گیا اور اس کو اسی حالت میں احتلام ہو گیا تو اس کا روزہ فاسد نہیں ہوگا کیونکہ حدیث ثلاث لا يفطرن الصيام القيء والحجامة والاحتلام تین چیزیں مفسد صوم نہیں ہیں ایک بے اختیار قے آنا، دوم پچھنا لگوانا، سوم احتلام ہونا، دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ احتلام میں جماع نہ صورۃ پایا گیا اور نہ معنیٰ صورۃ تو اس لئے کہ جماع کی صورت یہ ہے کہ ایک شرمگاہ دوسرے کی شرمگاہ میں داخل ہو جائے اور احتلام میں یہ بات نہیں ہوتی اور معنی جماع اس لئے نہیں پایا گیا کہ معنیٰ جماع یہ ہے کہ عورت و مرد شہوت کے ساتھ باہم چمٹ جائیں اور ادخال نہ پایا جائے لیکن انزال ہو جائے پس احتلام کی صورت میں جب نہ صورۂ جماع پایا گیا اور نہ معنی جماع پایا گیا تو روزہ فاسد ہونے کا سوال ہی پیدا نہیں ہوتا۔
Then if he sleeps and has a wet dream, he does not break his fast, because of his statement (peace be upon him): 'Three things do not break the fast: vomiting, cupping, and a wet dream.' And because neither the form of intercourse nor its meaning (which is emission with desire through direct contact) occurred. [Urdu translation and commentary follow:] If a fasting person sleeps and has a wet dream, his fast is not broken... Explained: If a fasting person sleeps and in that state has a wet dream, his fast is not invalidated because of the hadith... and the second proof is that in a wet dream neither the form of intercourse nor its meaning is found.
Source pages p. 208

Commentary
This passage provides a ruling with proof. The ruling is that a wet dream (ihtilam) does not invalidate the fast. The primary proof is the hadith of the Prophet ﷺ listing three things that do not break the fast: vomiting, cupping, and wet dream. The secondary proof is rational: the fast is only broken by actual intercourse or its legal equivalent (emission from direct contact). In a wet dream, neither the form (actual insertion) nor the meaning (voluntary sexual arousal leading to emission) of intercourse occurs, so the fast remains valid. The commentary explains that the act is involuntary and lacks the elements that would make the fast invalid.

Key Terms
احتلام (ihtilām): Wet dream; involuntary emission of semen during sleep.
صورة الجماع (ṣūrat al-jimāʿ): The physical form of intercourse: insertion of the genital into another's genital.
معنى الجماع (maʿnā al-jimāʿ): The legal meaning of intercourse: direct physical contact with sexual desire leading to emission.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary proof that a wet dream does not break the fast?
A) The verse from Surah al-Ma'arij
B) The hadith: 'Three things do not break the fast: vomiting, cupping, and wet dream'
C) Consensus of the Companions
D) Qiyas on sleeping

Key Takeaway
A wet dream during fasting does not invalidate the fast because it is involuntary and lacks the form or meaning of intercourse, as proven by prophetic hadith and rational reasoning.

Looking and Emitting Without Contact: Fast Remains Valid
Ruling that looking and emitting without contact does not break fast, with qiyas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that looking at a woman and emitting maniy does not break the fast, explain the qiyas (analogy) used, and distinguish the intra-Hanafi difference on masturbation.

Core Idea
Looking and emitting does not break the fast – only direct stimulation (surat or ma‘na of intercourse) invalidates it.

The fasting person may encounter situations where he sees a woman and, without any physical contact, experiences emission. Is his fast broken? This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling that the fast remains valid, supported by an explicit analogy (qiyas jaliy) between looking and thinking. The passage also addresses the controversial case of masturbation, where some Hanafi scholars require qada' while others do not, and clarifies the ruling for a non-fasting person.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage rules on a fasting person who looks at a woman (or her private part) and emits maniy. The ruling is that the fast is not broken (sahih).
This applies only to involuntary or voluntary looking without direct physical contact.
2
Understand the reasoning: lack of surat and ma‘na
The fast is not broken because neither the form (insertion) nor the meaning (direct physical stimulation leading to emission) of intercourse is present. This is the key principle underlying the ruling.
‘Surat’ refers to the physical act; ‘ma‘na’ refers to the essential effect (emission) caused by direct stimulation.
3
Analyze the qiyas (analogy)
The passage draws an analogy between looking and the case of a person who merely thinks about a beautiful woman and emits. Both lack direct contact. The asl (original case) is the thinking person; the far‘ (new case) is the looking person. The illa (effective cause) is the absence of direct physical contact (mubashara).
This is a jaliy (explicit) qiyas because the illa is clearly identifiable.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on masturbation
The passage mentions that some Hanafi scholars (mashayikh) hold that masturbation (istimna' bi al-yad) does not break the fast at all, while others require qada' because the meaning of intercourse (ma‘na) is present through direct hand contact. The text does not definitively resolve this difference.
This ikhtilaf is legitimate and both views are recorded in Hanafi works.
5
Distinguish the non-fasting permissibility
The commentary adds that for a non-fasting person, masturbation is absolutely haram if done for lust (based on Quran and hadith), but permissible if done solely to cool desire (e.g., to avoid sin). This is a separate ruling not directly related to the fasting case.
This distinction is important for comprehensive fiqh understanding but does not affect the fasting ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَكَذَا إِذَا نَظَرَ إِلَى امْرَأَةٍ فَأَمُنى لِمَا بَيْنَا وَصَارَ كَالْمُتَفَكِّرِ إِذَا أمنى وَكَالْمُسْتَمْنِي بِالْيَدِ عَلَى مَا قَالُوا ... الخ

عورت کی شرمگاہ دیکھی اور منی نکل گئی روزہ فاسد نہیں ہوا

ترجمہ: اور اسی طرح اگر کسی عورت کو دیکھا اور منی نکل گئی اور اس دلیل کی وجہ سے جو ہم نے بیان کی ہے اور یہ ایسا ہو گیا جیسے متفکر جبکہ اس کی منی نکل آئی اور ہتھیلی سے منی نکالنے والے کے مانند ہوگیا اس قول کی بناء پر جو مشائخ نے کہا ہے۔

تشریح: اگر کسی روزہ دار نے کسی اچھی سی عورت کو یا اس کی شرمگاہ کو دیکھا اور غریب کی منی نکل گئی تو اس کا روزہ فاسد نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ اس صورت میں بھی جماع نہ صورت پایا گیا اور نہ معنی اور یہ ایسا ہو گیا جیسے کوئی روزہ دار کسی حسین اور خوبصورت عورت کا تصور کر کے بیٹھ گیا اور اسی تصور میں منی خارج ہو گئی تو اس کا روزہ فاسد نہ ہوگا اور جیسے روزہ دار اپنی ہتھیلی سے منی نکالے تو اس کا روزہ فاسد نہ ہوگا بعض مشائخ اسی کے قائل ہیں البتہ بعض کا خیال یہ ہے کہ استمناء بالید کی صورت میں قضا واجب ہوگی کیونکہ استمناء بالید کی صورت میں معنی جماع پایا گیا ہے اب رہی یہ بات کہ غیر صائم کے لئے یہ حرکت جائز ہے یا نہیں؟ تو اس بارے میں قدرے تفصیل ہے چنانچہ استمناء بالید سے اگر قضا شہوت مقصود ہے تو قطعا جائز نہیں کیونکہ اللہ تعالیٰ نے فرمایا وَلَّذِينَ هُمْ لِفُرُوجِهِمْ حَافِظُونَ إِلَّا عَلَى أَزْوَاجِهِمْ أَوْ مَا مَلَكَتْ أَيْمَانُهُمْ فَإِنَّهُمْ غَيْرُ مَلُومِينَ فَمَنِ ابْتَغَى وَرَاءَ ذَالِكَ فَأُولَئِكَ هُمْ الْعَادُونَ (المعارج: 30-31) ابن حریج کہتے ہیں کہ میں نے عطاء سے دریافت کیا تو عطاء نے کہا کہ میں نے سنا ہے کہ ایک قوم قیامت میں اس حال میں آئے گی کہ ان کے ہاتھ حامل والے ہوں گے پس میرا خیال ہے کہ وہ لوگ یہی استمنا بالید کرنے والے ہیں اور حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ناكح اليد ملعون ہاتھ کے ساتھ جماع کرنے والا ملعون ہے اور ہاتھ کے ساتھ جماع کرنا یہی استمنا بالید ہے اور اگر استمناء بالید سے شہوت کو ٹھنڈا کرنا مراد ہے تو اس میں کوئی مضائقہ نہیں ہے۔
Similarly, if he looks at a woman and emits maniy, [he does not break his fast] because of what we have stated, and he becomes like the one who thinks and emits, and like the one who masturbates with his hand, according to what they said... [Urdu translation:] If a fasting person looks at a beautiful woman or her private part and maniy comes out, his fast is not invalidated... Explanation: If a fasting person looks at a beautiful woman or her private part and maniy comes out, his fast is not invalidated because in this case neither the form nor the meaning of intercourse is found. It is like a person who imagines a beautiful woman and maniy comes out, or like the one who masturbates with his hand. Some scholars hold that in the case of masturbation, qada' is obligatory because the meaning of intercourse is found. As for whether it is permissible for a non-fasting person: if the purpose is to satisfy desire, it is absolutely impermissible, based on the Quranic verse (70:30-31) and hadith 'The one who marries his hand is cursed.' But if the purpose is to cool desire, there is no harm.
Source pages p. 208

Commentary
This passage rules on a scenario where a fasting person looks at a woman (or her private part) and emits maniy without any direct contact. The ruling is that the fast is not broken. The reasoning is that neither the form (insertion) nor the meaning (direct physical stimulation leading to emission) of intercourse is present. The commentary provides analogies: (1) a person who merely thinks about a beautiful woman and has emission; (2) a person who masturbates (istimna' bi al-yad). The text notes an intra-Hanafi dispute: some scholars hold that masturbation requires qada', but the majority (some mashayikh) say it does not break the fast at all. Then the commentary shifts to discuss the permissibility of masturbation for a non-fasting person, citing the Quranic verse and a hadith declaring such a person cursed if done for lust, but permissible if done to cool desire. This is additional guidance beyond the fasting ruling.

Key Terms
نظر (nazar): Looking, gazing (at a woman or her private part).
امنیٰ (أمنى) (amannā / amnā): He emitted maniy.
متفکر (mutafakkir): One who thinks or imagines (a beautiful woman) and emits.
استمناء باليد (istimnā' bi al-yad): Masturbation using the hand.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) The analogy of thinking about a beautiful woman and emitting
C) The analogy of eating forgetfully
D) The analogy of a wet dream

Key Takeaway
Looking at a woman and emitting maniy does not break the fast because neither the form nor the meaning of intercourse is present, as confirmed by the analogy to thinking and emitting.

Applying Oil, Cupping, and Kohl Do Not Break the Fast
Ruling with proof and refutation of objection

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on oil, cupping, and kohl during fasting and explain the proof for each, including the refutation of the objection against kohl.

Core Idea
Substances entering through pores do not break the fast; only open passages matter.

This passage addresses three common concerns: applying oil, cupping, and using kohl. Each is ruled permissible and non-invalidating because they do not introduce anything into the body through an open passage like the mouth or nose. The proof for kohl is particularly detailed, showing that the eye has no direct channel to the brain and that tears seep through pores. An objection from a hadith that seems to prohibit kohl is resolved by citing the Prophet's ﷺ practice on 'Ashura.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three actions and their common ruling
State that oil application, cupping, and kohl are all ruled not to break the fast. Note the overall bond: none involve entry through an open passage.
These are not invalidating acts (mufṭirāt).
2
Analyze the proof for oil and cupping
For oil, the absence of a contradictory element (munāfī) is cited. For cupping, a hadith directly exempts it (ثلاث لا يفطرن الصيام: القيء والحجامة والاحتلام). Recognize the ḥadīth as a direct textual proof.
The hadith is clear; no further analysis needed for cupping.
3
Examine the rational proof for kohl
The text gives a rational argument: there is no passage (manfadh) between the eye and the brain; tears exit through pores (masām). Anything entering through pores does not invalidate the fast, just as bathing in cold water does not break it even if coolness is felt internally.
The effect (taste in throat) is not the substance itself; only the substance entering via an open passage would break the fast.
4
Consider the objection and its refutation
A hadith says 'Let the fasting person avoid kohl.' The response: the Prophet ﷺ recommended kohl on 'Ashura, and the ummah agreed. This overrides (or indicates abrogation of) the earlier prohibition. Understand that later practice and consensus (ijmāʿ) can clarify or supersede isolated reports.
The 'Ashura practice is well-established and used as a preponderant proof (tarjīḥ).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَوِ ادْهَنَ لَمْ يَفْطِرُ لِعَدَمَ الْمُنَافِي وَكَذَا إِذَا احْتَجَمَ لِهَذَا وَ لِمَا رَوَيْنَا وَلَوْ اكْتَحَلَ لَمْ يُفْطِرُ لِأَنَّهُ لَيْسَ بَيْنَ الْعَيْنِ وَالدِّمَاغِ مَنفَةٌ وَالدَّمَعُ يَتَرَشَحُ كَالْعِرْقِ وَالدَّاخِلُ مِنَ الْمَسَامِ لَا يُنَا فِي كَمَا لَوْ اغْتَسَلَ بِالْمَاءِ الْبَارِدِ

جیل اور سرمہ لگانے سے روزہ فاسد نہیں ہوتا (عنایہ شرح نقایہ)

ترجمہ: اور اگر روزہ دار نے تیل لگایا تو افطار نہیں ہوا کیونکہ منافی صوم نہیں پایا گیا اور ایسے ہی جب پچھنا لگایا اس دلیل کی وجہ سے اور اس حدیث کی وجہ سے جو ہم نے روایت کی ہے اور اگر سرمہ لگایا تو بھی افطار نہیں ہوا۔ کیونکہ آنکھ اور دماغ کے درمیان کوئی راستہ نہیں ہے آنسو پسینہ کی طرح ٹپکتے ہیں اور مسامات میں داخل ہونے والی چیز روزے کے منافی نہیں ہے۔ جیسے اگر کسی نے ٹھنڈے پانی سے غسل کیا ہو۔

تشریح: مسئلہ - بدن یا سر میں تیل لگانا روزے کا فاسد نہیں کرتا کیونکہ روزہ اس وقت فاسد ہوتا ہے جبکہ روزہ کے منافی کوئی چیز پائی جائے اور تیل لگانا منافی صوم ہے نہیں اس لئے اس سے روزہ فاسد نہ ہوگا اور پچھنا لگوانا بھی مفسد صوم نہیں ہے ایک تو اسی لئے کہ پچھنا لگوانا منافی صوم نہیں ۔ دوم اس حدیث کی وجہ سے جو ہم سابق میں روایت کر چکے یعنی ثلاثٌ لا يفطرن الصيام القيء والحجامة والاحتلام اور اگر سرمہ لگایا تب بھی روزہ فاسد نہ ہوگا ۔ اگر چہ حلق میں اس کا مزہ محسوس ہوا ہو کیونکہ آنکھ اور دماغ کے درمیان کوئی راستہ نہیں ہے اس لئے سرمہ کا حلق میں جا ناممکن نہیں ہے اور رہا یہ کہ جب آنکھ اور دماغ کے درمیان کوئی راستہ نہیں تو حلق میں اس کا مزہ کیونکر محسوس ہوا اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ مزہ سرمہ کا اثر ہے نہ کہ عین سرمہ اور روزہ عین سرمہ کے حلق میں جانے سے ٹوٹتا ہے نہ کہ سرمہ کے اثر سے اور رہا یہ اعتراض کہ آنکھ اور دماغ کے درمیان جب کوئی راہ نہیں تو آنسو کہاں سے نکلتے ہیں؟ اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ آنسو پسینہ کی طرح مسامات کے اندر سے مترشح ہوتے ہیں اور مسامات کے ذریعہ داخل ہونے والی چیز روزے کے منافی نہیں ہے لہذا اس سے روزہ نہیں ٹوٹے گا جیسا کہ اگر کسی روزہ دار نے ٹھنڈے پانی سے غسل کیا اور ٹھنڈک کا اثر دل و دماغ تک پہنچ گیا تو اس سے روزہ نہیں ٹوٹے گا کیونکہ ٹھنڈک کا حصول بذریعہ مسامات ہوا ہے۔

لیکن اگر یہ سوال کیا جائے کہ حدیث سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ روزے کی حالت میں سرمہ لگانا ممنوع ہے کیونکہ معبد بن ہوذۃ انصاری اللہ کے رسول صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم سے روایت کرتے ہیں کہ آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا عَلَيْكُمُ بِالْإِثْمَدِ الْمِرْوَحِ وَقْتَ النَّوْمِ وَلْيَتَّقِهِ الصَّائِمُ یعنی تم سوتے وقت راحت بخش اثمد کا سرمہ لگایا کرو اور روزہ دار اس کو لگانے سے اجتناب کرے اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ روزہ دار سرمہ کا استعمال نہ کرے۔ جواب: صاحب عنایہ نے فرمایا کہ رسول اکرم صلى الله عليه وسلم نے عاشوراء کا روزہ اور اس دن سرمہ لگانا مندوب کیا ہے اور امت نے عاشورہ کے دن سرمہ لگانے پر اتفاق بھی کیا ہے پس یہ روایت سابقہ روایت سے رائج ہے۔ نیز صاحب کفایہ نے ابورافع کی
And if he applies oil, he does not break his fast due to absence of that which contradicts fasting. And similarly, if he undergoes cupping, due to this and because of what we narrated. And if he applies kohl, he does not break his fast, because there is no passage between the eye and the brain; tears seep like sweat; and what enters through pores does not invalidate, just as if he bathed with cold water. [Urdu translation:] If a fasting person applies oil, the fast is not broken because no contradictory element is found; similarly cupping... and kohl does not break it because there is no passage between eye and brain; tears seep like sweat; what enters through pores does not invalidate. [Commentary explains: oil and cupping do not break the fast; kohl also does not break it even if its taste is felt in the throat, because the taste is an effect, not the substance itself. Tears exit through pores, not a direct passage. Then an objection is raised: a hadith says 'The fasting person should avoid kohl.' The answer is that the Prophet ﷺ recommended kohl on the day of 'Ashura along with fasting, and the ummah agreed, so that hadith is abrogated or overridden.]
Source pages p. 209

Commentary
This passage covers three distinct rulings on things that do not break the fast: applying oil (duhn) to the body or head, cupping (hijama), and applying kohl (kuhl) to the eyes. The primary justification is that nothing enters the body through an open passage (e.g., mouth or nose) that would invalidate the fast. For oil and cupping, it is simply not a contradictory action. For kohl, there is a detailed rational proof: there is no direct passage between the eye and the brain; tears emerge through pores (masam), just like sweat. Even if the taste of kohl is sensed in the throat, that is an effect, not the substance itself. The commentary then addresses an objection from a hadith that seems to prohibit kohl for the fasting person. It resolves this by pointing to the established sunnah of the Prophet ﷺ on 'Ashura, where fasting and applying kohl are both recommended. This indicates that the prohibition was either abrogated or restricted, and the practice of the ummah confirms its permissibility.

Key Terms
ادّهان (ادْهَنَ) (idhān / adhana): Applying oil (to the body or hair).
احتجام (احْتَجَمَ) (iḥtijām / iḥtajama): Cupping; a therapeutic practice of drawing blood to the surface.
اكتحال (اكْتَحَلَ) (iktihāl / iktaḥala): Applying kohl (antimony) to the eyes.
مسام (masām): Pores in the skin; minute openings through which sweat and tears can pass.
منفذ (manfadh): An open passage or channel; skin pores are not considered open passages.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary reason given for kohl not breaking the fast?
A) The Prophet ﷺ forbade it during fasting
B) There is no passage between the eye and the brain, and it enters only through pores
C) It is not food or drink
D) It is a medicinal application

Key Takeaway
Oil, cupping, and kohl do not break the fast because they involve no entry through an open passage; the 'Ashura practice overrides the prohibition hadith for kohl.

Sawm — Fasting
intermediate
8 min
Oil, Cupping, and Kohl Do Not Break the Fast
Rulings and proofs for oil, cupping, and kohl not invalidating fasting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on oil, cupping, and kohl during fasting and explain the proofs and response to the opposing hadith.

Core Idea
Only entry through open passages breaks the fast – oil, cupping, and kohl are safe.

This passage from Al-‛Ināyah Sharḥ al-Nuqāyah addresses three common concerns: applying oil, undergoing cupping, and using kohl while fasting. The author establishes that none invalidate the fast, grounding each ruling in clear principles and prophetic practice. We will walk through the evidence and address a key objection.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
State the three actions and the Hanafi hukm for each: applying oil, cupping, and kohl are all permissible and do not break the fast.
The ruling is mubah (permissible) but the focus is on invalidation.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites a hadith: 'Three things do not break the fast: vomiting, cupping, and wet dream.' For kohl, specific hadiths of the Prophet applying kohl while fasting are used.
The hadith is narrated in various collections; its transmission is zanni but meaning clear.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The explicit mention of cupping in the hadith shows it is not a nullifier. For kohl, the lack of a direct passage between eye and throat means no entry through an open passage; any substance that enters via pores (masam) does not invalidate the fast.
Analogy: cold bath cools the body through pores without breaking the fast.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some schools (e.g., Shafi‛ī) consider cupping or kohl breaking the fast if substance reaches the throat. Also, a hadith seems to prohibit kohl for the fasting person.
The objection is based on a weak or abrogated hadith.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The Hanafi position is muftā bihi, supported by multiple authentic hadiths of the Prophet's practice, including on Ashura when fasting was obligatory. The contrary hadith is superseded.
The author of Al-‛Ināyah and Al-Kifāyah provide these narrations.

Oil and kohl do not break the fast. (From 'Inayah Sharh Nuqayah): And if he applies oil, he does not break his fast due to the absence of that which contradicts fasting. Similarly, if he undergoes cupping, for this reason and due to what we have narrated. And if he applies kohl, he does not break his fast because there is no passage between the eye and the brain, and tears seep through like sweat, and what enters through the pores does not contradict fasting, just as if he bathed with cold water. Commentary: The issue is that applying oil to the body or head does not invalidate fasting because fasting is only invalidated when something contradictory to fasting occurs, and applying oil is not contradictory. Likewise, cupping is not invalidating, first for that reason, second due to the hadith we previously narrated: 'Three things do not break the fast: vomiting, cupping, and wet dream.' And if he applies kohl, the fast is still not invalidated, even if its taste is felt in the throat, because there is no passage between the eye and the brain, so it is impossible for kohl to reach the throat. As for how the taste is felt, the answer is that the taste is the effect of kohl, not the substance itself, and the fast breaks only from the substance entering the throat, not from its effect. As for how tears come out, the answer is that tears seep through the pores like sweat, and what enters through the pores does not contradict fasting, so the fast is not broken, just as if a fasting person bathes with cold water and the coolness reaches the heart and brain, the fast is not broken because the coolness is obtained through pores. But if it is asked that a hadith indicates that applying kohl while fasting is prohibited, because Ma'bad ibn Hudha al-Ansari narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Use ithmid kohl that invigorates at night, and the fasting person should avoid it.' The answer: The author of 'Inayah stated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) made fasting on Ashura and applying kohl on that day recommended, and the ummah has agreed on applying kohl on Ashura, so this narration is superseded by the previous one. Also, the author of Kifayah narrated the hadith of Abu Rafi': 'The Prophet (peace be upon him) called for a kohl container of ithmid in Ramadan, and he applied kohl while fasting.' And the hadith of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud: 'The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) came out on Ashura from the house of Umm Salamah with his eyes filled with kohl, which Umm Salamah had applied. Ibn Mas'ud said this was when fasting on Ashura was obligatory and later abrogated.' Mulla Ali Qari in Sharh Nuqayah wrote from Ibn Majah the hadith of Aisha: 'He (peace be upon him) applied kohl while fasting.' All these narrations testify that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) used to apply kohl while fasting.
Source pages p. 209

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It addresses three actions: applying oil, cupping, and applying kohl (surma) while fasting. The author establishes that none of these invalidate the fast. The reasoning is based on the principle that fasting is only broken by something that directly contradicts it, i.e., entry of a substance into the body through an open passage. Oil and cupping do not involve entry of anything into the internal body. Kohl is addressed in detail: although some may think it reaches the throat via the tear duct, the author clarifies that there is no direct passage between the eye and the brain/throat; tears exit through pores, not a duct. Therefore, any substance entering through pores does not break the fast, analogized to the cooling effect of a cold bath. The author then addresses a potential objection from a hadith that seems to prohibit kohl for the fasting person. The response is that this hadith is abrogated or superseded by numerous authentic hadiths showing that the Prophet himself applied kohl while fasting, including on Ashura when the fast was obligatory. Thus, the permissibility is established.

Key Terms
ادْهَنَ (adhana): Applied oil to the hair or skin
احْتَجَمَ (ihtajama): Underwent cupping (hijama)
اكْتَحَلَ (iktahala): Applied kohl (antimony) to the eyes
مَسَام (masam): Pores of the skin through which substances can seep but not in a way that breaks the fast
مُنَافِي (munafi): Something that contradicts (the fast), i.e., an invalidator

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
According to the Hanafi school, applying oil, cupping, and kohl do not invalidate the fast based on hadith and the principle that only entry through open passages breaks the fast.

Kissing While Fasting Without Ejaculation
Ruling statement with comparative analysis

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on kissing one's spouse while fasting and explain when it invalidates the fast.

Core Idea
Kissing without ejaculation does not break the fast.

This passage clarifies that not every act of intimacy with a spouse during fasting is invalidating. The key factor is whether ejaculation occurs, because the invalidator of fasting is intercourse in form (physical penetration) or meaning (emission). The author also contrasts this with rulings on revocation of divorce (raj'ah) and marital prohibition (musaharah), which are established even without ejaculation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is kissing one's spouse while fasting. The ruling is that the fast remains valid if no ejaculation occurs.
The ruling is conditional on the absence of ejaculation.
2
Understand the legal reasoning
The fast is invalidated by intercourse (jima') in form or meaning. Kissing without ejaculation lacks both: no penetration (form) and no emission (meaning).
This is based on the principle that the invalidator must be present in actuality or effect.
3
Compare with raj'ah and musaharah
In the cases of revoking a divorce and establishing marital prohibition, kissing with desire is sufficient even without ejaculation. The difference is that those rulings depend on the cause (sabab) of intercourse, not its completion.
This shows that the same act can have different legal effects depending on the context.
4
Note the scope of the ruling
The ruling applies only to kissing that does not lead to ejaculation. If ejaculation occurs, the fast is invalidated and requires qada (and kaffarah if intentional).
The ruling also implies that kissing is permissible (mubah) as long as one controls desire.

وَ لَوْ قَبَّلَ امْرَأَةٌ لَا يُفْسِدُ صَوْمَهُ يُرِيدُ بِهِ إِذَا لَمْ يُنْزِلُ لَعَدَمِ الْمُنَافِى صُورَةً وَ مَعْنى بِخِلَافِ الرَّجْعَةِ وَالْمُصَاهَرَةِ لأنّ الْحُكْمَ هُناكَ أَدِيرَ عَلَى السَّبَبِ عَلَى مَايَأْتِي فِي مَوْضِعِهِ إِنْ شَاءَ اللَّهُ
ترجمہ اور اگر کسی عورت کا بوسہ لیا تو روزہ دار کا روزہ فاسد نہ ہوگا مراد اس سے یہ ہے کہ جب انزال نہ ہوا ہو کیونکہ منافی صوم نہ صور پایا گیا اور نہ معنی ، برخلاف رجعت اور مصاہرت کے کیونکہ رجعت اور مصاہرت میں حکم کا مدار سبب پر ہے چنانچہ اپنے موقع پر آئے گا ان شاء اللہ تعالی ۔

The fast is not invalidated by kissing a woman without ejaculation: And if he kisses a woman, it does not invalidate his fast, meaning when he does not ejaculate, due to the absence of contradiction in form and meaning. Unlike the case of revocation of divorce (raj'ah) and relation by marriage (musaharah), because the ruling there is attached to the cause, as will come in its place, God willing. Commentary: The issue is that if a fasting person kisses a woman and does not ejaculate, his fast is not invalidated, because without ejaculation, intercourse is not found in form nor in meaning, whereas the invalidator of fasting is intercourse, whether in form or meaning. Unlike raj'ah and musaharah, which are established by kissing with desire and touching with desire, even without ejaculation, because these two are dependent on the cause of intercourse.
Source pages p. 210

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement. It clarifies that kissing one's spouse while fasting does not break the fast provided there is no ejaculation. The reasoning is that the fast is only broken by actual intercourse (jima') in form or meaning. Kissing without desire or without ejaculation lacks both the form (physical penetration) and the meaning (emission of fluid) of intercourse. The author distinguishes this from rulings on raj'ah (revocation of divorce during the waiting period) and musaharah (prohibition due to marriage relation), which can be established by kissing with desire even without ejaculation, because those rulings are based on the cause (sabab) of intercourse, not on the full act.

Key Terms
قَبَّلَ (qabbala): To kiss
أَنْزَلَ (anzala): To ejaculate, emit semen
رَجْعَة (raj'ah): Revocation of a revocable divorce during the waiting period
مُصَاهَرَة (musaharah): Relation by marriage; prohibition due to marriage ties

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a fasting husband kisses his wife without ejaculation, what is the ruling according to the Hanafi school?
A) The fast is invalidated and requires qada and kaffarah
B) The fast is invalidated but only qada is required
C) The fast remains valid and is not broken
D) The fast is makruh but still valid

Key Takeaway
Kissing without ejaculation does not break the fast; the fast is only invalidated by intercourse in form or meaning (ejaculation).

Ejaculation from Kissing or Touching: Qada without Kaffarah
Ruling with reasoning (ta'lil) on ejaculation from kissing/touching in fasting.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for ejaculation from kissing or touching during fasting and explain why qada is required but not kaffarah.

Core Idea
Ejaculation from kissing or touching invalidates the fast but requires only qada, not kaffarah.

This lesson examines a specific scenario where a fasting person experiences ejaculation not through full intercourse but through kissing or touching with desire. The Hanafi school draws a careful distinction: while the fast is broken and must be made up (qada), the heavy expiation (kaffarah) is not imposed. The reasoning hinges on the principle that kaffarah requires a complete offense, and doubts (shubhah) avert it. Let's explore the legal reasoning step by step.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act is ejaculation resulting from a kiss or touch while fasting. The ruling is that the fast becomes invalid (fasid), requiring qada (a makeup day) but not kaffarah.
Hanafi position: only penetration triggers kaffarah.
2
Understand the reasoning for qada
Qada is required because the 'meaning of intercourse' (ejaculation) has occurred, which is a nullifier in meaning, even if not in form. The existence of a nullifier – whether in form or meaning – is sufficient to necessitate compensation (qada) out of precaution.
Precaution (ihtiyat) demands that the fast be made up when there is any doubt about its validity.
3
Understand the reasoning for no kaffarah
Kaffarah is not required because it demands 'completeness' of the offense (kamal al-jinayah). The act lacked the full form of intercourse. Moreover, kaffarah is repelled by doubts (shubhah), akin to hudud punishments. Since there is a doubt whether this act constitutes the full nullifier, the severe penalty is avoided.
The principle 'admit the prescribed penalties by doubts' (idra' al-hudud bi al-shubuhat) extends to kaffarah.
4
Apply the principle of shubhah
The doubt here is whether the act (kissing/touching leading to ejaculation) is equivalent to full intercourse. Because it is not, the doubt suspends kaffarah. This is consistent with the Hanafi legal maxim that punitive measures are averted where doubt exists.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

وَلَوْ أَنْزَلَ بِقَبْلَةٍ أَوْ لَـمْس فَعَلَيْهِ الْقَضَاءُ دُونَ الْكَفَّارَة لِوُجُودِ مَعْنَى الْحِمَاعِ وَوُجُودِ الْمُنَافِى صُورَةً أَوْ مَعْنَى يَكْفِي لا يُجَابِ الْقَضَاءِ اِحْتِيَاطًا أَمَّا الْكَفَّارَةُ فَتَفْتَقِرُ إلى كَمَالِ الْجِنَايَةِ لِأَنَّهَا تَنْدَرِئُ بِالشُّبُهَاتِ كَالْحُدُودِ

And if he ejaculates due to a kiss or touch, then qada is upon him, not kaffarah, because the meaning of intercourse is found, and the existence of the contradictory in form or meaning is sufficient for requiring qada as a precaution. As for kaffarah, it requires completion of the offense, because it is repelled by doubts, like hudud punishments. Commentary: The issue is that if a fasting person ejaculates from kissing or touching, qada (making up the fast) is obligatory, but not kaffarah (expiation). The rational is that the 'meaning' of intercourse (i.e., ejaculation) has occurred, and the presence of a nullifier in form or meaning is enough to necessitate qada as a precaution. Kaffarah, however, requires the full offense (actual intercourse), because kaffarah is repelled by doubts, similar to the fixed punishments (hudud).
Source pages p. 210

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with reasoning (ta'lil). It addresses the scenario where a fasting person kisses or touches his spouse with desire and ejaculates. The Hanafi ruling is that this invalidates the fast, requiring only qada (a makeup day), not kaffarah (expiation). The reasoning is that although the 'meaning' of intercourse—ejaculation—is present, the act lacks the full form of actual intercourse. For kaffarah to be obligatory, the offense must be complete in both form and meaning. Because there is a doubt (shubha) whether this act fully constitutes the nullifier, kaffarah is not imposed, analogous to how hudud punishments are suspended in cases of doubt.

Key Terms
قَضَاء (qada): Compensatory fast, i.e., making up a missed day of fasting
كَفَّارَة (kaffarah): Expiation: a heavy penalty for breaking a fast by sexual intercourse during Ramadan, which involves freeing a slave, fasting two months consecutively, or feeding sixty poor people.
جِنَايَة (jinayah): Offense, crime; here referring to the act of breaking the fast intentionally
شُبْهَة (shubhah): Doubt, uncertainty; a legal principle that averts severe penalties

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, ejaculation from kissing or touching during fasting requires only qada (a makeup day), not kaffarah, because the offense is incomplete and kaffarah is averted by doubts.

Kohl While Fasting: Hanafi Proof from Hadith
Proof from multiple hadiths for permissibility

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on applying kohl while fasting and identify the hadith evidence that supports it.

Core Idea
Applying kohl does not break the fast — the Prophet's own practice proves it.

Many assume that anything entering the body invalidates the fast. The Hanafi school, however, distinguishes based on whether the substance reaches the stomach. This lesson examines the primary proof: the Prophet ﷺ himself applied kohl while fasting. We will walk through the hadith evidence and the legal reasoning that makes this act permissible.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being discussed (applying kohl to the eyes) and what the Hanafi ruling is (permissible/mubah).
The ruling is based on direct action of the Prophet, not mere analogy.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the proof texts: the hadiths cited in the passage. They include a hadith about Ramadan, one about Ashura, and a narration from Aisha. All show the Prophet applying kohl while fasting.
These are ahad hadith, but their number and consistency strengthen the proof.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how these hadiths prove permissibility. The Prophet's action is a sunnah that indicates permissibility (ibaha). If kohl nullified the fast, he would not have done it.
The Hanafi principle: the Prophet's actions that are not clearly obligatory or prohibited indicate permissibility.
4
Note the cross-madhhab disagreement
Some scholars (e.g., some Shafi'is) consider kohl makruh or even breaking because they treat any substance entering the body through an open passage as a nullifier. The Hanafi school restricts nullifiers to substances reaching the stomach or having nutritional value.
The difference stems from the definition of 'ayn (substance) and the concept of 'ain al-mufattira.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position (mufta bihi) is that kohl is permissible and does not break the fast. The hadith evidence is clear, and the ruling is consistent with the principle that only things entering the stomach or providing nutrition nullify the fast.
This is the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school.

These hadiths serve as direct evidence that applying kohl does not break the fast. The Hanafi school uses these proofs to establish that anything that does not reach the stomach or have nutritional value is not a nullifier of fasting, and kohl falls under this category. The passage highlights that the practice of the Prophet is the primary source for this ruling.

Kissing or Touching with Ejaculation: Qada Required, Kaffarah Waived
Ruling on ejaculation from kissing/touching during fasting with proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on ejaculation from kissing or touching during fasting, explain why qada is required but not kaffarah, and apply the distinction between the form and meaning of intercourse.

Core Idea
Ejaculation without penetration breaks the fast but does not require kaffarah; doubts repel expiatory penalties.

This lesson examines a subtle scenario in fasting law: what happens when a fasting person kisses or touches his spouse with desire and ejaculates? The Hanafi school draws a careful distinction between the physical act of intercourse (form) and its essential effect (meaning). The ruling provides important insight into how Islamic law balances strictness in obligations with leniency in penalties when doubt exists.

Guided Path
1
State the scenario and ruling
Identify the act (kissing/touching leading to ejaculation) and the two-part ruling: fast invalidated → qada wajib, but no kaffarah.
2
Locate the underlying principles
The ruling invokes two key concepts: 'meaning of intercourse' (ma'na al-jima') and 'doubt repelling penalties' (shubuhat). Understand each.
Ma'na al-jima' refers to ejaculation, the essential effect; surah (form) refers to penetration.
3
Trace the reasoning for qada
Because the 'opposite of fasting' (munafi) exists either in form or meaning, qada is required as a precaution (ihtiyat). Show that ejaculation constitutes the meaning of intercourse, thus breaking the fast.
4
Trace the reasoning for no kaffarah
Kaffarah demands a complete violation (kamil al-jinayah). Here the form is missing, creating a doubt. Kaffarah is repelled by doubts, analogous to hudud penalties.
The principle 'al-hudud tudra'u bi al-shubuhat' (penalties are repelled by doubts) is extended to kaffarah.
5
Apply the distinction to new scenarios
Given a scenario (e.g., mere touching without desire or ejaculation), determine whether qada or kaffarah applies using the form/meaning distinction. If no ejaculation, the fast is not invalidated.
Touching without desire and without ejaculation does not break the fast according to the Hanafi school.

The chapter: If ejaculation occurs from kissing or touching, qada is required, not kaffarah. And if he ejaculates from a kiss or touch, then upon him is qada without kaffarah, because the meaning of intercourse is found, and the presence of the opposite (of fasting) in form or meaning suffices for qada as a precaution. As for kaffarah, it depends on complete violation, because it is repelled by doubts like the hudud penalties. Translation: And if from kissing and touching the fasting person ejaculates, then upon him qada is obligatory, not kaffarah, because the meaning of intercourse is found, and the presence of the opposite in form or meaning is sufficient for making qada obligatory as a precaution. As for kaffarah, it is contingent on complete violation, because expiations are repelled by doubts, like hudud. Commentary: If a fasting person kisses a woman or touches her and ejaculates, his fast is invalidated. Now upon him is qada of that day; kaffarah is not obligatory. Qada is obligatory because although intercourse in form is not found (since they did not actually copulate), they embraced with desire and ejaculation occurred, which is called the meaning of intercourse. For qada, the presence of the opposite of fasting (either in form or meaning) is sufficient. As for kaffarah not being obligatory, the reason is that kaffarah is only obligatory when the crime is completely actualized. Here, due to the absence of intercourse in form, the crime is lightened; indeed a kind of doubt about the occurrence of intercourse arises. It is accepted that expiations are repelled by doubts, just as hudud penalties are repelled by doubts.

Commentary
This passage gives the ruling for a more serious case: if a fasting person kisses or touches his spouse with desire and ejaculates, his fast is invalidated. However, the only obligation is to make up that day (qada). There is no need for kaffarah (expiation), which is required for deliberate sexual intercourse during fasting. The reasoning is that ejaculation means the meaning of intercourse (ma'na al-jima') is present, even though the actual form (surah) of intercourse is absent. For qada, the presence of either form or meaning is sufficient, as a precautionary measure. But kaffarah requires a complete violation (kamil al-jinayah). Since there is a doubt (shubhah) about whether full intercourse occurred (because the form is missing), kaffarah is waived, similar to how penalties (hudud) are waived under doubts.

انزال (inzāl): Ejaculation of semen.
معنی جماع (ma'nā al-jimā'): The 'meaning of intercourse' i.e., ejaculation without actual penetration.

Key Takeaway
Ejaculation from kissing or touching during fasting invalidates the fast and requires qada, but kaffarah is waived due to the absence of complete intercourse and the principle that doubts repel penalties.

Kissing While Fasting: The Role of Consequences and the Hanafi–Shafi'i Dispute
Ruling on kissing with conditional permissibility and dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on kissing while fasting, identify the condition that changes the ruling, and contrast it with the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
Kissing does not break the fast itself, but its consequence can — so the ruling depends on whether one is safe from arousal.

This passage from al-Hidayah addresses a practical issue: may a fasting person kiss his spouse? The Hanafi school gives a conditional answer based on self-control, while Imam al-Shafi'i holds it absolutely permissible. Understanding this debate reveals how Hanafi fiqh considers consequences ('āqibat) in determining rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the condition
The act is kissing while fasting. The condition is whether the person feels safe from arousal or ejaculation.
Safety here means confidence that kissing will not lead to intercourse or ejaculation.
2
State the two rulings
If safe, kissing is permissible (mubah/la ba'sa). If not safe, it is disliked (makruh).
3
Understand the reasoning
The essence of kissing is not a nullifier of the fast. However, its potential consequence (arousal leading to nullification) is considered. Hence the ruling depends on the expected outcome.
This is an application of the Hanafi usul principle: al-‘ibratu li al-‘āqibah (consideration of consequences).
4
Examine the intra-Hanafi variant
Imam Muhammad holds that direct intimate touching (mubāsharah fāḥishah) is always disliked because it rarely escapes temptation.
Zahir al-riwayah equates such touching with kissing.
5
Analyze the dispute with Shafi'i
Imam al-Shafi'i permits kissing absolutely in both cases. The Hanafi response is that the consequence must be considered to avoid potential invalidation.
The practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) is that Hanafis require caution, while Shafi'is allow more leniency.

Source Text

نفس پر اطمینان ہو تو بوسہ لینے کی گنجائش ہے اور اطمینان نہ ہو تو مکروہ ہے
وَلَا بَأْسَ بِالْقُبْلَةِ إِذَا أَمِنَ عَلَى نَفْسِهِ أَى الْجِمَاعِ أو الإنزال وَيُكْرَهُ إِذَا لَمْ يَأْمَنُ لِأَنَّ عَيْنَهُ لَيْسَ بِفِطْرٍ وَرُبَمَا يَصِيرُ ـطرًا بِعَاقِبَتِهِ فَإِنْ أمِنَ أَعْتَبرَ عَيْنَهُ وَ أبِيحَ لَهُ وَإِنْ لَمْ يَأْمَنُ تُعْتَبَرُ عَاقِبَتُهُ وَكُرِهَ لَهُ وَالشَّافِعِيُّ أَطْلَقَ فِيهِ فِي الْحَالَيْنِ وَالْحُجَّةُ عَلَيْهِ مَا ذَكَرَنَا وَالْمُبَاشَرَةُ الْفَاحِشَةُ مِثْلُ التَّقْبِيلِ فِى ظَاهِرِ الرّوَايَةِ وَعَنْ مُحَمَّدٍ أَنَّهُ كُرِهَ الْمُبَاشَرَةُ الْفَاحِشَةُ لِأَنَّهُ قَالَ مَا تَخلُو عَنِ الْفِتْنَةِ
ترجمہ اور بوسہ لینے میں کوئی مضائقہ نہیں جبکہ اپنے نفس پر امن ہو یعنی جماع یا انزال سے اور اگر امن نہ ہو تو مکروہ ہے۔ کیونکہ بوسہ لینا بذات خود مفطر نہیں ہے اور بسا اوقات اپنے انجام کے اعتبار سے معطر ہو جاتا ہے پس اگر روزہ دار مطمئن ہو تو عین بوسہ کا اعتبار ہوگا اور وہ صائم کے لئے مباح ہوگا اور اگر مطمئن نہ ہو تو اس کے انجام کا اعتبار ہوگا اور صائم کے لئے اس کو مباح قرار نہ دیا جائے گا اور امام شافعی نے دونوں حالتوں میں جواز کو مطلق رکھا ہے اور امام شافعی کے خلاف حجت وہ دلیل ہے جو ہم نے ذکر کی ہے اور مباشرت فاحشہ ظاہر الروایہ میں بوسہ لینے کے مانند ہے اور امام محمد سے مروی ہے کہ مباشرت فاحشہ مکروہ ہے کیونکہ مباشرت فاحشہ فتنہ سے بہت کم خالی ہوتی ہے۔
تشریح مسئله روز و دار اگر اپنے نفس پر اطمینان رکھتا ہوتو اس کو اپنی بیوی کا بوسہ لینے میں کوئی مضائقہ نہیں ہے یعنی جماع کے اندر واقع ہونے سے اطمینان ہو اور خروج منی سے اطمینان ہو تو روزے کی حالت میں بوسہ لینے میں کوئی مضائقہ نہیں ہے اور اگر اطمینان نہ ہو بلکہ جماع میں مبتلا ہونے کا اندیشہ ہو یا خروج منی کا اندیشہ ہو تو ایسی صورت میں روزہ دار کے لئے بوسہ لینا مکروہ ہے کیونکہ بوسہ لینا بذات خود تو روزہ فاسد نہیں کرتا لیکن بسا اوقات انجام کے اعتبار سے فساد صوم کا سبب بن جاتا ہے بایں طور کہ روزہ دار نے اپنی بیوی کا بوسہ لیا اور تاب نہ لا کر صحبت کر بیٹھایا اس قدر مشتعل ہوا کہ بوسہ لیتے لیتے انزال ہو گیا تو ان دونوں صورتوں میں روزہ فاسد ہو جائے گا پس اگر روزہ دار اس بات پر مطمئن ہو کہ انجام بد کی نوبت نہیں آئے گی تو عین بوسہ کا اعتبار کر کے بوسہ کی اجازت دیدی جائے گی اور اگر یہ اطمینان نہ ہو تو انجام کا اعتبار کر کے مکروہ قرار دیا جائے گا۔ بہر حال ثابت ہو گیا کہ بحالت امن روزہ دار کے لئے بوسہ لینا بلا کراہت جائز ہے۔
The chapter: If one has confidence in himself, then kissing is permissible; if not confident, it is disliked. And there is no harm in kissing when one feels safe from himself, i.e., from intercourse or ejaculation. And it is disliked when one does not feel safe, because its essence is not a breaker, but sometimes it becomes a breaker by its consequence. So if he is safe, its essence is considered and it is permitted for him. If he is not safe, its consequence is considered and it is disliked for him. And al-Shafi'i allowed it absolutely in both cases. The proof against him is what we have mentioned. And direct intimate touching (mubasharah fahishah) is like kissing in the apparent transmission (zahir al-riwayah). And from Muhammad that he disliked direct intimate touching, because he said it rarely remains free from temptation. Translation: And there is no harm in kissing when one is secure about himself, i.e., from intercourse or ejaculation. If not secure, it is disliked, because kissing in itself is not a nullifier, but sometimes it becomes a nullifier by its consequence. So if the fasting person is confident, the essence of kissing is considered and it is permissible for him. If not confident, its consequence is considered and it is not declared permissible for him. And Imam Shafi'i allowed it absolutely in both states. The proof against Imam Shafi'i is the argument we have mentioned. And direct intimate touching is like kissing in the manifest narration (zahir al-riwayah). And from Imam Muhammad that he disliked direct intimate touching, because it rarely remains free from temptation. Commentary: The issue: A fasting person, if he has confidence in himself, then there is no harm in kissing his wife, i.e., confidence that he will not fall into intercourse and that semen will not come out. If he is not confident, but fears falling into intercourse or ejaculation, then in that case kissing is disliked for the fasting person, because kissing in itself does not invalidate the fast, but sometimes it becomes a cause of invalidation due to its consequence. That is, the fasting person kissed his wife and could not restrain himself and copulated, or became so aroused that he ejaculated while kissing. In both cases, the fast would be invalidated. So if the fasting person is confident that the bad outcome will not occur, then the essence of kissing is considered and permission is given. If he does not have confidence, then the consequence is considered and it is declared disliked. In any case, it is established that in a state of security, kissing is permissible without dislike.
Source pages p. 211

Commentary
This passage refines the ruling on kissing based on the individual's self-control. If a fasting person is confident that kissing will not lead to arousal or ejaculation, it is permissible (la ba'sa). If he is not confident, it is disliked (makruh). The reasoning is that the act of kissing itself is not a nullifier, but its potential consequence (ejaculation or intercourse) would invalidate the fast. So the ruling depends on the expected outcome. The author then contrasts with Imam al-Shafi'i, who holds that kissing is absolutely permissible in both cases. The Hanafi position is that considering the consequence is necessary. Additionally, the text mentions that according to the explicit transmission of the school (zahir al-riwaya), direct intimate touching (mubasharah fahishah) is treated like kissing. However, there is a narration from Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani that such touching is disliked because it rarely escapes temptation.

Key Terms
مباشرت فاحشۃ (mubāsharah fāḥishah): Direct intimate touching, such as skin-to-skin contact with desire.
عاقبت (āqibat): Consequence or end result of an action.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when is kissing permissible for a fasting person?
A) Anytime
B) Only if one is certain it will not lead to ejaculation
C) Only at night
D) Never

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling on kissing while fasting depends on the expected consequence, not merely the act itself.

Sawm — Fasting
intermediate
8 min
The Ruling on Kissing While Fasting – Condition of Security
Ruling on kissing with and without security

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on kissing during fasting, identify the condition of security (amn), and distinguish the Hanafi position from the Shafi'i absolute permissibility.

Core Idea
Kissing is permissible if secure from arousal; otherwise makruh – actions judged by their consequences.

This passage clarifies when a fasting person may kiss their spouse. While the act itself does not break the fast, its potential consequence may. The Hanafi school distinguishes based on security from arousal or ejaculation, drawing from prophetic practice and differentiating between the old and the young.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling on kissing
The matn states: 'There is no harm in kissing if one is secure from himself (i.e., from intercourse or ejaculation); it is disliked if not secure.' Identify the two scenarios.
Security (amn) is the condition.
2
Identify the basis of the ruling
The act itself does not break the fast (laysa bi-fitri), but it may become a breaker in its consequence. The ruling focuses on the outcome.
Consequence (aqibah) is key.
3
Examine the dalil
Use the hadith from Sahihain (the Prophet kissed while fasting) and Abu Dawud (distinction between old and young) to understand the permissibility with condition.
The dalil supports the condition of security.
4
Note the Shafi'i opposition
Imam al-Shafi'i permits kissing absolutely in both states. The Hanafi proof against him is the potential fitnah, as shown in the hadith.
The thamarah al-khilaf: young people should avoid kissing.

تشریح اگر روزہ دار نے عورت کا بوسہ لیا یا اس کو مس کیا اور انزال ہو گیا تو اس کا روزہ فاسد ہو گیا اب اس پر اس روزہ کی قضاء واجب ہوگی کفارہ واجب نہ ہو گا قضاء تو اس لئے واجب ہے کہ جماع صورۃ اگر چہ نہیں پایا گیا کیونکہ عورت ومرد شہوت کے ساتھ چمٹ گئے اور انزال ہو گیا اس کو معنی جماع کہتے ہیں اور احتیا طاقضا واجب کرنے کے لئے منافی صوم کا پایا جانا کافی ہے خواہ صورۃ پایا جائے خواہ معنی پایا جائے اور رہا کفارہ کا واجب نہ ہونا تو اس کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ کفارہ اس وقت واجب ہوتا ہے جبکہ جرم مکمل طور پر تی متحقق ہو اور یہاں صورۃ جماع نہ پائے جانے کی وجہ سے جرم ہلکا ہو گیا بلکہ ایک گونہ عدم جماع کا شبہ پیدا ہو گیا اور یہ بات مسلم ہے کہ شبہات کی وجہ سے کفارات دور کر دیے جاتے ہیں جیسے کہ شبہات کی وجہ سے حدود دور کر دی جاتی ہے۔
نفس پر اطمینان ہو تو بوسہ لینے کی گنجائش ہے اور اطمینان نہ ہو تو مکروہ ہے
وَلَا بَأْسَ بِالْقُبْلَةِ إِذَا أَمِنَ عَلَى نَفْسِهِ أَى الْجِمَاعِ أو الإنزال وَيُكْرَهُ إِذَا لَمْ يَأْمَنُ لِأَنَّ عَيْنَهُ لَيْسَ بِفِطْرٍ وَرُبَمَا يَصِيرُ ـطرًا بِعَاقِبَتِهِ فَإِنْ أمِنَ أَعْتَبرَ عَيْنُهُ وَ أبِيحَ لَهُ وَإِنْ لَمْ يَأْمَنُ تُعْتَبَرُ عَاقِبَتُهُ وَكُرِهَ لَهُ وَالشَّافِعِيُّ أَطْلَقَ فِيهِ فِي الْحَالَيْنِ وَالْحُجَّةُ عَلَيْهِ مَا ذَكَرَنَا وَالْمُبَاشَرَةُ الْفَاحِشَةُ مِثْلُ التَّقْبِيلِ فِى ظَاهِرِ الرّوَايَةِ وَعَنْ مُحَمَّدٍ أَنَّهُ كُرِهَ الْمُبَاشَرَةُ الْفَاحِشَةُ لِأَنَّهُ قَالَ مَا تَخلُو عَنِ الْفِتْنَةِ
ترجمہ اور بوسہ لینے میں کوئی مضائقہ نہیں جبکہ اپنے نفس پر امن ہو یعنی جماع یا انزال سے اور اگر امن نہ ہو تو مکروہ ہے۔ کیونکہ بوسہ لینا بذات خود مفطر نہیں ہے اور بسا اوقات اپنے انجام کے اعتبار سے معطر ہو جاتا ہے پس اگر روزہ دار مطمئن ہو تو عین بوسہ کا اعتبار ہوگا اور وہ صائم کے لئے مباح ہوگا اور اگر مطمئن نہ ہو تو اس کے انجام کا اعتبار ہوگا اور صائم کے لئے اس کو مباح قرار نہ دیا جائے گا اور امام شافعی نے دونوں حالتوں میں جواز کو مطلق رکھا ہے اور امام شافعی کے خلاف حجت وہ دلیل ہے جو ہم نے ذکر کی ہے اور مباشرت فاحشہ ظاہر الروایہ میں بوسہ لینے کے مانند ہے اور امام محمد سے مروی ہے کہ مباشرت فاحشہ مکروہ ہے کیونکہ مباشرت فاحشہ فتنہ سے بہت کم خالی ہوتی
