تشریح مسئله روز و دار اگر اپنے نفس پر اطمینان رکھتا ہوتو اس کو اپنی بیوی کا بوسہ لینے میں کوئی مضائقہ نہیں ہے یعنی جماع کے اندر واقع ہونے سے اطمینان ہو اور خروج منی سے اطمینان ہو تو روزے کی حالت میں بوسہ لینے میں کوئی مضائقہ نہیں ہے اور اگر اطمینان نہ ہو بلکہ جماع میں مبتلا ہونے کا اندیشہ ہو یا خروج منی کا اندیشہ ہو تو ایسی صورت میں روزہ دار کے لئے بوسہ لینا مکروہ ہے کیونکہ بوسہ لینا بذات خود تو روزہ فاسد نہیں کرتا لیکن بسا اوقات انجام کے اعتبار سے فساد صوم کا سبب بن جاتا ہے بایں طور کہ روزہ دار نے اپنی بیوی کا بوسہ لیا اور تاب نہ لا کر صحبت کر بیٹھایا اس قدر مشتعل ہوا کہ بوسہ لیتے لیتے انزال ہو گیا تو ان دونوں صورتوں میں روزہ فاسد ہو جائے گا پس اگر روزہ دار اس بات پر مطمئن ہو کہ انجام بد کی نوبت نہیں آئے گی تو عین بوسہ کا اعتبار کر کے بوسہ کی اجازت دیدی جائے گی اور اگر یہ اطمینان نہ ہو تو انجام کا اعتبار کر کے مکروہ قرار دیا جائے گا۔ بہر حال ثابت ہو گیا کہ بحالت امن روزہ دار کے لئے بوسہ لینا بلا کراہت جائز ہے۔ صحیحین میں بے أَنَّهُ عَلَيْهِ الصَّلَوةُ وَالسَّلَامُ كَانَ يُقَبِّلُ وَيُبَاشِرُ وَ هُوَ صَائِم یعنی رسول خدا صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم بحالت روزہ بیوی کا بوسہ لے لیا کرتے تھے اور با ہم چمٹ جاتے تھے اور حضرت ام سلمہ سے مروی ہے اُنَّہ عَلَيْهِ الصَّلوةَ وَالسَّلَامُ كَانَ يُقبلُهَا وَهُوَ صَائِم ام سلمى فرماتی ہیں کہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم ان کا بوسہ بحالت صوم لے لیا کرتے تھے ان دونوں روایتوں سے بھی روزہ دار کے لئے بوسہ لینے کی اجازت معلوم ہوتی ہے۔ حضرت امام شافعی نے امن اور غیر امن دونوں حالتوں میں بوسہ کو بلا کراہت جائز قرار دیا ہے لیکن ہماری طرف سے بیان کردہ دلیل امام شافعی کے خلاف حجت ہو گی۔ مباشرت فاحشہ یہ ہے کہ عورت و مرد دونوں ننگے ہو کر اپنی شرمگاہوں کو اوپر اوپر سے ملا دیں ادخال نہ کریں بہر حال ظاہر الروایہ کے مطابق مباشرت فاحشہ، بوسہ لینے کے مانند ہے یعنی اگر مباشرت فاحشہ کرنے کے باوجود اپنے نفس پر اطمینان ہو تو بلا کراہت جائز ہے اور اگر اطمینان نہ ہو تو مکروہ ہے اس کی تائید ابو داؤد کی اس روایت سے بھی ہوتی ہے عن أبي هُرَيْرَةَ رَضِيَ الله تَعَالَى عَنْهُ أَنَّهُ عَلَيْهِ الصَّلوةُ وَالسَّلام سَأَلَهُ رَجُلٌ عَنِ الْمُبَاشَرَةِ لِلصَّائِمِ فَرَحْضَ لَهُ وَأَنَاهُ أَخَرُ فَنَهَاهُ فَإِذَا الَّذِى رَحْصَ لَهُ شَيْحٌ وَالَّذِى نَهَاهُ شاب ، یعنی ایک آدمی نے روزہ دار کے لئے مباشرت کی بابت پوچھا تو آپ نے اس کو اجازت دیدی اور دوسرا آدمی آپ کے پاس آیا تو اس کو منع کر دیا پس جس کو اجازت دی تھی وہ بوڑھا آدمی تھا اور جس کو منع کیا تھا وہ جو ان آدمی تھا ۔ ملاحظہ فرمائیے کہ اس حدیث میں وجی تفصیل مذکور ہے جس کو ہم نے اعتبار کیا ہے اور امام محمد نے روزے کی حالت میں مباشرت فاحشہ کو مطلقا مکروہ قرار دیا ہے کیونکہ اس کا امکان بہت کم ہے کہ آگ پھونس مل جائیں اور آگ نہ لگے یعنی عورت و مرد مادر زاد ننگے ہو کر دونوں چمٹ جائیں اور آگے کچھ نہ ہو یہ کیسے ہو سکتا ہے اس لئے خیریت اسی میں ہے کہ مباشرت فاحشہ کا ارتکاب نہ کرے اس وجہ سے حضرت امام محمد نے روزے کی حالت میں اس کو علی الاطلاق مکر وہ لکھا ہے۔
Explanation: If a fasting person kissed a woman or touched her and had ejaculation, his fast is invalidated. He must make up (qada') that day, but no expiation (kaffarah) is due. Qada' is due because although actual intercourse did not occur, the man and woman came together with desire and ejaculation occurred, which is considered 'intercourse in meaning' (ma'na al-jima'). And for the obligation of qada', the existence of something contrary to the fast (munafi al-sawm) is sufficient, whether in form or meaning. As for kaffarah not being due, that is because kaffarah is only due when the violation is complete, but here due to the absence of actual intercourse the violation is lightened, and there is a shade of doubt about the absence of intercourse. It is established that kaffarah are repelled by doubts, just as hadd punishments are repelled by doubts. If one is secure about himself, kissing is permissible; if not secure, it is makruh. There is no harm in kissing when one is secure from himself, i.e., from intercourse or ejaculation, and it is disliked when not secure. Because in itself it is not a fast-breaker, but it may become a breaker in its consequence. If secure, its essence is considered and permissibility; if not secure, its consequence is considered and it is disliked. Al-Shafi'i made it absolutely permissible in both states; the proof against him is what we mentioned. Excessive direct contact (al-mubasharah al-fahishah) is like kissing in the apparent riwayah. From Muhammad (ibn al-Hasan) it is narrated that he disliked excessive direct contact because he said it is rarely free from fitnah. Translation of the Arabic: And there is no harm in kissing when one is secure from himself, i.e., from intercourse or ejaculation. It is disliked when not secure. Because in itself it is not a fast-breaker, but sometimes it becomes a breaker in its consequence. So if he is secure, its essence is considered and it is made permissible for him; if not secure, its consequence is considered and it is disliked for him. Al-Shafi'i made it absolute in both cases; the proof against him is what we mentioned. Excessive direct contact is like kissing in the apparent riwayah; from Muhammad he disliked excessive direct contact because he said it is rarely free from fitnah. Then the Urdu commentary continues explaining the ruling, the hadith evidence from Sahihain, Umm Salama, and Abu Dawud, and the difference with Muhammad regarding absolute dislike of direct contact.
Source pages p. 211

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute and ruling explanation. It begins by discussing the ruling on a fasting person who kisses or touches his wife and experiences ejaculation. Such an act invalidates the fast, requiring only qada' (make-up), not kaffarah (expiation). The author explains that qada' is required because the act achieved the 'meaning' of intercourse, even if not the form. Kaffarah is waived because the violation is incomplete due to doubt, following the principle that penalties are repelled by doubts. The passage then addresses the ruling on kissing alone (without ejaculation). The matn states: 'There is no harm in kissing when one is secure from himself (from intercourse or ejaculation), and it is disliked when not secure.' The reasoning is that the act itself does not break the fast, but its potential consequence might. Thus, if secure, the essence is considered and it is permissible; if not, the consequence is considered and it is makruh. The text then notes that Imam al-Shafi'i permits kissing absolutely in both states. The Hanafi proof against him is what was stated. Next, the passage discusses 'excessive direct contact' (mubasharah fahishah), defined as a naked man and woman rubbing their private parts together without insertion. According to Zahir al-Riwayah, this ruling is like kissing: permissible if secure, makruh otherwise. Imam Muhammad, however, holds it absolutely makruh because such contact is rarely free from fitnah. The commentary supports the Zahir al-Riwayah view with hadith from Abu Dawud where the Prophet differentiated between an old man (permitted) and a young man (disallowed). Thus, the Hanafi position is that the ruling depends on security from arousal.

Key Terms
قُبْلَة (qubla): Kissing, specifically of one's spouse during fasting.
أَمْن (amn): Security or assurance from falling into intercourse or ejaculation.
فِطْر (fir): Breaking the fast; anything that invalidates sawm.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi madhhab (Zahir al-Riwayah), when is it permissible for a fasting person to kiss his wife?
A) Always, regardless of security
B) Only if he is secure from arousal or ejaculation
C) Only if he is not secure from arousal
D) Never, it is always disliked

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, kissing during fasting is permissible only when one is secure from arousal or ejaculation; otherwise it is makruh.

Sawm — Fasting
intermediate
10 min
Direct Contact (Mubasharah Fahishah) – Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf
Ruling on direct contact and intra-Hanafi difference

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the ruling on excessive direct contact during fasting according to Zahir al-Riwayah, compare it with Imam Muhammad's view, and apply the hadith of Abu Dawud.

Core Idea
Direct contact is like kissing in ruling per Zahir al-Riwayah, but Imam Muhammad deems it absolutely makruh due to inevitable fitnah.

Excessive direct contact (mubasharah fahishah) refers to naked skin-to-skin contact of private parts without insertion. The Hanafi school has an internal difference: the relied-upon Zahir al-Riwayah equates it to kissing, while Imam Muhammad holds it absolutely disliked. This lesson unpacks the evidence and the practical application.

Guided Path
1
Define mubasharah fahishah
Understand the term: it means a man and woman bringing their private parts together without penetration.
It is a form of intimate contact short of intercourse.
2
State the Zahir al-Riwayah ruling
According to the apparent riwayah, the ruling is exactly like kissing: permissible if secure, makruh otherwise.
This is the mufta bihi position.
3
State Imam Muhammad's position
Imam Muhammad holds it absolutely makruh because such contact is rarely free from fitnah (temptation).
His view is based on caution.
4
Examine the evidence
The hadith of Abu Dawud where the Prophet allowed an old man but forbade a young man supports the Zahir al-Riwayah view, differentiating by security.
This hadith is used to prefer the conditional view.
5
Apply the ruling in practice
A fasting person should assess their own state; if young and easily aroused, they should avoid direct contact. For the elderly, it may be permissible.
The thamarah al-khilaf is clear in this differentiation.

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute and ruling explanation. It begins by discussing the ruling on a fasting person who kisses or touches his wife and experiences ejaculation. Such an act invalidates the fast, requiring only qada' (make-up), not kaffarah (expiation). The author explains that qada' is required because the act achieved the 'meaning' of intercourse, even if not the form. Kaffarah is waived because the violation is incomplete due to doubt, following the principle that penalties are repelled by doubts. The passage then addresses the ruling on kissing alone (without ejaculation). The matn states: 'There is no harm in kissing when one is secure from himself (from intercourse or ejaculation), and it is disliked when not secure.' The reasoning is that the act itself does not break the fast, but its potential consequence might. Thus, if secure, the essence is considered and it is permissible; if not, the consequence is considered and it is makruh. The text then notes that Imam al-Shafi'i permits kissing absolutely in both states. The Hanafi proof against him is what was stated. Next, the passage discusses 'excessive direct contact' (mubasharah fahishah), defined as a naked man and woman rubbing their private parts together without insertion. According to Zahir al-Riwayah, this ruling is like kissing: permissible if secure, makruh otherwise. Imam Muhammad, however, holds it absolutely makruh because such contact is rarely free from fitnah. The commentary supports the Zahir al-Riwayah view with hadith from Abu Dawud where the Prophet differentiated between an old man (permitted) and a young man (disallowed). Thus, the Hanafi position is that the ruling depends on security from arousal.

Key Terms
مُبَاشَرَة فَاحِشَة (mubāsharah fāḥishah): Direct skin-to-skin contact of private parts without insertion, between a man and woman.
فِتْنَة (fitnah): Temptation, especially leading to sexual arousal or sin.
ظَاهِر الرِّوَايَة (ẓāhir al-riwāyah): The apparent/established narration, representing the authoritative position of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani on most issues.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Absolutely makruh
B) Like kissing: permissible if secure, else makruh
C) Always permissible
D) Invalidates the fast in all cases

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school relies on the conditional view for direct contact (like kissing), while Imam Muhammad's absolute dislike offers a more cautious alternative.

Sawm — Fasting
beginner

Ruling on a Fly Entering the Throat While Fasting
Explaining the ruling when a fly enters the throat, contrasting qiyas and istihsan.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a fly enters the throat while fasting, and explain the role of istihsan in overriding qiyas.

Core Idea
A fly entering the throat involuntarily does not break the fast because it is unavoidable, ruled by istihsan not qiyas.

This passage from al-Hidayah addresses a common concern: does an unintentional fly break the fast? The Hanafi school uses istihsan (juristic preference) to override the apparent qiyas, analogizing the fly to dust and smoke. Let's examine the reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is a fly entering the throat of a fasting person who is mindful of his fast. The ruling is that the fast is not broken (istihsan).
Note that the ruling is conditional on the fly being unavoidable.
2
Understand the qiyas argument
By strict qiyas, any substance reaching the stomach breaks the fast, even if not nutritious (like dust). So a fly would break the fast.
Qiyas here is overridden.
3
Understand the istihsan argument
Istihsan sets aside qiyas because a fly cannot be easily avoided, similar to dust and smoke which also do not break the fast.
The effective cause (illa) is the impossibility of avoidance.
4
Compare with rain and snow
Rain and snow break the fast because they can be avoided by taking shelter.
This shows the importance of the ability to avoid.
5
Apply to similar cases
Any unavoidable substance (e.g., dust, smoke, involuntary insect) does not break the fast, while avoidable ones do.
This principle can be extended.

A fly entering the throat does not break the fast. And if a fly entered his throat while he is mindful of his fast, he does not break his fast. By qiyas, it would invalidate his fast because a fast-breaker reached his belly, even though it is not nutritious, like dust and gravel. The basis of istihsan is that it cannot be avoided, so it resembles dust and smoke. They differed concerning rain and snow; the most correct is that it invalidates because it can be avoided if he takes shelter in a tent or roof. By qiyas, his fast would be invalidated because a fast-breaker reached his belly, even though nourishment is not obtained from it, like dirt and pebbles. The reason for istihsan is that it cannot be avoided, so it becomes similar to dust and smoke. The scholars differed regarding rain and snow; the most correct is that it invalidates because it can be avoided when the fasting person has a tent or roof. Explanation: The issue is that if a fly enters the throat involuntarily and reaches the stomach while remembering the fast, then by istihsan his fast is not invalidated, but by qiyas it would be. The reason for qiyas is that a fast-breaking thing entered the stomach even if it does not provide nutrition. The reason for istihsan is that a fly cannot be avoided; rather, sometimes a fly enters the mouth involuntarily and reaches the belly. So the fly resembles dust and smoke, and if dust and smoke enter involuntarily, the fast is not broken. Therefore, in the case of a fly entering the belly involuntarily, the fast is also not broken. Source pages p. 212

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof, demonstrating the use of istihsan (juristic preference) to override qiyas (analogy). The issue: if a fasting person, mindful of his fast, has a fly enter his throat and reach his stomach. By strict qiyas (analogy), this would break the fast because any substance entering the body is a fast-breaker, even if not nutritious (like dust or gravel). However, the Hanafi school applies istihsan, reasoning that one cannot easily avoid a fly, similar to dust and smoke which also do not break the fast when ingested unintentionally. Thus, the fast remains valid. The passage also addresses rain and snow: if they enter the mouth, the more sound opinion is that they break the fast because they can be avoided by shelter. The commentary explains the reasoning and extends the analogy to dust and smoke.

Key Terms
ذُبَاب (dhubāb): A fly, specifically one that enters the throat unintentionally.
استحسان (istiḥsān): Juristic preference, setting aside qiyas for a more suitable ruling based on ease or necessity.
قياس (qiyās): Analogical reasoning: applying the ruling of a known case (asl) to a new case (far') due to shared effective cause (illa).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
An unavoidable substance like a fly does not break the fast, but a avoidable one like rain does.

Kissing and Mubasharat During Fasting: A Hanafi Inter-Madhhab Analysis
Ruling on kissing and direct contact for a fasting person with inter-madhhab disputes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on kissing and mubasharat fahishah for a fasting person, explain the basis of tafsil (conditional permissibility based on self-control), and compare it with the Shafi'i and Imam Muhammad's views.

Core Idea
The Hanafi ruling on physical intimacy during fasting depends on self-control, not blanket permission or prohibition.

The question of whether a fasting person can kiss or engage in direct contact (mubasharat) has been debated among scholars. This passage from al-Hidayah presents the Hanafi position with its proof, contrasting it with the views of Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Muhammad. By studying the detailed reasoning, you will understand how the Hanafi school uses textual evidence and practical caution to derive a nuanced ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi position
State the Hanafi school's ruling on kissing and mubasharat fahishah for a fasting person: both are permissible without dislike if one is confident of controlling sexual desires; otherwise, they are makruh.
This is the mufta bihi position from Zahir al-Riwayah, as stated in the text.
2
Identify the opposing views
Note that Imam al-Shafi'i holds kissing absolutely permissible without dislike. Imam Muhammad holds mubasharat fahishah absolutely makruh.
These are the two main opposing positions addressed in the passage.
3
Analyze the Hanafi evidence
The Hanafi school relies on the hadith of Abu Hurairah where the Prophet differentiated between an old man (permitted) and a young man (forbidden), indicating the ruling depends on the ability to control desires.
This hadith (Sunan Abi Dawud) is a key proof; the Hanafis argue it cannot be overridden by general permission.
4
Examine the responses to opponents
The Hanafi response to Imam al-Shafi'i: the tafsil (detail) in the hadith of Abu Hurairah shows that absolute permission is not intended. To Imam Muhammad: the absolute dislike is a precaution not required by the primary evidence.
Imam Muhammad's view is considered a minority position (nawadir) while the Zahir al-Riwayah view is the school's relied-upon position.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practically, a Hanafi may kiss or engage in mubasharat if confident of control; a Shafi'i may do so absolutely; a follower of Imam Muhammad would avoid it completely.
This difference in practical fatwa reflects the different weights given to evidence and precaution.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كرتے تھے اور باہم چمٹ جاتے تھے اور حضرت ام سلمہ سے مروی ہے أَنَّهُ عَلَيْهِ الصَّلَاةُ وَالسَّلَامُ كَانَ يُقَبِّلُهَا وَهُوَ صَائِمٌ۔ ام سلمیٰ فرماتی ہیں کہ رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم ان کا بوسہ بحالت صوم لے لیا کرتے تھے۔ ان دونوں روایتوں سے بھی روزہ دار کے لیے بوسہ لینے کی اجازت معلوم ہوتی ہے۔ حضرت امام شافعی نے امن اور غیر امن دونوں حالتوں میں بوسہ کو بلا کراہت جائز قرار دیا ہے لیکن ہماری طرف سے بیان کردہ دلیل امام شافعی کے خلاف حجت ہو گی۔ مباشرت فاحشہ یہ ہے کہ عورت و مرد دونوں ننگے ہو کر اپنی شرمگاہوں کو اوپر اوپر سے ملا دیں ادخال نہ کریں۔ بہرحال ظاہر الروایہ کے مطابق مباشرت فاحشہ، بوسہ لینے کے مانند ہے یعنی اگر مباشرت فاحشہ کرنے کے باوجود اپنے نفس پر اطمینان ہو تو بلا کراہت جائز ہے اور اگر اطمینان نہ ہو تو مکروہ ہے۔ اس کی تائید ابو داؤد کی اس روایت سے بھی ہوتی ہے عن أبي هريرة رضي الله تعالى عنه أنَّهُ عَلَيْهِ الصَّلَاةُ وَالسَّلَامُ سَأَلَهُ رَجُلٌ عَنِ الْمُبَاشَرَةِ لِلصَّائِمِ فَرَخَّصَ لَهُ وَأَنَاهُ آخَرُ فَنَهَاهُ فَإِذَا الَّذِي رَخَّصَ لَهُ شَيْخٌ وَالَّذِي نَهَاهُ شَابٌّ، یعنی ایک آدمی نے روزہ دار کے لیے مباشرت کی بابت پوچھا تو آپ نے اس کو اجازت دے دی اور دوسرا آدمی آپ کے پاس آیا تو اس کو منع کر دیا۔ پس جس کو اجازت دی تھی وہ بوڑھا آدمی تھا اور جس کو منع کیا تھا وہ جوان آدمی تھا۔ ملاحظہ فرمائیے کہ اس حدیث میں وہی تفصیل مذکور ہے جس کو ہم نے اعتبار کیا ہے۔ اور امام محمد نے روزے کی حالت میں مباشرت فاحشہ کو مطلقاً مکروہ قرار دیا ہے کیونکہ اس کا امکان بہت کم ہے کہ آگ پھونس مل جائیں اور آگ نہ لگے یعنی عورت و مرد مادر زاد ننگے ہو کر دونوں چمٹ جائیں اور آگے کچھ نہ ہو یہ کیسے ہو سکتا ہے اس لیے خیریت اسی میں ہے کہ مباشرت فاحشہ کا ارتکاب نہ کرے اس وجہ سے حضرت امام محمد نے روزے کی حالت میں اس کو علی الإطلاق مکروہ لکھا ہے۔
They used to do and cling to each other, and it is narrated from Umm Salama that he (peace be upon him) used to kiss her while fasting. Umm Salama says that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) would kiss her while fasting. From both these narrations, permission is known for the fasting person to kiss. Imam al-Shafi'i declared kissing permissible without dislike in both safe and unsafe states, but the evidence presented from our side will be an argument against Imam al-Shafi'i. Mubasharat fahishah is that a man and a woman both become naked and press their private parts together without penetration. In any case, according to Zahir al-Riwayah, mubasharat fahishah is like kissing: if one is confident about oneself despite doing it, it is permissible without dislike; if not confident, it is disliked. This is supported by the narration of Abu Dawud from Abu Hurairah that a man asked him about mubasharat for the fasting person, and he permitted him; another came and he forbade him; the one he permitted was an old man and the one he forbade was a young man. Note that in this hadith the same detail is mentioned which we have considered. And Imam Muhammad declared mubasharat fahishah absolutely disliked during fasting because it is very unlikely that fire and tinder meet and fire does not ignite—meaning a man and woman become completely naked and cling together and nothing further happens; how can that be? Therefore, it is better not to commit mubasharat fahishah; for this reason Imam Muhammad wrote it as absolutely disliked during fasting.
Source pages p. 212

Commentary
This passage discusses the rulings on kissing and mubasharat (direct contact without penetration) for a fasting person. It begins with evidence from hadiths showing that the Prophet himself kissed while fasting, establishing permissibility. The Hanafi position, according to Zahir al-Riwayah, distinguishes based on one's control over desires: if a person is confident they will not be aroused to the point of ejaculation or invalidating the fast, both kissing and mubasharat are permissible without dislike; otherwise they are makruh. Imam al-Shafi'i holds that kissing is absolutely permissible without any dislike, but the Hanafis argue against him using the same hadiths that show the Prophet differentiated based on age (old vs. young). Imam Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani takes a stricter view, ruling mubasharat fahishah as absolutely makruh because of the high risk of temptation. The passage thus presents the three positions within the Hanafi school and the Shafi'i opposition, with the relied-upon position (Zahir al-Riwayah) being tafsil (detail).

Key Terms
مُبَاشَرَة فَاحِشَة (mubāsharat fāḥishah): Direct contact of the private parts without penetration, while both are naked.
ظَاهِر الرِّوَايَة (Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah): The six core books of Imam Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani, forming the primary transmitted corpus of the Hanafi school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) It is absolutely forbidden.
B) It is permissible without dislike.
C) It is makruh tanzihi.
D) It is makruh tahrimi.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits kissing and mubasharat during fasting for those confident in their self-control, making the ruling conditional rather than absolute.

When a Fly Enters the Throat: Qiyas vs. Istihsan in Fasting
Ruling on unintentional fly entry in fasting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of istihsan to cases where an unavoidable substance enters the body during fasting, distinguishing it from invalidating entry by qiyas.

Core Idea
Istihsan overrides qiyas when avoidance is impossible — the fly does not break the fast.

This passage from al-Hidayah addresses a subtle yet practical issue: a fly accidentally entering the throat while fasting. The fast's validity depends on whether the entry is considered an intentional act. The Hanafi school uses istihsan (juristic preference) to set aside the apparent analogy (qiyas) that would invalidate the fast, because guarding against a fly is impossible. Understanding this ruling reveals how Hanafi usul balances textual analogy with practical necessity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The passage opens with the clear ruling: If a fly enters the throat while the fasting person is mindful of the fast, the fast is not broken. Note the condition 'while mindful' (dhakir li-sawmihi) emphasizes that the entry is unintentional.
Mindfulness implies intention; here the act is not chosen.
2
Understand the qiyas argument
The text then presents the counter-argument by qiyas: by analogy, any substance reaching the interior (jawf) should invalidate, like dust or pebbles. The 'illa (effective cause) is wusul al-mufṭir ila al-jawf (a fast-breaking thing reaching the cavity).
Qiyas khafi (hidden analogy) is at play.
3
Examine the istihsan reasoning
The basis of istihsan is that one cannot guard against (la yustaṭā'u al-iḥtirāz) the fly. Compare it to dust and smoke, which are also unavoidable and do not break the fast. The inability to avoid creates an exception.
Istihsan is a preferred ruling over qiyas due to necessity.
4
Derive the underlying principle
From this case, a principle emerges: if a substance is impossible to avoid and unintentional, it does not invalidate the fast, regardless of whether it reaches the stomach. This applies to flies, dust, smoke, etc.
The scope: only unavoidable, unintentional things.
5
Apply to similar cases
Consider other small insects or water splashes entering the mouth. If unavoidable, the fast remains valid. If someone deliberately swallows a fly (possible?), the ruling would differ.
Intentional swallowing of a fly would break the fast because it becomes chosen.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَوْ دَخَلَ حَلْقَهُ ذُبَابٌ وَهُوَ ذَاكِرٌ لِصَوْمِهِ لَمْ يُفْطِرْ وَفِي الْقِيَاسِ يُفْسِدُ صَوْمَهُ لِوُصُولِ الْمُفْطِرِ إِلَى جَوْفِهِ وَإِنْ كَانَ لَا يُتَغَذَّى بِهِ كَالْتُّرَابِ وَالْحَصَاةِ. وَجْهُ الِاسْتِحْسَانِ أَنَّهُ لَا يُسْتَطَاعُ الِاحْتِرَازُ عَنْهُ فَأَشْبَهَ الْغُبَارَ وَالدُّخَانَ۔ ترجمہ: اور اگر روزہ دار کے حلق میں مکھی گھس گئی حالانکہ اس کو اپنا روزہ یاد ہے تو روزہ افطار نہ ہوگا۔ اور قیاس یہ ہے کہ اس کا روزہ فاسد ہو جائے گا کیونکہ مفطر صوم اس کے جوف تک پہنچ گیا ہے اگرچہ اس سے غذا حاصل نہیں کی جاتی جیسے مٹی اور کنکری۔ وجہ استحسان یہ ہے کہ مکھی سے بچاؤ ممکن نہیں پس غبار اور دھویں کے مشابہ ہو گیا۔
If a fly enters his throat while he is mindful of his fast, he does not break his fast. By qiyas, his fast would be invalidated because a fast-breaking substance has reached his interior, even if it is not nourishing, like dust and pebbles. The basis of istihsan is that one cannot guard against it, so it resembles dust and smoke.
Source pages p. 212

Commentary
This passage presents a classic Hanafi usul issue: the conflict between qiyas and istihsan. By qiyas, any substance entering the body through the mouth invalidates the fast, even if it is not food, because it reaches the internal cavity (jwf). However, the Hanafi ruling based on istihsan is that the fast remains valid if entry is unintentional and unavoidable. The reason ('illa) for istihsan is that one cannot protect oneself from a fly, just as one cannot guard against dust or smoke. Since avoidance is impossible, the ruling of invalidation is lifted out of necessity. This is a ruling from Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah.

Key Terms
قِيَاس (qiyās): Analogical reasoning: comparing the fly to food/drink because it reaches the stomach.
اسْتِحْسَان (istiḥsān): Juristic preference: setting aside qiyas for a more appropriate ruling based on ease or necessity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi school rule that a fly entering the throat does not break the fast, even though it reaches the stomach?
A) Because a fly is not considered food.
B) Because the fast is only invalidated by intentional eating.
C) Because one cannot guard against it, making it like dust and smoke.
D) Because the fly is not a physical object.

Key Takeaway
The fast remains valid when an unavoidable substance like a fly enters the throat unintentionally, based on istihsan overriding qiyas.

Rain and Snow Entering the Mouth: Avoidability Invalidates the Fast
Ruling on rain and snow entering the mouth of a fasting person

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on rain and snow entering the mouth during fasting and explain the rationale of avoidability (imkan al-imtina') that distinguishes it from unavoidable substances like dust and smoke.

Core Idea
Rain and snow invalidate the fast because you can avoid them by closing your mouth or taking shelter.

The fast is broken when anything enters the stomach intentionally. But what about rain or snow that fall into the mouth unexpectedly? In this passage, the later Hanafi masters rule that such unintentional intake still invalidates the fast, unlike dust or smoke, because avoidance is possible. This ruling illustrates the principle that avoidable substances break the fast, while unavoidable ones do not.

Guided Path
1
Identify the hukm (ruling) and its authority level
The passage states that the most correct (al-asahh) view is that both rain and snow invalidate the fast. Note that this comes from later mashayikh (mutakhkhirin), not from Zahir al-Riwayah.
The phrase 'al-asahh' indicates this is the preferred ruling among later authorities.
2
Recognize the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf (disagreement)
Some early Hanafis said only rain invalidates, others only hail. The general body (ammat al-mashayikh) holds both invalidate. This ikhtilaf is a legitimate difference within the school.
The student should understand that later preference reconciled these views.
3
Understand the dalil (proof) based on avoidability
The reasoning is that one can avoid rain and snow by taking shelter under a tent or roof, or by closing the mouth. Hence they are unlike dust and smoke, which are unavoidable.
The key 'illa is imkan al-imtina' (possibility of avoidance).
4
Analyze the critique by Sahib Fath al-Qadir
Ibn al-Humam (Sahib Fath al-Qadir) objects: if a traveler has no shelter, avoidance by tent/roof is impossible, yet the fast still breaks. He proposes a more universal 'illa: closing the mouth avoids entering in all cases.
This critique shows refinement of the 'illa within the Hanafi tradition.
5
See the author's defense and final consolidation
The author argues that the original 'illa encompasses both means (shelter and mouth-closing). The intent is that avoidance is within human capacity, not that a specific means is required.
The final position remains: rain and snow invalidate.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَاخْتَلَفُوا فِي الْمَطْرِ وَالثَّلْجِ وَالْأَصَحُّ أَنَّهُ يُفْسِدُ لِإِمْكَانِ الِامْتِنَاعِ عَنْهُ إِذَا أَوَاهُ خَيْمَةٌ أَوْ سَقْفٌ۔ ترجمہ: اور مشائخ نے بارش اور برف میں اختلاف کیا ہے اور اصح یہ ہے کہ روزہ فاسد ہو جائے گا کیونکہ اس سے بچنا ممکن ہے جبکہ روزہ دار کو خیمہ یا چھت پناہ دے۔ تشریح: مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر روزہ دار کے منہ میں بارش کی بوند اور اولہ گر کر معدہ میں چلا گیا تو روزہ ٹوٹے گا یا نہیں؟ اس بارے میں مشائخ امت کا اختلاف ہے۔ چنانچہ بعض نے کہا کہ بارش کی بوندیں تو مفسد ہیں لیکن اولہ مفسد نہیں ہے اور بعض نے اس کے برعکس کہا اور عامۃ المشائخ کا قول یہ ہے کہ دونوں سے روزہ فاسد ہو جائے گا اور یہی زیادہ صحیح قول ہے۔ دلیل اس کی یہ ہے کہ بارش کی بوندوں اور آسمانی برف سے بچاؤ ممکن ہے بایں طور کہ جب بارش اور برف باری ہو تو کسی خیمہ یا چھت کے سایہ میں پناہ لے۔ پس جب ان دونوں سے بچاؤ ممکن ہے تو یہ غبار اور دھویں کے مشابہ نہ ہوئے۔ صاحب فتح القدیر نے اس علت پر اعتراض کرتے ہوئے فرمایا کہ اگر صائم مسافر ہو اور وہاں نہ کوئی خیمہ ہو اور نہ کوئی سائبان تو ایسی صورت میں چونکہ مینہ اور برف سماوی سے بچاؤ ممکن نہیں اس لیے روزہ فاسد نہ ہونا چاہیے حالانکہ روزہ اس صورت میں بھی فاسد ہو جاتا ہے۔ صاحب فتح القدیر کہتے ہیں کہ زیادہ بہتر یہ ہے کہ علت یہ بیان کی جائے کہ منہ بند کر کے بارش کے پانی اور اولوں سے بچاؤ ممکن ہے پس یہ علت تمام صورتوں کو شامل ہو گی خواہ صائم حضر میں ہو خواہ سفر میں ہو۔ لیکن ہم کہتے ہیں کہ فاضل مصنف کا مقصد یہ ہے کہ بارش اور برف ایسی چیزیں نہیں ہیں جن سے بچنا انسان کی قدرت میں نہ ہو۔ بلکہ ان سے بچنا انسان کی وسعت میں ہے خواہ وہ منہ بند کر کے ہو خواہ خیمہ اور چھت کے سایہ میں پناہ پکڑ کر ہو۔ وَاللَّهُ أَعْلَمُ بِالصَّوَابِ۔ جمیل غفرلہ
And they differed concerning rain and snow, and the most correct is that it invalidates because it is possible to avoid it when one has a tent or roof. Commentary: The issue is whether the fast breaks if a raindrop or hail enters the mouth and reaches the stomach. The mashayikh differed: some said raindrops invalidate but not hail; others said the opposite; the majority said both invalidate, and that is the more correct view. The proof is that one can avoid rain and snow by taking shelter under a tent or roof. Since avoidance is possible, they are not like dust and smoke. Sahib Fath al-Qadir objected to this reasoning, saying if the fasting person is a traveler and has no tent or shelter, then avoidance is not possible, yet the fast still breaks. He suggested a better reason: one can avoid by closing the mouth, which applies in all cases. But we say the author's intention is that rain and snow are not things that are entirely beyond human ability to avoid; one can avoid them either by closing the mouth or by taking shelter. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 212

Commentary
This passage deals with the ruling when rain or snow enters the mouth of a fasting person. The majority of Hanafi mashayikh (later scholars) hold that it invalidates the fast, unlike dust or smoke. The key difference is that one can reasonably avoid rain and snow by taking shelter or closing the mouth. This is a ruling from later authorities (mutakhkhirin), not from Zahir al-Riwayah. There is an ikhtilaf among them, but the preferred view is that both rain and snow invalidate. Sahib Fath al-Qadir (Ibn al-Humam) critiques the reasoning based on shelter, pointing out that a traveler may have no shelter, yet the fast still breaks. He suggests a more universal 'illa: closing the mouth is always possible. The text defends the original reasoning by saying that the availability of shelter is not the only means; one can also close the mouth. The final ruling is that both invalidate.

Key Terms
مَطَر (maṭar): Rainwater that enters the mouth.
ثَلْج (thalj): Snow or hail that enters the mouth.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Because they are avoidable by closing the mouth or seeking shelter.
C) Because they are nourishing.
D) Because the Prophet specifically forbade them.

Key Takeaway
Avoidable substances like rain and snow invalidate the fast even if they enter unintentionally, unlike unavoidable substances like dust and smoke.

Eating Meat Remnants Between Teeth While Fasting: The Hanafi Quantity Distinction
Ruling on swallowing meat remnants between teeth

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi majority ruling on swallowing meat remnants during fasting and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between the majority and Imam Zufar, including the chickpea threshold.

Core Idea
A small meat remnant (less than a chickpea) is like saliva; it does not break the fast.

This lesson tackles a practical situation for a fasting person: unintentionally swallowing tiny food particles stuck between teeth. The Hanafi school distinguishes between negligible and substantial amounts, setting a clear boundary at the size of a chickpea. Imam Zufar, another Hanafi scholar, disagreed, arguing that any swallowing from the mouth breaks the fast. We will examine the evidence, understand the operative ruling, and see how this dispute applies to daily life.

Guided Path
1
State the Majority Position
Identify the Hanafi majority view (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad): swallowing a small amount (less than a chickpea) does not break the fast; swallowing a large amount (chickpea or more) breaks it.
The text says: 'If it is little, he does not break; if much, he breaks.'
2
Identify the Dissent
Recognize that Imam Zufar holds the opposite: he says the fast breaks in both cases, regardless of quantity.
Zufar's view is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
3
Analyze Zufar's Evidence
Zufar's proof: the mouth is treated like the exterior of the body (like skin), so any substance swallowed from the mouth is akin to eating external food. He supports this with the ruling that rinsing does not break the fast.
He uses qiyas: the mouth's ruling as exterior makes any swallowing count as eating.
4
Examine the Majority's Rebuttal
The majority respond that a small amount of food between teeth is akin to saliva, which naturally exists and does not break the fast. The analogy with rinsing is false because rinsing water is not swallowed. The quantity distinguishes: large amounts do not remain naturally and so invalidate.
The dividing line is the size of a chickpea; what is less is little.
5
Apply the Chickpea Threshold
In practice, measure the remnant against a chickpea. If smaller, the fast is valid; if equal or larger, the fast is broken and requires qada'.
This threshold is specific to Hanafi fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَوْ أَكَلَ لَحْمًا بَيْنَ أَسْنَانِهِ فَإِنْ كَانَ قَلِيلًا لَمْ يُفْطِرْ وَإِنْ كَانَ كَثِيرًا يُفْطِرُ وَقَالَ زُفَرُ يُفْطِرُ فِي الْوَجْهَيْنِ لِأَنَّ الْفَمَ لَهُ حُكْمُ الظَّاهِرِ حَتَّى لَا يُفْسِدُ صَوْمَهُ بِالْمَضْمَضَةِ وَلَنَا أَنَّ الْقَلِيلَ تَابِعٌ لِأَسْنَانِهِ بِمَنْزِلَةِ رِيقِهِ بِخِلَافِ الْكَثِيرِ لِأَنَّهُ لَا يَبْقَى فِيمَا بَيْنَ الْأَسْنَانِ وَالْفَاصِلُ مِقْدَارُ الْحِمَّصَةِ وَمَا دُونَهُ قَلِيلٌ۔ ترجمہ: اور اگر دانتوں کے درمیان گوشت کا ریشہ کھا گیا پس اگر وہ قلیل ہے تو روزہ فاسد نہ ہوگا اور اگر کثیر ہے تو روزہ فاسد ہو جائے گا اور امام زفر نے فرمایا ہے کہ دونوں صورتوں میں افطار ہو جائے گا کیونکہ منہ کے لیے ظاہر کا حکم ہے حتی کہ کلی کرنے سے اس کا روزہ فاسد نہیں ہوتا۔ اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ قلیل اس کے دانتوں کا تابع ہو کر اس کے تھوک کے مرتبہ میں ہے برخلاف کثیر کے کیونکہ وہ دانتوں کے درمیان باقی نہیں رہتا ہے اور حد فاصل چنے کی مقدار ہے اور جو اس سے کم ہو وہ قلیل ہے۔
If one eats meat that is between his teeth, then if it is little, he does not break his fast; if it is much, he breaks his fast. And Zufar said: he breaks his fast in both cases, because the mouth is considered like the exterior (of the body) such that his fast is not invalidated by rinsing. Our evidence is that a small amount is considered a part of his teeth, having the same ruling as his saliva, unlike a large amount because it does not remain between the teeth. The dividing line is the size of a chickpea; what is less than that is little.
Source pages p. 213

Commentary
This passage deals with the ruling when a fasting person swallows meat fibers that were stuck between his teeth. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: the majority (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) distinguish between a small amount and a large amount. A small amount (less than a chickpea) is treated like saliva, so the fast remains valid. A large amount invalidates the fast because it is considered an intentional intake of food. Imam Zufar argues that any eating from the mouth breaks the fast because the mouth's interior is treated as external (like rinsing not invalidating). He analogizes that just as rinsing does not break the fast, swallowing a meat fiber is like eating something external. The majority respond that a small amount is like saliva that accumulates, while a large amount is not remaining naturally. The relied-upon position is the majority view with the chickpea distinction.

Key Terms
قَلِيل (qalīl): Less than the size of a chickpea (hummasah).
فَاصِل (fāṣil): The dividing line between qalil and kathir: the size of a chickpea.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority Hanafi view, what is the ruling if a fasting person swallows meat remnants between his teeth that are less than the size of a chickpea?
A) The fast becomes invalid.
B) The fast remains valid.
C) It is makruh but the fast is valid.
D) It requires qada'.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes between little and much meat remnants; little (less than chickpea) does not break the fast.

Do Raindrops and Hail Break the Fast? Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on rain and hail nullifying fast

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi majority view on raindrops and hail breaking the fast, explain the evidence and its refinement, and apply the principle to new scenarios.

Core Idea
Raindrops and hail break the fast because they can be avoided – unavoidable elements do not.

This passage presents a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute about whether raindrops and hail entering the mouth nullify the fast. While some Hanafi scholars differentiated between rain and hail, the majority held that both break the fast, citing the possibility of avoidance. The author of Fath al-Qadeer critiques the initial reasoning and refines the cause, strengthening the legal proof and resolving a potential loophole.

Guided Path
1
State the majority position
Identify that the majority of mashayikh (عامتہ المشائخ) hold that both raindrops and hail break the fast, and this is the more correct view.
Minority opinions: some said only rain breaks, others only hail.
2
Examine the proof (dalil)
The proof given is qiyas: since it is possible to avoid raindrops and hail (by shelter or closing mouth), they are like food/drink – intentionally entering the stomach invalidates the fast. This distinguishes them from unavoidable dust or smoke.
The key distinction is possibility of avoidance.
3
Analyze the objection
The author of Fath al-Qadeer objects: if a traveller has no shelter, avoidance seems impossible, yet the fast still breaks. This reveals a flaw in the initial proof.
The objection challenges the universality of the cause.
4
Evaluate the refined cause
The refined cause is that closing the mouth is always possible, regardless of shelter. This covers all cases – traveller or resident – and a closing the mouth prevents entry.
The refined cause is more comprehensive and answers the objection.
5
Apply the ruling
In practice, if a raindrop or hail enters the mouth and is swallowed, the fast is invalid (fasid) and requires qada, because the fasting person could have avoided it by closing the mouth or seeking shelter.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصوم کے منہ میں بارش کی بوند اور اولہ گر کر معدہ میں چلا گیا تو روزہ ٹوٹے گا یا نہیں ؟ اس بارے میں مشائخ امت کا اختلاف ہے چنانچہ بعض نے کہا کہ بارش کی بوندیں تو مفسد ہیں لیکن اولہ مفسد نہیں ہے اور بعض نے اس کے برعکس کہا کہ اور عامتہ المشائخ کا قول یہ ہے کہ دونوں سے روزہ فاسد ہو جائے گا اور یہی زیادہ صحیح قول ہے۔ دلیل اس کی یہ ہے کہ بارش کی بوندوں اور آسمانی برف سے بچاؤ ممکن ہے بایں طور کہ جب بارش اور برف باری ہو تو کسی خیمہ یا چھت کے سایہ میں پناہ لیلے پس جب ان دونوں سے بچاؤ ممکن ہے تو یہ غبار اور دھویں کے مشابہ نہ ہوئے۔ صاحب فتح القدیر نے اس علت پر اعتراض کرتے ہوئے فرمایا کہ اگر صائم مسافر ہو اور وہاں نہ کوئی خیمہ ہو اور نہ کوئی سائبان تو ایسی صورت میں چونکہ مینہ اور برف سماوی سے بچاؤ ممکن نہیں اس لئے روزہ فاسد نہ ہونا چاہئے حالانکہ روزہ اس صورت میں بھی فاسد ہو جاتا ہے۔ صاحب مفتح القدیر کہتے ہیں کہ زیادہ بہتر یہ ہے کہ علت یہ بیان کی جائے کہ منہ بند کر کے بارش کے پانی اور اولوں سے بچاؤ ممکن ہے پس یہ علت تمام صورتوں کو شامل ہو گی خواہ صائم حضر میں ہو خواہ سفر میں ہو لیکن ہم کہتے ہیں کہ فاضل مصنف کا مقصد یہ ہے کہ بارش اور برف ایسی چیزیں نہیں ہیں جن سے بچنا انسان کی قدرت میں نہ ہو۔ بلکہ ان سے بچنا انسان کی وسعت میں ہے خواہ وہ منہ بند کر کے ہو خواہ خیمہ اور چھت کے سایہ میں پناہ پکڑ کر ہو۔ وَاللَّهُ أَعْلَمُ بِالصَّوابِ جمیل غفرلہ
About the fast: if a raindrop or hail falls into the mouth and goes down to the stomach, will the fast break or not? Regarding this, there is a difference among the mashayikh of the ummah. Some said that raindrops break the fast but hail does not. Others said the opposite. The general majority of the mashayikh hold that both break the fast, and this is the more correct view. The proof for this is that it is possible to avoid raindrops and heavenly snow (hail) by taking shelter under a tent or roof. Since it is possible to avoid both, they are not similar to dust and smoke. The author of Fath al-Qadeer objected to this reasoning, saying: if the fasting person is traveling and there is neither a tent nor an awning, then since it is not possible to avoid rain and hail, the fast should not break, yet the fast does break in this case. The author of Fath al-Qadeer says that it is better to state the cause as: it is possible to avoid raindrops and hail by closing the mouth. So this cause covers all cases, whether the fasting person is at home or traveling. But we say that the noble author's intent is that rain and snow are not things that are beyond human power to avoid. Rather, avoiding them is within human capacity, whether by closing the mouth or by taking shelter under a tent or roof. And Allah knows best. Jameel Ghufrlah.
Source pages p. 213

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the effect of raindrops and hail on the fast. The author first states the issue: if a raindrop or hail enters the mouth and reaches the stomach, does it break the fast? He then mentions the differing opinions among the mashayikh: some say only raindrops break the fast, some say only hail, but the majority (عامتہ المشائخ) hold that both break the fast, and this is the more correct view. The proof provided is that both can be avoided by taking shelter or by closing the mouth, thus they are like food or drink, unlike dust or smoke which are unavoidable. The author of Fath al-Qadeer objects that if a traveler cannot find shelter, the fast should not break according to this reasoning, yet it still does. The author of Fath al-Qadeer then refines the cause: it is possible to avoid by closing the mouth, which applies in all situations. The passage concludes by affirming the majority view that avoidance is always possible, either by shelter or by mouth closure.

Key Terms
مشائخ امت (mashayikh al-ummah): Scholars of the ummah, specifically Hanafi scholars in this context.
اولہ (al-ullah): Hailstone; heavenly snow that falls from the sky.
فتح القدیر (Fath al-Qadeer): A commentary by Ibn al-Humam (d. 861 AH) on al-Hidayah, an important Hanafi fiqh work.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Only raindrops break the fast
B) Only hailstones break the fast
C) Both break the fast
D) Neither breaks the fast

Key Takeaway
Raindrops and hail break the fast because they can be avoided, unlike unavoidable dust and smoke.

Meat Stuck Between Teeth: The Qalil vs Kathir Distinction
Ruling on swallowing meat stuck between teeth and disagreement with Imam Zufar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi distinction between qalil and kathir to determine if meat stuck between teeth breaks the fast and explain the rebuttal to Imam Zufar’s objection.

Core Idea
A little meat stuck between teeth (less than a chickpea) is like saliva and does not break the fast; a lot does.

This lesson examines a specific scenario in Hanafi fiqh: a fasting person swallows meat stuck between teeth. The majority opinion distinguishes based on quantity, while Imam Zufar holds that any amount breaks the fast. Understanding this distinction clarifies the role of unavoidability in determining the validity of the fast.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act is swallowing meat stuck between teeth. Identify the ruling for two cases: qalil (less than a chickpea) and kathir (equal or more).
Qalil: fast valid; kathir: fast invalid (fasid).
2
Understand the majority proof
The majority argue that the small amount is unavoidable and follows the teeth like saliva, thus does not break the fast. The large amount is avoidable and breaks it.
The dividing line is the chickpea (himmasah).
3
Analyze Imam Zufar’s objection
Imam Zufar holds that the mouth is like the external body; swallowing any amount from inside is like eating from outside, so even a little breaks the fast.
He analogizes to rinsing not breaking the fast, but that does not involve swallowing.
4
Evaluate the rebuttal
The majority respond that the small amount is unavoidably stuck and thus akin to saliva, not to intentional eating from outside.
This establishes the qalil/kathir distinction.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The majority position (distinguishing qalil and kathir) is the relied-upon view for fatwa.
Imam Zufar’s view is a minority within the Hanafi school.

Source Text

دانتوں میں پھنسا ہوا گوشت کھانے سے روزہ فاسد نہیں ہوتا اور اگر کثیر مقدار میں ہو تو کھانے سے روزہ فاسد ہو جائے گا .. اقوال فقہاء
وَلَوْ أَكَلَ لَحْمًا بَيْنَ أَسْنَائِهِ فَإِنْ كَانَ قَلِيلًا لَمْ يُفْطَرُ وَإِنْ كَانَ كَثِيرًا يُفْطَرُ وَقَالَ زُفُرُ يُقْطَرُ فِي الْوَجْهَيْنِ لأَنَّ الْفَمَ لَهُ الظَّاهِرِ حَتَّى لَا يُفْسِدُ صَومُهُ بِالْمَضْمَضَةِ وَلَنَا أَنَّ الْقَلِيْلَ تَابِعُ لِأسْنَانِهِ بِمَنْزِلَةِ رِيقِهِ بِخِلَافِ الْكَثِيرِ لِأَنَّهُ لَا يَقِي فِيمَا بَيْنَ الْأسْنَانِ وَالْفَاصِلُ مِقْدَارَ الْحِمَّصَةِ وَمَا دُونَها قَلِيل ترجمہ اور اگر دانتوں کے درمیان گوشت کا ریشہ کھا گیا پس اگر وہ قلیل ہے تو روزہ فاسد نہ ہوگا اور اگر کثیر ہے تو روزہ فاسد ہو جائے گا اور امام زفر نے فرمایا ہے کہ دونوں صورتوں میں افطار ہو جائے گا کیونکہ منہ کے لئے ظاہر کا حکم ہے حتی کہ کلی کرنے سے اس کا روزہ فاسد نہیں ہوتا اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ قلیل اس کے دانتوں کا تابع ہو کر اس کے تھوک کے مرتبہ میں ہے برخلاف کثیر کے کیونکہ وہ دانتوں کے درمیان باقی نہیں رہتا ہے اور حد فاصل چنے کی مقدار ہے اور جو اس سے کم ہودہ قلیل ہے۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ گوشت کا ریشہ جو دانتوں میں لپٹا ہوارہ گیا تھا اور روزہ دار نے اس کو اندر اندر ہی نہان سے حرکت دے کر کھا لیا تو وہ ریسہ اگر قلیل مقدار میں تھا تو روزہ فاسد نہیں ہوا اور اگر کثیر مقدار میں ہے تو فاسد ہو جائیگا امام زفر فرماتے ہیں کہ دونوں صورتوں میں فاسد ہو جائے گا۔ امام زفر کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اندرون منہ کو ظاہر بدن کا حکم حاصل ہے چنانچہ روزے کی حالت میں کلی کرنے سے روزہ نہیں ٹوٹتا حالانکہ پانی باہر سے منہ میں ڈالا گیا ہے پس جب اندرون منہ کو ظاہر بدن کا حکم حاصل ہے تو گوشت کا ریشہ جو منہ میں تھا اس کو حلق سے نیچے اتارنا ایسا ہے جیسا کہ خارج منہ سے کوئی چیز اٹھا کر کھائی گئی ہو اور خارج سے شئی قلیل کا کھانا بھی مفسد صوم ہے لہذا اس گوشت کے ریشہ کو نگل جانے سے بھی روزہ فاسد ہو جائے گا۔

ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ گوشت کے ریشہ کی مقدار قلیل دانتوں کے تابع ہے کیونکہ اس سے بچاؤ ممکن نہیں پس یہ بمنزلہ تھوک کے ہو گیا اور تھوک نگلنے سے روزہ فاسد نہیں ہوتا لہذا گوشت کے اس قلیل ریشہ سے بھی روزہ فاسد نہ ہوگا بر خلاف کثیر کے کہ وہ دانتوں کے درمیان بالعموم باقی نہیں رہتا لہذا اس سے بچاؤ ممکن ہوگا اور تقلیل و کثیر کے درمیان حد فاضل چنے کی مقدار ہے یعنی پنے کی مقدر کو کثیر کہا جائے گا اور اس سے کم کو قلیل کہا جائے گا۔
Eating meat stuck between teeth does not break the fast, and if it is a large amount, then eating it breaks the fast... Statements of the jurists. And if he ate meat between his teeth, then if it is little, he does not break fast, and if it is much, he breaks fast. Zufar said: he breaks fast in both cases because the mouth is considered external, such that his fast is not broken by rinsing. And our proof is that the little amount follows his teeth, akin to his saliva, unlike the much because it does not remain between the teeth. The dividing line is the amount of a chickpea, and what is less than it is little. Translation: And if he ate a meat fiber between his teeth, then if it is little, the fast is not broken, and if it is much, the fast is broken. Imam Zufar said that in both cases he breaks fast because the interior of the mouth has the ruling of the exterior, so rinsing does not break the fast. Since the interior has the ruling of the exterior, swallowing the meat fiber from the mouth is like taking something from outside and eating it, and eating even a little from outside breaks the fast, so swallowing this fiber also breaks the fast. Our proof is that a little amount is subordinate to the teeth and is like saliva, and swallowing saliva does not break the fast, so a little meat fiber does not break the fast. The much amount does not remain between the teeth, so it can be avoided. The dividing line is a chickpea: its amount is considered much, and less is little.
Source pages p. 213

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute between the majority (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) and Imam Zufar regarding meat stuck between teeth. The rule: if the amount is less than a chickpea (قلیل), the fast is not broken; if equal to or more than a chickpea (کثیر), it breaks. Imam Zufar argues that the mouth is like the external body, so even a little breaks the fast, analogizing to rinsing not breaking the fast. The Hanafi majority respond that a small amount is unavoidably stuck and thus like saliva, which does not break the fast. They set the chickpea as the boundary: anything less is considered negligible and unavoidable, while a chickpea or more is avoidable and breaks the fast.

Key Terms
قلیل (qalil): Less than the amount of a chickpea (حمصة). Considered negligible and unavoidable.
کثیر (kathir): Equal to or more than a chickpea. Considered avoidable and breaks the fast.
حمصة (himmasah): A chickpea; the standard measure for differentiating little and much in this context.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority Hanafi view, if a fasting person swallows a piece of meat stuck between teeth that is less than a chickpea, what is the ruling?
A) The fast is broken and qada is required
B) The fast is not broken
C) The fast is broken and kaffarah is required
D) The fast is invalid but no compensation needed

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi majority rule that a small amount (less than a chickpea) of residual food does not break the fast because it is unavoidable and akin to saliva.

Removing Food from Teeth: Fast-Breaking and Kaffarah Dispute
Ruling on food stuck in teeth and intra-Hanafi kaffarah dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a fasting person removes food stuck between teeth with his hand and then eats it, and explain why Abu Yusuf's view (no kaffarah for a chickpea-sized piece swallowed without removal) is the mufta bihi.

Core Idea
Removing stuck food with the hand triggers fast-break like external food; a chickpea-sized piece swallowed without removal requires qada but not kaffarah, per Abu Yusuf.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a delicate scenario in fasting: what if food stuck between the teeth is removed and then eaten? The text also explores a dispute between two great Hanafi imams—Abu Yusuf and Zufar—over whether kaffarah is due for swallowing a chickpea-sized piece from between the teeth without removal. This lesson will guide you through the rulings and the reasoning behind the preferred view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage states: if a fasting person removes food stuck between his teeth with his hand and then eats it, the fast breaks, even if the food is less than a chickpea. This is because removal makes it like external food.
Compare with the case of swallowing a sesame seed without removal.
2
Compare swallowing without removal
If a sesame seed (or smaller) stuck between the teeth is swallowed without removal, the fast does not break; similarly, if it is chewed first, it also does not break because it disintegrates and does not count as intentional swallowing.
The key distinction: removal changes the ruling.
3
Identify the disputed scenario
For a chickpea-sized piece stuck between the teeth that is swallowed without removal, the fast breaks and qada is due. However, there is a dispute (ikhtilaf) between Abu Yusuf and Zufar regarding kaffarah.
This is the specific point of disagreement.
4
State the two views and their proofs
Abu Yusuf: qada only, no kaffarah, because the food is spoiled and nature abhors it, making it a deficient violation. Zufar: qada and kaffarah, because it is still food and intentional eating requires both.
Both imams agree on qada; the dispute is only on kaffarah.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon view in the Hanafi school is that of Abu Yusuf: qada is necessary but kaffarah is not. This is supported by the nature of the food and the deficiency of the violation.
This is the operative position for fatwa.

وَإِنْ أَخْرَجَهُ وَأَخَذَهُ بِيَدِهِ ثُمَّ أَكَلَهُ يَنْبَغِى أَنْ يَفْسُدَ صَوْمُهُ كَمَا رُوِيَ عَنْ مُحَمَّدٍ أَنَّ الصَّائِمَ إِذَا ابْتَلَعَ سِمْسِكَةٌ بَيْنَ أَسْنَانِه لَا يَفْسُدُ صَومُه وَلَوْ أَكَلَهَا ابْتِدَاءً يَفْسُدُ صَومَهُ وَلَوْمَضَعَهَا لا يَفْسُدُ لأنَّهَا تَتَلاشى وَفِي مِقْدَارِ الْحِمَّصَةِ عَلَيْهِ القَضَاءُ دُونَ الْكَفَّارَةِ عِنْدَ أَبِى يُوسُفَ وَ عِنْدَ زُفُر عَلَيْهِ الْكَفَّارَةُ أَيْضًا لِأَنَّهُ طَعَامُ مُتَغَيَّرُ وَلا بِى يُوسُفَ أنه يُعَافُهُ الطَّبع ترجمہ اور اگر اس چیز کو نکال کر ہاتھ میں لے لیا پھر اس کو کھالیا تو مناسب یہ ہے کہ اس کا روزہ فاسد تو فاسد نہیں ہوگا کیونکہ وہ پراگندہ ہو کر نیست ہو جائے گا اور چنے کی مقدار میں اس پر قضاء واجب ہے نہ که کفاره ابو یوسف کے نزدیک اور امام زفر کے نزدیک اس پر کفارہ بھی واجب ہے کیونکہ یہ بگڑا ہوا طعام ہے۔ اور ابو یوسف کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ طبیعت اس کو مکر وہ بجھتی ہے۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ جو چیز دانتوں میں انکی ہوئی ہے روزہ دار نے اس کو اپنے ہاتھ سے منہ سے باہر نکالا اور پھر اس کو کھا گیا تو مناسب یہ ہے کہ اس صورت میں روزہ فاسد ہو جائے اگر چہ وہ چیز چنے کے دانہ سے کم مقدار ہو ۔ چنانچہ امام محمد سے مروی ہے کہ روزہ دار اگر دانتوں کے درمیان پھنسے ہوئے تل کے داللہ کو نگل گیا تو روزہ فاسد نہیں ہو گا اور A thing stuck between teeth, if taken out with the hand and then eaten, the fast will break. And if he took it out, held it in his hand, then ate it, it is appropriate that his fast breaks, as narrated from Muhammad: if a fasting person swallows a sesame seed between his teeth, his fast does not break; if he eats it from the start (i.e., places it in his mouth and swallows), his fast breaks; and if he chews it, it does not break because it disintegrates. And regarding the amount of a chickpea, qada is due upon him without kaffarah according to Abu Yusuf, and according to Zufar, kaffarah is also due because it is spoiled food. Abu Yusuf's proof is that nature abhors it... Explanation: The ruling is that if the fasting person takes out the stuck food with his hand from the mouth and then eats it, it is appropriate that the fast breaks even if the amount is less than a chickpea. As narrated from Imam Muhammad: if a fasting person swallows a sesame seed stuck between teeth, fast does not break; if he eats it initially (directly), fast breaks; if he chews it, fast does not break because it becomes dispersed. Regarding a chickpea-sized amount: qada is due but not kaffarah according to Abu Yusuf; Zufar says both qada and kaffarah are due because it is food, albeit spoiled. The author of Hidayah states that if a chickpea-sized amount is swallowed from between teeth (without removing with hand), the ruling has passed: fast breaks and qada is due, but there is dispute on kaffarah. Zufar's proof: it is food, and eating food intentionally in Ramadan requires both qada and kaffarah. Abu Yusuf's proof: the food has deteriorated, so it is a deficient violation, and deficient violation does not require kaffarah.
Source pages p. 214

Commentary
This passage first states a new ruling: if food stuck between teeth is removed with the hand and then eaten, the fast is broken, even if the food was less than a chickpea. This is because by removing it, it becomes like external food. The passage then discusses a related scenario from Imam Muhammad: swallowing a sesame seed from between teeth without removing it does not break the fast; but if one initially places a sesame seed in the mouth and eats it, the fast breaks. Chewing a sesame seed before swallowing also does not break it because it disintegrates and does not count as intentional swallowing. Then the passage addresses a chickpea-sized amount stuck between teeth: if it is swallowed without removing, the fast breaks and qada is due, but there is a dispute between Abu Yusuf and Zufar on kaffarah. Abu Yusuf says no kaffarah because the food has become spoiled and abhorrent to nature, making the violation deficient. Zufar says kaffarah is due because it is still food, and intentional eating of food in Ramadan necessitates both. The relied-upon view in the Hanafi school is that kaffarah is not required in this case, following Abu Yusuf.

Key Terms
افطار (iftar): Breaking the fast; here used synonymously with فساد صوم (invalidating the fast).
قضائ (qada): Making up a missed day of fasting after Ramadan.
كفاره (kaffarah): Expiation for deliberately breaking a Ramadan fast without valid reason; traditionally fasting for 60 consecutive days.
طعام متغير (ta'am mutaghayyar): Food that has changed (spoiled, putrid) due to being stuck between teeth.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The fast is not broken if the food is less than a chickpea.
B) The fast is broken regardless of the amount.
C) The fast is broken only if the food is a chickpea or more.
D) The fast is not broken because it was already in the mouth.

Key Takeaway
Removing stuck food with the hand makes it like external food, breaking the fast; for a chickpea-sized piece swallowed without removal, qada is due but kaffarah is not according to the mufta bihi view.

Ruling on Swallowing Food Stuck Between Teeth
Explains rulings on food remnants between teeth and their effect on fasting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on swallowing food remnants stuck between teeth during fasting, apply the chickpea threshold to distinguish between valid and invalid fasts, and explain the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on whether kaffarah is required.

Core Idea
Small unavoidable remnants are like saliva; intentional swallowing of large remnants breaks the fast.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah addresses a practical concern: what if food becomes stuck between the teeth while fasting? The author provides a detailed rational (istihsani) analysis, distinguishing between small and large amounts, and between inadvertent and intentional swallowing. The ruling hinges on the size of the remnant and whether it was extracted before swallowing. An important intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Yusuf and Zufar about the need for kaffarah is also discussed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Identify the different scenarios: inadvertent swallowing of small remnants, intentional swallowing after extraction, and chewing without swallowing. Determine whether the fast remains valid or becomes invalid in each case.
Focus on the distinction between qalil (small) and kathir (large) as defined by the chickpea threshold.
2
Locate the dalil
The evidence is rational (istihsan): small remnants are unavoidable, like saliva, so swallowing them does not invalidate the fast. The chickpea size is the dividing line.
The text also cites a narration from Imam Muhammad about a sesame seed.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Understand how the analogy with saliva and the threshold are justified. The author argues that small remnants are subject to the teeth and impossible to avoid, so they are excused.
This is a qiyas-based reasoning on the basis of istihsan.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Identify the dispute between Abu Yusuf (no kaffarah) and Zufar (kaffarah required) for chickpea-sized remnants swallowed intentionally after extraction.
Both agree that qada is required.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The relied-upon position is Abu Yusuf's: only qada. The reason is that the food is spoiled and nature abhors it, so the offense is incomplete (naqis jinaya), and kaffarah is only for complete offenses.
This tarjih is based on leniency and istihsan.

ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ گوشت کے ریشہ کی مقدار قلیل دانتوں کے تابع ہے کیونکہ اس سے بچاؤ ممکن نہیں پس یہ بمنزلہ تھوک کے ہو گیا اور تھوک نگلنے سے روزہ فاسد نہیں ہوتا لہذا گوشت کے اس قلیل ریشہ سے بھی روزہ فاسد نہ ہوگا بر خلاف کثیر کے کہ وہ دانتوں کے درمیان بالعموم باقی نہیں رہتا لہذا اس سے بچاؤ ممکن ہوگا اور تقلیل و کثیر کے درمیان حد فاضل چنے کی مقدار ہے یعنی پنے کی مقدر کو کثیر کہا جائے گا اور اس سے کم کو قلیل کہا جائے گا۔
دانتوں میں پھنسی ہوئی چیز کو ہاتھ سے نکالا پھر کھا لیا روزہ فاسد ہو جائے گا
وَإِنْ أَخْرَجَهُ وَأَخَذَهُ بِيَدِهِ ثُمَّ أَكَلَهُ يَنْبَغِي أَنْ يَفْسُدَ صَوْمُهُ كَمَا رُوِيَ عَنْ مُحَمَّدٍ أَنَّ الصَّائِمَ إِذَا ابْتَلَعَ سِمْسِمَةً بَيْنَ أَسْنَانِهِ لَا يَفْسُدُ صَوْمُهُ وَلَوْ أَكَلَهَا ابْتِدَاءً يَفْسُدُ صَوْمُهُ وَلَوْ مَضَغَهَا لَا يَفْسُدُ لِأَنَّهَا تَتَلَاشَى وَفِي مِقْدَارِ الْحِمِّصَةِ عَلَيْهِ الْقَضَاءُ دُونَ الْكَفَّارَةِ عِنْدَ أَبِي يُوسُفَ وَعِنْدَ زُفَرَ عَلَيْهِ الْكَفَّارَةُ أَيْضًا لِأَنَّهُ طَعَامٌ مُتَغَيِّرٌ وَلِأَبِي يُوسُفَ أَنَّهُ يُعَافُهُ الطَّبْعُ
ترجمہ اور اگر اس چیز کو نکال کر ہاتھ میں لے لیا پھر اس کو کھالیا تو مناسب یہ ہے کہ اس کا روزہ فاسد ہو جائے جیسا کہ امام محمد سے روایت ہے کہ روزہ دار جب تل کا دانہ دانتوں کے درمیان سے نگل گیا تو اس کا روزہ فاسد نہ ہوگا اور اگر تل کو ابتدا کھایا تو اس کا روزہ فاسد ہو جائے گا اور اگر اس کو چبا کر نگلا تو فاسد نہیں ہوگا کیونکہ وہ پراگندہ ہو کر نیست ہو جائے گا اور چنے کی مقدار میں اس پر قضاء واجب ہے نہ کہ کفارہ ابو یوسف کے نزدیک اور امام زفر کے نزدیک اس پر کفارہ بھی واجب ہے کیونکہ یہ بگڑا ہوا طعام ہے۔ اور ابو یوسف کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ طبیعت اس کو مکروہ سمجھتی ہے۔
تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ جو چیز دانتوں میں پھنسی ہوئی ہے روزہ دار نے اس کو اپنے ہاتھ سے منہ سے باہر نکالا اور پھر اس کو کھا گیا تو مناسب یہ ہے کہ اس صورت میں روزہ فاسد ہو جائے اگر چہ وہ چیز چنے کے دانہ سے کم مقدار ہو ۔ چنانچہ امام محمد سے مروی ہے کہ روزہ دار اگر دانتوں کے درمیان پھنسے ہوئے تل کے دانہ کو نگل گیا تو روزہ فاسد نہیں ہو گا اور اگر تل یا بقدر تل کوئی چیز ابتدا منہ میں ڈال کر کھائی تو روزہ فاسد ہو جائے گا اور اگر تل کے دانہ کو منہ میں ڈال کر چبایا اور نگلا تو اس سے روزہ فاسد نہ ہوگا کیونکہ تل کا دانہ جب چبایا گیا تو وہ دانتوں اور زبان کو لگ کر ختم ہو جائے گا اس پر اندر داخل ہونا صادق نہ آئے گا اور جب جوف میں داخل ہونا صادق نہ آیا تو روزہ بھی فاسد نہ ہو گا صاحب ہدایہ کہتے ہیں کہ چنے کی مقدار کوئی چیز دانتوں میں سے اندر اندر نگل گیا تو سابق میں اس کا حکم گذر چکا کہ اس سے روزہ فاسد ہو جائے گا اور قضا واجب ہوگی لیکن کفارہ واجب ہونے میں اختلاف ہے چنانچہ حضرت امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک کفارہ واجب نہ ہوگا اور امام زفر فرماتے ہیں کہ کفارہ بھی واجب ہوگا۔ امام زفر کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ چنے کی مقدار جو چیز دانتوں میں پھنسی ہوئی ہے وہ بھی طعام ہے اگر چہ بدبودار طعام ہے اور طعام کو بالارادہ کھانے سے بشرطیکہ رمضان کا روزہ ہو قضاء اور کفارہ دونوں واجب ہوتے ہیں اس لئے اس صورت میں بھی قضاء اور کفارہ دونوں واجب ہوں گے ۔ اور امام ابو یوسف کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ جو چیز دانتوں میں پھنس کر رہ گئی اس کے غذا ہونے میں نقصان پیدا ہو گیا اسی لئے بسا اوقات اس میں اس قدر ناگوار بدبو پیدا ہو جاتی ہے کہ طبیعت سلیمہ اس سے نفرت کرنے لگتی ہے پس اس کو کھانے سے جنایت تو پائی گئی مگر ناقص، اور ناقص جنایت سے کفارہ واجب نہیں ہوتا اس لئے :
Our evidence is that a small amount of meat fiber is subject to the teeth because it is impossible to avoid it, so it becomes like saliva, and swallowing saliva does not invalidate the fast. Therefore, swallowing a small amount of meat fiber also does not invalidate the fast, unlike a large amount which generally does not remain between the teeth, so avoiding it is possible. The dividing line between small and large is the size of a chickpea: the measure of a chickpea is called large, and less than that is called small.
If he extracts what is stuck between his teeth with his hand and then eats it, his fast becomes invalid.
And if he takes it out and takes it in his hand then eats it, it is proper that his fast becomes invalid, as is narrated from Muhammad: if a fasting person swallows a sesame seed that was between his teeth, his fast does not become invalid. But if he eats it in the beginning, his fast becomes invalid. And if he chews it, it does not invalidate because it disintegrates. For the amount of a chickpea, he must make up the fast (qada) but not expiation (kaffarah) according to Abu Yusuf. According to Zufar, expiation is also required because it is spoiled food. Abu Yusuf's evidence is that nature abhors it.
Translation: And if he extracts it and takes it in his hand and then eats it, it is proper that his fast becomes invalid, as narrated from Muhammad: if a fasting person swallows a sesame seed from between his teeth, his fast does not become invalid; but if he eats it intentionally (initially), his fast becomes invalid; and if he chews it, it does not invalidate because it disintegrates. For the amount of a chickpea, he owes qada but not kaffarah according to Abu Yusuf, and according to Zufar, kaffarah is also obligatory because it is spoiled food. Abu Yusuf's evidence is that nature finds it repulsive.
Explanation: The issue is that if a fasting person extracts a thing stuck between his teeth with his hand and then eats it, it is proper that his fast becomes invalid in this case, even if it is less than the size of a chickpea. Thus, it is narrated from Imam Muhammad that if a fasting person swallows a sesame seed stuck between his teeth, his fast does not become invalid. But if he eats a sesame seed or similar intentionally from the start, his fast becomes invalid. And if he puts a sesame seed in his mouth, chews it, and swallows it, his fast does not become invalid because the seed when chewed disintegrates and gets attached to the teeth and tongue, so the act of entering the stomach is not verified. When entering the stomach is not verified, the fast does not become invalid. Author of Hidayah says: if a thing of the size of a chickpea is swallowed from between the teeth internally, its ruling has already passed that the fast becomes invalid and qada is obligatory. However, there is disagreement about kaffarah being obligatory. According to Imam Abu Yusuf, kaffarah is not obligatory; Imam Zufar says kaffarah is also obligatory. Zufar's evidence: the thing of chickpea size stuck between teeth is also food, even if spoiled food, and eating food intentionally provided it is a Ramadan fast makes both qada and kaffarah obligatory, so here both are obligatory. Abu Yusuf's evidence: the thing stuck between teeth has become defective in its nutritive property, therefore sometimes it develops such a bad odor that a healthy nature begins to detest it. So eating it involves an offense but a defective one, and a defective offense does not require kaffarah. Therefore:
Source pages p. 214

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidaya deals with the ruling on food remnants between teeth during fasting. The author first establishes a principle: small remnants that are difficult to avoid (like meat fibers) are analogous to saliva, so inadvertently swallowing them does not break the fast. Large remnants that can be avoided do break the fast. The dividing line is the size of a chickpea (حمصة). This is a rational (istihsan) argument. The passage then moves to a specific case: if a fasting person extracts something from between his teeth with his hand and then swallows it, the fast breaks, regardless of quantity, because it becomes intentional ingestion. A narration from Imam Muhammad is cited: swallowing a sesame seed stuck between teeth inadvertently does not break the fast; but eating it intentionally at the start does; chewing and swallowing it does not break it because it disintegrates and is not considered a distinct object entering the stomach. For a chickpea-sized amount, qada (make-up) is required but kaffarah (expiation) is disputed: Abu Yusuf says no kaffarah because the food is spoiled and nature abhors it, making the offense incomplete; Zufar says kaffarah is required because it is still food and intentional eating of food in Ramadan entails both. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is typically Abu Yusuf's view in the Hanafi school, as it is more lenient.

Key Terms
بقدر الحمصة (biqadr al-himmah): The size of a chickpea, used as the threshold to distinguish between a small (qalil) and large (kathir) amount of food remnant.
جنایت (jinayat): Offense or transgression against the fast; here used to describe the act of eating after extraction.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling if a fasting person swallows a sesame seed that was stuck between his teeth without prior extraction?
A) The fast breaks and requires qada and kaffarah.
B) The fast does not break.
C) The fast breaks and requires qada only.
D) The fast becomes makruh.

Key Takeaway
Small unavoidable food remnants between teeth do not break the fast, but intentional swallowing of substantial remnants after extraction does, with qada required and kaffarah disputed.

Sawm — Fasting
intermediate
8 min
Ruling on Vomiting During Fasting: Involuntary vs. Deliberate
Covers involuntary vs intentional vomiting and the effect of vomit returning to the stomach

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on vomiting during fasting, distinguish between involuntary and deliberate vomiting, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute about vomit returning to the stomach.

Core Idea
Involuntary vomiting does not break the fast; deliberate vomiting does. Dispute arises when vomit returns spontaneously.

Fasting requires abstaining from eating, drinking, and other nullifiers from dawn to sunset. Vomiting is a specific issue addressed in the hadith, which clearly distinguishes between involuntary and deliberate vomiting. The Hanafi school elaborates on this with further scenarios involving the amount of vomit and whether it returns to the stomach, leading to a well-known dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary ruling and proof
State the ruling that involuntary vomiting does not require qada and deliberate vomiting does. Identify the hadith as the dalil (proof).
The hadith is 'Man qaa ...' – focus on the explicit distinction.
2
Analyze the scope: mouthful vs. less
Notice that the hadith is absolute – it applies whether the vomit fills the mouth or is less. The primary ruling remains the same.
The commentary emphasizes the general nature of the hadith.
3
Examine the dispute on spontaneous return of a mouthful
When a mouthful of vomit exits involuntarily and then spontaneously returns to the stomach, Abu Yusuf holds the fast invalid while Muhammad holds it valid. Understand each imam's reasoning.
Abu Yusuf: vomit that exits is 'outside' (like it breaks wudu), so re-entry is like a foreign object. Muhammad: no intentional swallowing and no nutritive purpose.
4
Apply the same logic to less than a mouthful
If the vomit is less than a mouthful and returns spontaneously, both agree the fast is not invalidated. If deliberately returned, Abu Yusuf holds no invalidation (since it never fully exited), while Muhammad holds it invalidates.
The key factor is whether the vomit is considered 'exited' (kharij) and whether the person acted deliberately.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
The dispute leads to different rulings on whether qada (make-up fast) is required. According to Abu Yusuf, qada is required when a mouthful returns spontaneously; according to Muhammad, it is not. For less than a mouthful deliberately returned, Muhammad requires qada, Abu Yusuf does not.
Most Hanafi works prefer Abu Yusuf's view as more cautious (ihtiyat).
