Kaffarah for Anal Intercourse during Fasting
Intra-Hanafi dispute on kaffarah for anal intercourse during Ramadan.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on kaffarah for anal intercourse during Ramadan and state the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Kaffarah for anal intercourse is wajib because quenching desire suffices, even without inzal.

This lesson examines a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute: does kaffarah become obligatory for anal intercourse (liwat) during Ramadan? The passage refutes the idea that inzal is required, using analogies from eating a morsel and the hadd penalty. It then presents the two narrations from Imam Abu Hanifa and the view of the Sahibayn, concluding which position is relied upon for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is anal intercourse during a Ramadan fast. Determine whether it invalidates the fast and triggers kaffarah.
The fast is invalidated by intentional intercourse, but the kaffarah is disputed.
2
Refute the misconception that inzal is necessary
The passage argues that quenching desire (qada al-shahwa) occurs without inzal, using the morsel analogy: a single morsel causes kaffarah even without satiety.
This establishes that kaffarah does not depend on inzal.
3
Examine the dispute: two narrations from Abu Hanifa
One narration says no kaffarah (analogy with hadd), the other says kaffarah for both parties (with Sahibayn).
The first narration considers the act unnatural, not a complete jinaya.
4
Understand the Sahibayn's position and the second narration
They hold that kaffarah is wajib because the act quenches desire, making it a complete offense.
They reject the analogy with hadd because kaffarah is both worship and punishment.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The text states the second narration is more correct (azhar), so kaffarah is obligatory.
This is the operative ruling for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
انزال کے شہوت کا پورا نہ ہونا ہمیں تسلیم نہیں ہے کیونکہ قضا شہوت تو بغیر انزال کے متحقق ہو جاتی ہے البتہ انزال سے سیری حاصل ہوتی ہے پس جب یہ ثابت ہو گیا کہ قضاء شہوت میں انزال کو کوئی دخل نہیں ہے تو یہ بھی ثابت ہو گیا کہ بغیر انزال کے جماع کے معنی متحقق ہو جاتے ہیں اور جب بغیر انزال کے جماع کے معنی محقق ہو گئے تو عدم جماع کا شبہ نہ رہا اور جب شبہ نہ رہاتو کفارہ ساقط نہ ہوگا بلکہ کفارہ ثابت ہوگا آپ نے بھی اس پر غور نہیں کیا کہ اگر روزہ دار عمداً ایک لقمہ کھالے تو اس پر کفارہ واجب ہو جائے گا حالانکہ ایک لقمہ سے میری حاصل نہیں ہوتی پس اسی طرح جماع کی صورت میں کفارہ کا وجوب میری حاصل کرنے (انزال ) پر موقوف نہیں ہوگا بلکہ قضاء شہوت پر موقوف رہے گا اور قضا شہوت کا تحقق بغیر انزال کے ہو جاتا ہے لہذا بغیر انزال جماع کرنے سے بھی کفارہ واجب ہو جائے گا وجوب کفارہ کے لئے انزال شرط نہ ہونے پر صاحب کفایہ نے ایک دلیل یہ بیان کی ہے کہ حد واجب کرنے کے لئے انزال شرط نہیں ہے یعنی اگر ایک فرج کا دوسرے کے فرج میں ادخال پایا گیا تو حد واجب ہو جائے گی اگر چہ انزال نہ ہوا ہو حالانکہ حد محض ایک عقوبت اور سزا ہے پس کفارہ جو عبادت اور عقوبت دونوں جہتوں کو شامل ہے اسکے وجوب کے لئے بدرجہ اولی انزال شرط نہ ہو گا۔
حضرت امام ابوحنیفہ سے ایک روایت یہ ہے کہ دبر میں جماع (لواطت ) کرنے سے کفارہ واجب نہیں ہو گا حضرت امام اعظم نے اس کو وجوب حد پر قیاس کیا ہے یعنی جس طرح اس غیر فطری اور ناشائستہ حرکت پر حد واجب نہیں ہوتی اسی طرح اس حرکت سے روزہ کا کفارہ بھی واجب نہ ہوگا اور علت مشترکہ کہ جنابت کا ملہ کا نہ پایا جانا ہے یعنی حد اور کفارہ دونوں کے وجوب کے لئے جنابت کاملہ کا ہونا ضروری ہے اور حضرت امام اعظم نے اس کو کامل جنایت شمار نہیں کیا ہے کیونکہ طبیعت سلیمہ اس بہیمانہ فعل سے نفرت کرتی ہے اور حضرت امام اعظم کی دوسری روایت یہ ہے کہ فاعل و مفعول اگر دونوں روزہ دار ہوں تو دونوں پر کفارہ واجب ہوگا یہی صاحبین کا قول ہے اور یہی زیادہ صحیح ہے کیونکہ دبر کے اندر جماع کی وجہ سے بھی چونکہ قضاء شہوت ہوتی ہے اس لئے اس صورت میں بھی جنایت کامل درجہ کی پائی گئی اور جنایت کا ملہ موجب کفارہ ہے لہذا اس صورت میں بھی کفارہ واجب ہوگا۔
The fact that the desire is not fully satisfied by inzal is not acceptable to us, because the quenching of desire is achieved without inzal; however, satiety is obtained through inzal. So when it is established that inzal has no role in quenching desire, it is also established that the meaning of intercourse is realized without inzal. And when the meaning of intercourse is realized without inzal, there remains no doubt of non-intercourse. And when there is no doubt, kaffarah will not be dropped, rather kaffarah will be established. You have not considered this: if a fasting person intentionally eats a single morsel, kaffarah becomes obligatory on him, even though satiety is not obtained from one morsel. Similarly, in the case of intercourse, the obligation of kaffarah does not depend on obtaining satiety (inzal), but rather on quenching desire. And quenching desire occurs without inzal. Therefore, kaffarah becomes obligatory even by intercourse without inzal. On the point that inzal is not a condition for the obligation of kaffarah, the author of Kifayah gave this proof: that inzal is not a condition for the obligation of hadd; i.e., if insertion of one private part into another is found, hadd becomes obligatory even if no inzal occurred. And hadd is purely a punishment and penalty. So for kaffarah, which includes both worship and punishment, a fortiori inzal should not be a condition for its obligation.
A narration from Imam Abu Hanifa is that kaffarah is not obligatory by anal intercourse (sodomy). Imam A'zam analogized this to the obligation of hadd: just as hadd is not obligatory for this unnatural and obscene act, similarly kaffarah for fasting will not be obligatory by this act. The common cause is that complete janaba is not achieved; i.e., for the obligation of both hadd and kaffarah, complete janaba is necessary. And Imam A'zam did not consider this as a complete offense because a sound nature abhors this bestial act. Another narration from Imam A'zam is that if both the active and passive participants are fasting, then kaffarah is obligatory on both. This is the saying of the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), and this is more correct because by anal intercourse, quenching of desire does occur, so in this case a complete degree of offense is found, and a complete offense necessitates kaffarah. Therefore, in this case too, kaffarah is obligatory.
Source pages p. 219

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding kaffarah for anal intercourse during fasting. The text first refutes the idea that inzal is necessary for kaffarah, arguing that quenching desire (qada al-shahwa) occurs without inzal, and uses the analogy of eating a single morsel to show that satiety is not required for kaffarah. The author of Kifayah supports this by noting that hadd (flogging for zina) becomes obligatory upon mere insertion, without inzal, so kaffarah—which combines worship and punishment—should similarly not require inzal. Then, the dispute within the Hanafi school is introduced: Abu Hanifa has two narrations. In one, he says no kaffarah for anal intercourse, analogizing it to hadd (which is not applied for sodomy in Hanafi law) because the act is unnatural and does not constitute complete janaba. In the other narration (also held by the Sahibayn), kaffarah is obligatory on both parties because quenching of desire occurs, making it a complete offense. The text concludes that the second narration is more correct (azhar). This lesson covers the reasoning and the ikhtilaf within the school.

Key Terms
جنابت کاملہ (janaba kāmila): Complete state of major ritual impurity requiring ghusl, achieved by genital-to-genital contact with or without inzal
قضاء شہوت (qaḍā al-shahwa): Quenching of sexual desire, considered the essence of the offense (jinaya)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position (mufta bihi), what is the ruling on kaffarah for anal intercourse during Ramadan?
A) No kaffarah is obligatory because it is an unnatural act.
B) Kaffarah is obligatory only on the active participant.
C) Kaffarah is obligatory on both participants if both are fasting.
D) Kaffarah is obligatory only if inzal occurs.

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position: kaffarah for anal intercourse during Ramadan is wajib on both fasting participants, as quenching desire is achieved without inzal.

Kaffarah for Intercourse with Corpse or Animal and Women's Liability
Hanafi vs Shafi'i on kaffarah for corpse/animal and women's liability

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on kaffarah for intercourse with a corpse/animal, explain the condition of mahall mushtahi, and argue why a woman is independently liable for kaffarah when she willingly participates.

Core Idea
No kaffarah for corpse/animal because the desired place is absent; women are equally liable because they share the offense of invalidating the fast.

This passage from al-Hidayah addresses two nuanced rulings: kaffarah for intercourse with non-human objects and the woman's obligation. The Hanafi school makes a distinction: the act must be in a naturally desired place. A corpse or animal does not qualify. As for women, the general command 'man afṭara' includes her, and the cause is the offense of ifsad, not merely the man's act. The Shafi'i school differs on both points.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two issues
Recognize that the passage treats two distinct rulings: (1) intercourse with a dead body or animal, and (2) the woman's liability for kaffarah. Each has its own evidence and opposition.
2
Analyze the first issue: no kaffarah for corpse/animal
Note the Hanafi condition that kaffarah is only for a 'complete jinaya' which requires qada' shahwa (quenching desire) in a mahall mushtahi (a naturally desired place). A corpse or animal is not a mahall mushtahi, so the offense is incomplete.
Contrast with Shafi'i who says the mere act of insertion suffices.
3
Analyze the second issue: woman's liability
Examine the hadith 'man afṭara...' which is general and includes women. Hanafi argues that the cause (sabab) of kaffarah is jinayat al-ifṣād (the offense of invalidating the fast), not the intercourse per se. Since the woman shares in that offense, she is equally liable.
Shafi'i has two opinions: (a) no liability because kaffarah attaches to the man's act, (b) liability but the man bears it by analogy to ghusl water.
4
Understand the Hanafi response to Shafi'i
For the first, the condition of mahall mushtahi is not met. For the second, bearing (taḥammul) is invalid because kaffarah is either worship or punishment, which cannot be performed by proxy. The hadith itself is unambiguous.
5
Determine the operative ruling
The mufta bihi (relied-upon) position is: no kaffarah for corpse/animal (only qada if inzal occurred); a willing woman is independently obligated to pay kaffarah.
If coerced, no kaffarah on woman.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مردہ اور چوپائے سے ولی مفسد صوم ہے انزال ہو یا نہ ہو کفارہ لازم نہیں ، امام شافعی کا نقطہ نظر وَلَوْ جَامَعَ مَيْتَةً أَوْ بَهِيمَةً فَلَا كَفَّارَةَ أَنزَلَ أَوْلَمْ يُنْزِلُ خِلَافًا لِلشَّافِعِي لِأَنَّ الْجِنَايَةَ تَكَامُلُهَا بِقَضَاءِ الشَّهَوَةِ فِي مَحَلٍ مُشْتَهِي وَلَمْ يُوجَدُ ثُمَّ عِنْدَنَا كَمَا تَجِبُ الْكَفَّارَةُ بِالْوِقاع عَلَى الرَّجُلِ تَجِبُ عَلَى الْمَرْأَةِ وَقَالَ الشَّافِعِي فِي قَوْلٍ لَا تَجِبُّ عَلَيْهَا لأَنَّهَا مُتَعَلَّقَةُ بِالْجِمَاعِ وَهُوَ فِعْلُهُ وَإِنَّمَا هِيَ مَحَلَّ الْفِعْلِ وَفِي قَوْلٍ تَجِبُ وَيَتَحَمَّلُ الرَّجُلُ عَنْهَا اعْتِبَارًا بِمَاءِ الْاِغْتِسَالِ وَلَنَا قَوْلُهُ مَنْ أفْطَرَ فِي رَمَضَانَ فَعَلَيْهِ مَا عَلَى الْمُظَاهِرِ وَكَلِمَةُ مَنْ تَنتَظِمُ الدُّكُورَ وَالْإِنَاثَ وَلِأَنَّ السَّبَبَ جِنَايَةُ الْإِفْسَادِ لَا نَفْسُ الْوِقَاعِ وَقَدْ شَارَكَتْهُ فِيهَا وَلَا تَحْمِلُ لِأَنَّهَا عِبَادَةً أَوْ عَقُوبَةً وَلَا يَجْرَى فِيهَا الْحَمَلُ
And if he has intercourse with a dead body or an animal, there is no kaffarah, whether he ejaculates or not, contrary to al-Shafi'i, because the offense is completed by quenching desire in a desired place, and that is not found. Then according to us, just as kaffarah becomes obligatory upon the man by intercourse, it becomes obligatory upon the woman. Al-Shafi'i said in one opinion: it is not obligatory upon her because kaffarah is attached to intercourse, and intercourse is his act; she is merely the locus of the act. In another opinion, it is obligatory, and the man bears it on her behalf, drawing an analogy to water for ghusl. Our proof is his (peace be upon him) saying: 'Whoever breaks fast in Ramadan, upon him is what is upon the one who does zihar.' The word 'man' encompasses males and females. And because the cause is the offense of invalidating the fast, not the intercourse itself, and she shared in that offense. And he does not bear it because it is worship or punishment, and bearing is not applicable in them.
Source pages p. 219

Commentary
This passage presents two interrelated rulings from the Hanafi school, with opposition from Imam al-Shafi'i. First, if a fasting person intentionally has intercourse with a dead body or an animal, no kaffarah is required, regardless of ejaculation. The Hanafi reasoning is that kaffarah is for a 'complete offense' (jinaya kāmila), which requires both quenching of desire and a 'desired place' (maḥall mushtahi). A corpse or animal is not a naturally desired place, so the offense is incomplete, and only qada (makeup) is required if inzal occurs. Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees, arguing that the mere act of intercourse is sufficient for kaffarah. Second, the Hanafi school holds that a woman who willingly participates in intercourse during Ramadan is equally liable for kaffarah. The proof is the general word 'man' in the hadith 'Whoever breaks fast...' and the fact that she shares in the offense of invalidating the fast. Imam al-Shafi'i has two opinions: one that she is not liable because kaffarah is attached to the act of intercourse (done by the man), and another that she is liable but the man bears it for her (by analogy to providing water for ghusl). The Hanafi response rejects this bearing because kaffarah is either a worship or a punishment, and neither can be performed by proxy. The commentary also notes conditions: the woman must have consented willingly; if coerced, no kaffarah on her. Also, if she initially resisted but later enjoyed, still no kaffarah according to Fath al-Qadir.

Key Terms
مَحَلٍ مُشْتَهِي (maḥall mushtahī): A naturally desired place for intercourse, i.e., a living human female
جنایت الإفساد (jināyat al-ifṣād): The offense of invalidating the fast, which is the cause of kaffarah
التحمل (al-taḥammul): Bearing a liability on behalf of another, rejected in kaffarah because it is worship or punishment

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, does a woman who willingly engages in intercourse during Ramadan have to pay kaffarah?
A) No, because kaffarah is the man's responsibility.
B) Yes, but the man can bear it on her behalf.
C) Yes, she is independently obligated to pay kaffarah.
D) No, because she is the locus of the act.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school conditions kaffarah on a complete jinaya in a desired place, and holds women independently liable because they share the offense of ifsad, supported by the general text of the hadith.

Sawm — Fasting
intermediate

Kafarah for Intercourse with Corpse or Animal While Fasting
Hanafi ruling on kafarah for corpse/animal intercourse

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on kafarah for intercourse with a corpse or animal, explain the Hanafi proof based on jināyah kāmilah, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
Kafarah requires a complete violation in a natural place; intercourse with corpse or animal is incomplete, so no kafarah.

Intercourse with a corpse or animal while fasting is a grave sin, but does it trigger the same expiation as intercourse with a living spouse? The Hanafi school distinguishes between a complete violation (jināyah kāmilah) and an incomplete one. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind the Hanafi position, the Shafi'i objection, and the practical consequences for both men and women.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi ruling
Recall the Hanafi position: no kafarah for intercourse with a corpse or animal, only qada if ejaculation occurs. Also, for a woman, kafarah is wajib if she willingly participated.
The ruling applies regardless of ejaculation for kafarah; qada depends on ejaculation.
2
Identify the Hanafi proof (dalil)
The cause of kafarah is a complete violation (jināyah kāmilah), which requires fulfilling desire in its natural place (maḥall al-shahwah). Corpse and animal are not natural objects of desire, so the violation is incomplete.
Hanafi uses the hadith 'man afṭara fī Ramaḍāna' but restricts it via the condition of completeness.
3
Present the Shafi'i proof
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that any act of intercourse that nullifies the form of fasting (ṣūrat al-imsāk) triggers kafarah, regardless of the object.
Shafi'i relies on the general implication of the hadith without the completeness restriction.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
Hanafi responds that the hadith is general but must be restricted by the requirement of a complete violation, which is absent here. The Shafi'i position is countered by emphasizing the need for jināyah kāmilah.
This is an example of takhsis (restriction) of a general text by a condition from the maqāṣid.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: in Hanafi, no kafarah is required; in Shafi'i, kafarah is wajib. This affects advice given to a person who committed such an act.
The Fath al-Qadir note expands the Hanafi ruling to include male objects in sodomy.

Ashraf al-Hidaya sharh Urdu Hidaya volume 3, page 219. Book of Fasting. ... Explanation: If a fasting person has intercourse with a dead person, an animal, or a man (i.e., homosexual act), then kafarah is not wajib, whether or not ejaculation occurs. However, if ejaculation occurs, qada becomes wajib; without ejaculation, qada is not wajib. Imam Shafi'i said: kafarah is wajib. His proof: the cause of kafarah is intercourse that nullifies the form of refraining (from intercourse), and such intercourse occurs here. Our proof: the cause of kafarah is a complete violation, which is fulfilling desire in a natural place of desire. Here, the natural place is not present because sound nature abhors such acts; so the violation is incomplete, thus no kafarah. The author of Hidayah said: when kafarah is wajib on the man from intercourse, it is also wajib on the woman provided she consented willingly. If she was forced, no kafarah on her; similarly, if she initially resisted but later enjoyed, no kafarah. Fath al-Qadir commented it would be better if the author said 'upon the object' instead of 'upon the woman' to include the male object in sodomy. Imam Shafi'i said: kafarah is not wajib on the woman because intercourse is the man's act. His second opinion: kafarah is wajib on the woman but the man performs it, analogized to the cost of water for ghusl. Our proof: the hadith 'whoever breaks the fast in Ramadan owes what the one who performs zihar owes', and the word 'man' is general including male and female. Also, the cause is the crime of breaking the fast, not just intercourse, and the woman shares in that crime. As for his second opinion, kafarah is worship or penalty, and substitution is not valid in these.
Source pages p. 220

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute between Hanafi and Shafi'i on whether kafarah (expiation) is required for a fasting person who has intercourse with a corpse or an animal. The Hanafi position is that no kafarah is required, only qada if ejaculation occurs, because a complete violation (jināyah kāmilah) requires fulfilling desire in its natural place (maḥall al-shahwah), which is absent here. Shafi'i argues that any act of intercourse that nullifies the form of fasting (ṣūrat al-imsāk) triggers kafarah. The text then discusses the ruling for women: according to Hidayah, if a woman willingly participates in unlawful intercourse while fasting, she also must pay kafarah; if forced, she does not. Shafi'i's first view rejects any kafarah on the woman; his second view accepts kafarah but requires the man to perform it. The Hanafi response emphasizes that kafarah is a worship or penalty, and one person cannot bear it for another. The ḥadīth 'man afṭara fī Ramaḍāna faʿalayhi mā ʿalā al-muẓāhir' is cited to include both men and women. The Fath al-Qadir note suggests that the text should explicitly include anal intercourse (with a male) as also incurring kafarah.

Key Terms
جنایت کاملہ (jināyah kāmilah): A complete violation requiring fulfillment of desire in its natural place (maḥall al-shahwah).
محل شہوت (maḥall al-shahwah): The natural object of sexual desire, i.e., a living human partner.
کفارہ (kafārah): Expiation required for deliberately breaking a fast in Ramadan in a complete manner.
قضاء (qaḍāʾ): Making up a missed or broken fast on another day.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is kafarah not required for intercourse with a corpse while fasting?
A) Because the hadith about kafarah does not cover such acts.
B) Because the violation is incomplete due to the absence of a natural place of desire.
C) Because ejaculation is unlikely with a corpse.
D) Because the act is not considered a sin.

Key Takeaway
Kafarah in Hanafi fiqh requires a complete violation in a natural place of desire; acts with corpses or animals are incomplete and do not trigger expiation, only qada if ejaculation occurs.

Sawm — Fasting

Kafarah for Eating or Drinking Nourishing or Medicinal Substances While Fasting
Hanafi ruling on kafarah for eating/drinking food or medicine

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on kafarah for intentional eating/drinking/medication while fasting and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using the Bedouin hadith.

Core Idea
Intentional eating or drinking while fasting requires both qada and kafarah, as per Hanafi school.

In this passage, we examine a key dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding the requirement of kafarah (expiation) when a fasting person intentionally eats, drinks, or takes medicine. The Hanafi position extends kafarah beyond intercourse to all forms of breaking the fast, while the Shafi'i school confines it to intercourse alone. Understanding the proofs on both sides – especially the use of the Bedouin hadith and the role of qiyas – is essential for correctly deriving the ruling.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the exact ruling: both qada and kafarah are wajib for anyone who intentionally eats, drinks, or takes medicine while fasting in Ramadan.
2
Identify the opposing school and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i (and Imam Ahmad) hold that only qada is required; no kafarah.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The Shafi'i argue that kafarah was legislated for intercourse only as a special case against analogy (khilaf al-qiyas). Since tawbah removes sin, other acts cannot be analogized.
They rely on the Bedouin hadith where the Prophet prescribed kafarah despite the man's repentance.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafis argue that kafarah is attached to the complete crime of breaking the fast, whether by intercourse or food/drink. The Bedouin hadith shows tawbah does not suffice; otherwise the Prophet would not have ordered expiation. Thus kafarah is not khilaf al-qiyas and analogy to other acts is valid.
They use the same hadith to prove their point.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: Hanafi requires qada + kafarah; Shafi'i requires qada only. The Hanafi position is mufta bihi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
غذا کی اجناس سے کھا لیا یا پی لیا یا دوا کر لی تو قضا اور کفارہ دونوں لازم ہیں ، امام شافعی کا نقطہ نظر وَلَوْ أَكَلَ أَوْ شَرِب مَايُتَغَذَّى بِه أَوْ مَا يُدَاوِى بِهِ فَعَلَيْهِ الْقَضَاءُ وَالْكَفَّارَةُ وَ قَالَ الشَّافِعِيُّ لا كَفَّارَةَ عَلَيْهِ لِأَنَّهَا شُرعَتْ فِى الْوَقَائِعِ بِخِلَافِ الْقِيَاسِ لارتفاع الذَّنْبِ بِالتَّوْبَةِ فَلَا يُقَاسُ عَلَيْهِ غَيْرُهُ وَلَنَا أنَّ الكَفَّارَةَ تَعَلَّقَتُ بِجِنايَةِ الْإِفْطَارِ فِي رَمَضَانَ عَلى وَجْهِ الْكَمَالِ وَقَدْ تَحَقَّقَتْ وَبِايُجَابِ الْإِعْتَاقِ تَكْفِيرًا عُرِفَ أنَّ التَّوْبَةَ غَيْرُ مُكَفِّرَةٍ لهذه الجناية
ترجمہ اور اگر روزہ دار نے کوئی ایسی چیز کھالی یا پی لی جس سے غذا حاصل کی جاتی ہے یا اس سے کوئی دوا کی جاتی ہے تو اس پر قضا و کفارہ دونوں واجب ہوں گے اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا ہے کہ اس پر کفارہ واجب نہیں ہے کیونکہ کفارہ تو خلاف قیاس جماع کی صورت میں مشروع ہوا ہے کیونکہ گناہ تو بہ سے دور ہو گیا ہے اس لئے اس پر دوسری چیز کا قیاس نہ ہوگا اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ کفارہ رمضان میں علی وجہ الکمال جنایت افطار کی ساتھ متعلق ہے اور وہ محقق ہو گیا اور بطور کفارہ کے غلام کی آزادی واجب کرنے سے پہچانا گیا ہے کہ تو بہ اس گنا
کے لئے مفکر نہیں ہے۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ کہ اگر روزہ دار نے غذایا دوا کوئی چیز عمدا کھا پی لی تو اس پر قضا اور کفارہ دونوں واجب ہوں گے اور امام شافعی نے فرما ہے کہ اس پر کفارہ واجب نہ ہوگا یہی قول امام احمد کا ہے۔ امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ روزہ کی حالت میں جماع کرنے سے کفارہ کی مشروعیت خلاف قیاس ثابت ہے کیونکہ تو بہ کی وجہ سے گناہ کا مرتفع ہو جانا حدیث سے ثابت ہے چنانچہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم کا ارشاد ہے التَّوب تَمْحُو الحَوبَةُ تو بہ گناہ کو مٹادیتی ہے لیکن جب ایک اعرابی رمضان کے روزے کی حالت میں اپنی بیوی کے ساتھ جماع کر کے نادم او شرمندہ ہو کر دربار رسالت میں حاضر ہوا تو اس کی تو بہ اور ندامت کا تقاضا یہی ہے کہ اس کا یہ گناہ دور ہو گیا ہوگا لیکن اس کے باوجود رسول اکرم نے اس پر کفار و صوم واجب کیا ہے پس معلوم ہوا کہ کفارہ کا ثبوت خلاف قیاس ہے اور جو چیز خلاف قیاس ثابت ہو اس پر دوسر؟ چیز کو قیاس نہیں کیا جاتا لہذا رمضان کے روزے میں کھانے پینے سے کفارہ واجب نہ ہوگا۔
اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ کفارہ کا تعلق افطار کی جنایت کے ساتھ ہے جو رمضان المبارک میں علی وجہ الکمال پائی جائے اور جنابینہ کاملہ جس طرح جماع کی صورت میں پائی جاتی ہے اسی طرح کھانے پینے کی صورت میں بھی پائی گئی لہذا کھانے پینے کی صورت میں بھی
کفارہ واجب ہوگا۔ وَبِايْجَابِ الإعتاق ... الخ سے امام شافعی کی دلیل کا جواب ہے: جواب کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ رمضان کے روزے میں جماع کا جنایت کا تو بہ سے مرتفع ہونا ہمیں تسلیم نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ شریعت نے اعتاق رقبہ کو اس جنایت کا کفارہ بنا کر واجب کیا ہے پس اگر تو اس جنایت کے لئے مکفر ہوتی تو بطور کفارہ کے اعتاق رقبہ واجب نہ کیا جاتا پس ثابت ہو گیا کہ یہ جنایت محض تو بہ سے دور نہیں ہوگی جید چوری اور زنا کی جنابیتیں تو سہ سے دور نہیں ہوتیں بلکہ حد سے دور ہوتی ہیں اور جب رمضان کے روزے میں جماع کرنے کی جنایت کفا سے دور ہوتی ہے تو کفارہ کا ثبوت خلاف قیاس نہ ہوا بلکہ قیاس کے مطابق ہوا اور جب یہ قیاس کے مطابق ہے تو اس پر دوسری چیز کو قیا
کرنا بھی جائز نہ ہوگا یعنی رمضان کے روزے میں کھانے پینے کی صورت میں وجوب کفارہ کو بھی اس پر قیاس کیا جا سکتا ہے۔
If he ate or drank something nourishing or something medicinal, then qada and kafarah are both necessary. Imam Shafi'i said: there is no kafarah upon him, because kafarah was legislated for the specific incident of intercourse against analogy; since sin is removed by repentance, it cannot be analogized to other acts. Our (Hanafi) proof: kafarah is attached to the crime of breaking the fast in Ramadan in a complete manner, and that has occurred; and by the requirement of freeing a slave as expiation, it is known that repentance does not expiate this crime. Translation: And if a fasting person eats or drinks something that provides nourishment or is used as medicine, then both qada and kafarah are wajib. Imam Shafi'i said: kafarah is not wajib upon him... Our proof is that kafarah is related to the complete crime of breaking the fast in Ramadan... And through making freeing a slave wajib as expiation, it is understood that repentance is not expiatory for this crime.
Source pages p. 221

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling on eating, drinking, or taking medicine while fasting in Ramadan. The Hanafi position is that both qada and kafarah are wajib for these acts if done intentionally. Imam al-Shafi'i (and Imam Ahmad) hold that kafarah is not required; only qada. Their reasoning: kafarah for fasting was only established for intercourse (the story of the Bedouin), which was a special case contrary to analogy (khilaf al-qiyas). Since tawbah removes sin, no other act can be analogized to intercourse. The Hanafi response: kafarah is triggered by the complete crime of breaking the fast, whether by intercourse or by food/drink. The fact that the Prophet ﷺ prescribed freeing a slave as kafarah for the Bedouin despite his repentance shows that tawbah does not remove the need for expiation. Thus, kafarah is not khilaf al-qiyas but rather in accordance with qiyas, and analogical extension to other forms of breaking the fast is valid.

Key Terms
خلاف قیاس (khilāf al-qiyās): A ruling that contradicts rational analogy, established solely by textual evidence.
مکفر (mukaffir): That which expiates sin, e.g., repentance or a prescribed act.
اعتاق رقبہ (iʿtāq raqabah): Freeing a slave, the primary form of kafarah for breaking the fast.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on a fasting person who intentionally eats food?
A) Only qada is required.
B) Both qada and kafarah are required.
C) Neither qada nor kafarah is required.
D) Only kafarah is required.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, any intentional consumption of food, drink, or medicine while fasting necessitates both qada and kafarah, based on analogy to intercourse and the principle that tawbah alone does not expiate the crime.

Kaffara for Eating/Drinking in Ramadan: Hanafi Qiyas vs. Shafi'i Exception
States ruling on eating/drinking and refutes Shafi'i position on kaffara

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi qiyas argument for requiring kaffara on eating/drinking and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument based on the concept of khilaaf al-qiyas.

Core Idea
Complete violation of the fast triggers kaffara whether by intercourse or eating/drinking — qiyas applies, not exception.

This passage addresses a well-known inter-madhhab dispute: does intentional eating or drinking in Ramadan require kaffara (expiation) in addition to qada (make-up)? The Hanafi school holds that it does, analogizing it to intercourse, while the Shafi'i school restricts kaffara to intercourse only. Understanding the qiyas reasoning — particularly the identification of the common 'illa — is essential for grasping Hanafi legal methodology in sawm.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling: the passage opens with 'if one eats or drinks... both qada and kaffara are obligatory.' This is the mufta bihi view in the Hanafi school.
The ruling is for any substance that provides nourishment or is medicinal.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i (and Ahmad) hold that only qada is required; kaffara is not due because the kaffara for intercourse was established contrary to analogy (khilaaf al-qiyas).
They argue that repentance alone removes sin, so the intercourse ruling is exceptional.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Analyze the Shafi'i dalil: they cite the hadith 'al-tawbu tamhu al-hawbah' (repentance erases sin) and the Bedouin incident where the Prophet prescribed kaffara despite repentance, showing it is an exception.
Thus, they claim the asl (intercourse) cannot be used for qiyas.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response has two parts: first, the 'illa is the complete violation (jinaayah kamilah), which is present in both intercourse and eating/drinking. Second, the prescription of emancipation proves that repentance is not sufficient – otherwise emancipation would be unnecessary.
This shows the asl ruling is not khilaaf al-qiyas; it is based on a clear 'illa.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: under Hanafi law, the violator must do both qada and kaffara; under Shafi'i, only qada. This affects the actual religious duties after breaking the fast.
The Hanafi position is the mufta bihi for Hanafi followers.

Source Text

اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ کفارہ کا تعلق افطار کی جنایت کے ساتھ ہے جو رمضان المبارک میں علی وجہ الکمال پائی جائے اور جنايت کاملہ جس طرح جماع کی صورت میں پائی جاتی ہے اسی طرح کھانے پینے کی صورت میں بھی پائی گئی لہذا کھانے پینے کی صورت میں بھی کفارہ واجب ہوگا۔ وَبِايْجَابِ الإعتاق ... الخ سے امام شافعی کی دلیل کا جواب ہے: جواب کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ رمضان کے روزے میں جماع کا جنایت کا تو بہ سے مرتفع ہونا ہمیں تسلیم نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ شریعت نے اعتاق رقبہ کو اس جنایت کا کفارہ بنا کر واجب کیا ہے پس اگر تو اس جنایت کے لئے مکفر ہوتی تو بطور کفارہ کے اعتاق رقبہ واجب نہ کیا جاتا پس ثابت ہو گیا کہ یہ جنایت محض تو بہ سے دور نہیں ہوگی جیسے چوری اور زنا کی جنايتيں توبہ سے دور نہیں ہوتیں بلکہ حد سے دور ہوتیں اور جب رمضان کے روزے میں جماع کرنے کی جنایت کفارہ سے دور ہوتی ہے تو کفارہ کا ثبوت خلاف قیاس نہ ہوا بلکہ قیاس کے مطابق ہوا اور جب یہ قیاس کے مطابق ہے تو اس پر دوسری چیز کو قیاس کرنا بھی جائز ہوگا یعنی رمضان کے روزے میں کھانے پینے کی صورت میں وجوب کفارہ کو بھی اس پر قیاس کیا جا سکتا ہے۔
If one eats or drinks something that provides nourishment or is used as medicine, both qada and kaffara are obligatory. Al-Shafi'i said: No kaffara is due, because kaffara was legislated for intercourse contrary to analogy, since the sin is removed by repentance, so other things cannot be analogized to it. Our proof: Kaffara is attached to the violation of breaking the fast in Ramadan in a complete manner, and that has occurred. And by the obligation of emancipation as expiation, it is known that repentance alone does not expiate this violation. (Urdu translation and commentary follow, explaining the Shafi'i argument using the hadith 'al-tawbu tamhu al-hawbah' and the Bedouin incident, then the Hanafi response that repentance does not suffice as shown by the obligation of emancipation, and that the violation is like theft and zina which require hadd, not just tawba, therefore kaffara is based on qiyas and eating/drinking can be analogized to intercourse.)
Source pages p. 221

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute. It begins by stating the Hanafi ruling: if a fasting person deliberately eats or drinks something nourishing or medicinal, they must perform both qada (make up the fast) and kaffara (expiation). Imam al-Shafi'i (and Imam Ahmad) hold that no kaffara is required, only qada. The Shafi'i argument is that kaffara for intercourse was established contrary to analogy (khilaaf al-qiyas) because repentance alone would ordinarily remove the sin, as indicated by the hadith 'al-tawbu tamhu al-hawbah' (repentance erases sin). The Bedouin who committed intercourse was repentant, yet the Prophet still prescribed kaffara; thus the ruling is exceptional and cannot be extended by qiyas to eating or drinking. The Hanafi response is twofold. First, the 'illa (effective cause) for kaffara is the complete violation of the fast (jinaayah kamilah), which applies equally to intercourse and eating/drinking. Second, the very fact that the Prophet prescribed emancipation as kaffara proves that repentance alone does not expiate this violation; otherwise, emancipation would be unnecessary. This is analogous to hadd penalties for theft and zina, which are not waived by repentance. Thus the kaffara ruling is not contrary to qiyas; it is based on the clear 'illa, and therefore eating/drinking is validly analogized to intercourse, requiring both qada and kaffara in Hanafi law.

Key Terms
كفارة (kaffaarah): Expiation required for intentionally breaking the fast in Ramadan; in Hanafi law, it is wajib for eating/drinking as well as intercourse.
قضاء (qadaa'): Making up a missed or invalidated fast on another day.
جناية (jinaayah): The act of breaking the fast intentionally; here it is the violation that triggers kaffara.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling for a person who intentionally eats during a Ramadan fast?
A) Only qada is required.
B) Only kaffara is required.
C) Both qada and kaffara are required.
D) Neither qada nor kaffara is required.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, intentional eating/drinking during Ramadan requires both qada and kaffara, justified by qiyas on intercourse with the 'illa of complete violation.

Kaffara of Fasting is Like Kaffara of Zihar: Evidence from Hadith
Establishes kaffara of fast as same as zihar using Bedouin hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the kaffara for intentional fast-breaking, explain the evidence from the Bedouin hadith, and distinguish it from the Shafi'i and Maliki positions.

Core Idea
The kaffara for fasting mirrors zihar: order (tartib) and consecutiveness (tataabu') are required, not optional.

This passage establishes that the kaffara for deliberately breaking the Ramadan fast is identical to the kaffara of zihar. The Hanafi school relies on the hadith of the Bedouin, where the Prophet commanded a strict sequence: free a slave, then fast two consecutive months, then feed sixty poor. This sequence and the requirement of consecutiveness are decisive proofs against the Shafi'i position of free choice and the Maliki position of non-consecutiveness.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi ruling
State the Hanafi position on the kaffara for intentional fast-breaking: it is like zihar, with tartib and tataabu'.
2
Locate the primary proof
Identify the Bedouin hadith as the dalil. Note its chain and that it is a Sunnah ahad with zanni thubut but qati dalala.
The hadith is found in Bukhari and Muslim.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
Examine how the hadith proves tartib: the Prophet's commands came in a fixed order. Prove tataabu': the explicit phrase 'shahrayni mutataabi'ayn'.
The sequence of 'free, then fast, then feed' indicates that each is contingent on inability to do the previous.
4
Identify the ikhtilaf
State the opposing views: Shafi'i gives free choice (takhyir); Malik does not require consecutiveness in fasting.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
Explain why the Hanafi position is mufta bihi: the text of the hadith is explicit and its implication (muqtada) is order, so it is decisive.

ثُمَّ قَالَ وَالْكَفَّارَةُ مِثْلُ كَفَّارَةِ الظَّهَارِ لِمَا رَوْيْنَا وَلِحَدِيْثِ الْأَعْرَابِي فَإِنَّهُ قَالَ يَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ هَلَكْتُ وَاهْلَكُتُ فَقَالَ مَاذَا صَنَعْتَ قَالَ وَافَعتُ امْرَأَتِي فِى نَهَارِ رَمَضَانَ مُتَعَمِّدًا فَقَالَ اَعْدِق رَقَبَةً فَقَالَ لَا أَمْلِكُ إِلَّا رَقَتِي هَذِهِ فَقَالَ صُمْ شَهْرَيْنِ مُتَتَابِعَيْنِ فَقَالَ هَلْ جَاءَ نِى مَا جَاءَ إِلَّا مِنَ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ مسلسل ( بلا ناغہ ) دو ماہ کے روزے رکھو اس نے کہا کہ جو کچھ مجھ پر آیا ہے وہ روزہ ہی کی وجہ سے آیا ہے آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ ساٹھ مسکینوں کو کھانا کھلا دو اس عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ ان کو مساکین پر تقسیم کر دو اس اعرابی نے کہا کہ خدا کی قسم مدینہ کی دونوں لابتوں کے درمیان مجھ سے اور میری عیال سے زیادہ ضر روتمند کوئی نہیں ہے آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ تو اور تیری عیال کھالے یہ تیرے لئے کافی ہوگا اور تیرے بعد کسی کے لئے کافی نہ ہوگا اور یہ حدیث امام شافعی کے خلاف حجت ہے ان کے اس قول میں کہ اس کو اختیار ہے کیونکہ حدیث کا مقتضی ترتیب ہے اور یہ حدیث امام مالک کے خلاف حجت ہے پے در پے کی نفی کرنے میں کیونکہ تابع پر نص وارد ہے۔ تشریح امام قدوری نے فرمایا کہ روزہ کا کفارہ ظہار کے کفارہ کے مانند ہے اور ظہار کا کفارہ یہ ہے کہ مظاہر یعنی ظہار کرنے والا ایک رقبہ آزاد کرے اور اگر اس کی قدرت نہ ہو تو بلا ناغہ دو ماہ کے روزے رکھے اور اگر یہ بھی بس میں نہ ہو تو ساٹھ مسکینوں کو کھانا کھلا دے چنانچہ ٹھائیسویں پارے کے پہلے رکوع میں ہے وَالَّذِينَ يُظَاهِرُونَ مِنْ نِسَائِهِمْ ثُمَّ يَعُودُونَ لِمَا قَالُوا فَتَحْرِيرُ رَقَبَةٍ مِنْ قَبل أد يتَمَاسًا ذَالِكُمْ تُوعَظُونَ بِهِ وَاللَّهُ بِمَا تَعْمَلُونَ خَبِيرٌ ، فَمَنْ لَمْ يَجِدُ فَصِيَامُ شَهْرَينِ مُتَتَابِعَيْنِ مِنْ قَبْلِ أَنْ يَتَمَاسًا فَمَنْ لَّمْ يَسْتَطِعْ فَبِإِطْعَامُ سِيِّينَ مِسْكِيناً یعنی جو لوگ ماں کہ بیٹھیں اپنی عورتوں کو پھر کرنا چاہیں یہی کام جس کو کہا ہے تو آزاد کرنا چاہئے ایک رقبہ پہلے اس سے کہ آپس میں ہاتھ لگا ئیں۔ اس سے تم کو نصیحت ہوگی اور اللہ خبر رکھتا ہے جو کچھ تم کرتے ہو، پھر جو کوئی نہ پائے تو روزے ہیں دومارہ کے لگاتار پہلے اس سے کہ آپ میں چھوئیں پھر جو کوئی یہ نہ کر سکے تو کھانا دینا ہے ساتھ محتاجوں کا بہر حال کفارہ صوم کفارہ ظہار کے عین مطابق ہے یعنی مذکورہ تین چیزوں (غلام کی آزادی ، دو ماہ کے روزے ، ساتھ مسکینوں کا کھانا ) میں وہی ترتیب ملحوظ ہو گی جو کفارہ ظہار میں مذکور ہے یعنی غلام آزاد کرے اس پر قدرت نہ ہونے کی صورت میں دو ماہ کے لگا تار بلا ناغہ روزے رکھے اور اس پر قادر نہ ہونے کی صورت میں ساٹھ کینوں کو کھا نا دیدے۔ حضرت امام شافعی ان تینوں چیزوں کے درمیان اختیار دیتے ہیں یعنی اگر کوئی شخص غلام آزاد
Then he said: The kaffara is like the kaffara of zihar, due to what we have narrated and due to the hadith of the Bedouin: He said, 'O Messenger of Allah, I have destroyed myself and destroyed others.' He (ﷺ) said, 'What did you do?' He said, 'I deliberately had intercourse with my wife during the day of Ramadan.' He said, 'Free a slave.' He said, 'I do not possess any slave except this one of mine.' He said, 'Fast two consecutive months.' He said, 'The very thing that brought me here came from fasting.' He said, 'Feed sixty poor people.' He said, 'I cannot find [the means].' So the Messenger ordered that a faraq of dates be brought—and it is also narrated as 'irq containing fifteen sa' of dates—and said, 'Distribute them among the poor.' The Bedouin said, 'By Allah, there is no one between the two lava fields of Madinah more needy than me and my family.' He said, 'Eat, you and your family; it will suffice for you, and it will not suffice for anyone after you.' This hadith is an argument against al-Shafi'i in his saying that one has a choice, because its implication is order (tartib), and against Malik in denying consecutiveness (tataabu') because the text explicitly mentions it. (Then Urdu translation and commentary follow, explaining the parallel with zihar kaffara and citing Quran 58:3-4.)
Source pages p. 222

Commentary
This passage explains the nature of the kaffara for breaking the fast intentionally. It states that the kaffara is exactly like the kaffara of zihar (a form of pre-Islamic divorce). The proof is the well-known hadith of the Bedouin who had intercourse during Ramadan. The Prophet (ﷺ) commanded him first to free a slave, then to fast two consecutive months, and then to feed sixty poor people. This sequence (tartib) is crucial: one must follow this order, not choose freely. The hadith also explicitly requires the two months to be consecutive (mutataabi'ayn), refuting Imam Malik's view that consecutiveness is not necessary. The passage then quotes the Quranic verses from Surah al-Mujadilah (58:3-4) to confirm the same order and consecutiveness for zihar kaffara, establishing that the fast kaffara mirrors it. Imam al-Shafi'i held that one may choose any of the three options (takhyir), but the hadith's implication (muqtada) is tartib, not takhyir. Imam Malik held that the fast need not be consecutive, but the text explicitly says 'shahrayni mutataabi'ayn'. Thus the hadith is a decisive proof (hujjah) against both. The practical outcome: in the Hanafi school, the kaffara obligation for intentional fast-breaking follows the same order as zihar: free a slave; if unable, fast two consecutive months; if unable, feed sixty poor people. One cannot skip the first option if capable, nor break the consecutiveness of the fasts.

Key Terms
كفارة الظهار (kaffaarat al-zihaar): The expiation for zihar, which consists of three options in order: freeing a slave, fasting two consecutive months, or feeding sixty poor people.
ترتيب (tartib): The required order in performing the three options of kaffara: one must attempt the first before moving to the next.
متتابع (mutataabi'): Consecutive, without interruption. Used for the two-month fast in kaffara.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the correct sequence for the kaffara of intentionally breaking the Ramadan fast?
A) Fast two months, then free a slave, then feed sixty poor.
B) Free a slave; if unable, fast two consecutive months; if unable, feed sixty poor.
C) Choose any one of the three options freely.
D) Feed sixty poor; if unable, fast two months; if unable, free a slave.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires tartib and tataabu' in kaffara for fast-breaking, based on the explicit sequence and wording of the Bedouin hadith.

Sawm — Fasting

8 min
Kaffarah for Breaking the Fast: Sequence and Consecutiveness
Establishes kaffarah of fasting equals zihar kaffarah and refutes Shafi'i and Malik

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the kaffarah for intentionally breaking the fast in Ramadan, explain the sequential obligation and requirement of consecutiveness, and evaluate the Shafi'i and Maliki counter-arguments.

Core Idea
Kaffarah for fasting is like zihar kaffarah: sequential obligation with two consecutive months of fasting.

When a person intentionally breaks the Ramadan fast by intercourse, a major expiation becomes wajib. The Hanafi school holds that this kaffarah follows the same structure as the kaffarah of zihar: a strict sequential order starting with freeing a slave, then fasting two consecutive months, then feeding sixty poor people. This lesson examines the proof from the hadith of the Bedouin (al-A'rabi) and how it refutes the views of Imam al-Shafi'i, who allows a free choice among the three options, and Imam Malik, who does not require the two-month fast to be consecutive. Understanding this dispute is crucial for correctly applying the kaffarah in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that the act in question is intentionally breaking the fast in Ramadan by intercourse. The Hanafi school classifies the kaffarah as wajib. Note that the ruling is derived from the hadith and qiyas on zihar.
2
State the Hanafi position with its proof
The Hanafi position: the kaffarah is exactly like that of zihar, with a sequential obligation: free a slave, if unable then fast two consecutive months, if unable then feed sixty poor people. The primary proof is the hadith of the Bedouin, where the Prophet (peace be upon him) issued the commands in order without using the word 'or', indicating tartib. Additionally, the phrase 'two consecutive months' explicitly requires tataabu'.
The hadith is sahih and found in Bukhari and Muslim.
3
Identify the opposing schools and their arguments
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that one may choose any of the three options (takhyeer), citing a hadith with the word 'aw' (or). Imam Malik (or, as corrected, Ibn Abi Layla) holds that the two-month fast need not be consecutive, drawing analogy (qiyas) with qada' fasts where consecutiveness is not required.
The text in al-Hidayah may have misattributed; the correction notes it is Ibn Abi Layla who held both views.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response: The hadith of Sa'd (used by Shafi'i) is weak or contradicted by the explicit sequential command in the more authentic Bedouin hadith. As for the qiyas on qada', it is invalid because kaffarah is a penalty, not a makeup, and the text explicitly says 'consecutive'. The explicit text (nass) overrides qiyas.
In Hanafi usul, nass prevails over qiyas.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Under the Hanafi view, one must follow the sequence: cannot skip to feeding if able to fast, and the fast must be consecutive. Under Shafi'i, one may choose any option regardless of ability. Under the corrected Maliki/Ibn Abi Layla view, the fast could be non-consecutive. The Hanafi position is mufta bihi, relied upon for fatwa.
The difference affects validity of kaffarah in practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثُمَّ قَالَ وَالْكَفَّارَةُ مِثْلُ كَفَّارَةِ الظَّهَارِ لِمَا رَوْيْنَا وَلِحَدِيْثِ الْأَعْرَابِي فَإِنَّهُ قَالَ يَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ هَلَكْتُ وَاهْلَكُتُ فَقَالَ مَاذَا صَنَعْتَ قَالَ وَافَعتُ امْرَأَتِي فِى نَهَارِ رَمَضَانَ مُتَعَمِّدًا فَقَالَ اَعْدِق رَقَبَةً فَقَالَ لَا أَمْلِكُ إِلَّا رَقَتِي هَذِهِ فَقَالَ صُمْ شَهْرَيْنِ مُتَتَابِعَيْنِ فَقَالَ هَلْ جَاءَ نِى مَا جَاءَ إِلَّا مِنَ الصَّوْمِ فَقَالَ أَطْعِمُ سِيِّينَ مَسْكِينًا فَقَالَ لَا أَجِدُ فَأَمَرَ رَسُولُ أَنْ يُؤْتَى بِفَرَقٍ مِنْ تَمَرٍ وَيُرْوَى بَعَرقِ فِيهِ تَمَرُ خَمْسَةَ عَشَرَ صَاعًا وَ قَالَ فَرَقْهَا عَلَى الْمَسَاكِينِ فَقَالَ وَاللهِ مَابَيْنَ لَابَتَي المَدِينَةِ أَحَدٌ أَحَوَجُ مِنِى وَمِنْ عَيَالِى فَقَالَ كُل أَنتَ وَ عَمَالُكَ يَجْزِيْكَ وَلَا يُجْزِى أَحَدًا بَعْدَكَ وَهُوَ حُجَّةٌ عَلَى الشَّافِعِي فِى قَوْلِه يُخَيَّرُ لأَنَّ مُقْتَضَاهُ التَّرْتِيبَ وَ عَلى مَالِكَ فِى نَفْيِ التَّتَابِعِ لِلنَّصِ عَلَيْهِ
Then he said: The expiation is like the expiation of zihar due to what we have narrated and due to the hadith of the Bedouin: he said, 'O Messenger of Allah, I am destroyed and have destroyed.' He said, 'What have you done?' He said, 'I intentionally had intercourse with my wife during the day of Ramadan.' He said, 'Free a slave.' He said, 'I possess only this neck of mine.' He said, 'Fast two consecutive months.' He said, 'Nothing has come to me except from the fast.' He said, 'Feed sixty poor persons.' He said, 'I cannot find.' So the Messenger ordered that a farq of dates be brought—and it is narrated as 'irq containing fifteen sa' of dates—and he said, 'Distribute them among the poor.' He said, 'By Allah, there is no one between the two lava plains of Madinah more in need than me and my family.' He said, 'Eat, you and your family; it will suffice for you, and it will not suffice for anyone after you.' And it is an argument against al-Shafi'i in his saying that one has a choice, because its implication is order; and against Malik in negating consecutiveness, because of the explicit text on it.
Source pages p. 222

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute establishing the Hanafi position on the kaffarah (expiation) for intentionally breaking the fast in Ramadan. The author states that the kaffarah is exactly like the kaffarah of zihar (a form of divorce), which is based on the Quranic verse in Surah al-Mujadilah: free a slave, if unable then fast two consecutive months, if unable then feed sixty poor people. This sequence is obligatory, not a choice. The proof is the hadith of the Bedouin who broke his fast and the Prophet (peace be upon him) ordered him in a specific order: first freeing a slave, then fasting, then feeding. This hadith clearly shows the order (tartib) and the requirement of consecutive fasting (tataabu'). The Hanafi school uses this hadith to refute Imam al-Shafi'i, who allows a choice between the three options (takhyeer), and Imam Malik, who does not require consecutiveness in the fast. The text also notes a correction: the author of al-Hidayah may have erred in attributing these views to Shafi'i and Malik; in fact, it is Ibn Abi Layla who holds both choice and non-consecutiveness. The Hanafi position is the relied-upon view (mufta bihi) in the madhhab, based on the explicit text of the hadith and the clear sequential command from the Prophet.

Key Terms
الكفارة (al-kaffarah): The expiation for intentionally invalidating the fast in Ramadan by intercourse; it consists of freeing a slave, fasting two consecutive months, or feeding sixty poor people, in that obligatory order.
التتابع (al-tataabu'): The condition that the two months of fasting be consecutive without break; required in kaffarah for fasting.
التخيير (al-takhyeer): The view that one may choose any of the three expiatory acts (freeing, fasting, feeding) without needing to follow a sequence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the correct order of kaffarah for intentionally breaking the fast in Ramadan?
A) Free a slave, if unable then fast two consecutive months, if unable then feed sixty poor people.
B) One may choose any of the three options: free a slave, fast two months, or feed sixty poor people.
C) Feed sixty poor people first, then fast two months, then free a slave.
D) Fast two consecutive months, if unable then free a slave, if unable then feed sixty poor people.

Key Takeaway
The kaffarah for breaking the fast in the Hanafi school follows a strict sequential order with consecutive fasting, based on the hadith of the Bedouin.

Intercourse Outside the Private Parts: Qada Required, No Kaffarah
Ruling statement with rational proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi distinction between ma'nan and suratan of intercourse to determine when qada and kaffarah are required for invalidating the fast.

Core Idea
Intercourse in meaning (ma'nan) triggers qada; only intercourse in form (suratan) triggers kaffarah.

A fasting person engages in sexual activity but without full penetration—perhaps rubbing on the thigh or belly. Does this break the fast? If so, what is the consequence? The Hanafi school provides a nuanced answer: the act is invalidating because it constitutes intercourse in meaning (ma'nan), but the severe expiation (kaffarah) is reserved for the complete act of intercourse in form (suratan). This passage explains the ruling and its rational proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is non-penetrative sexual contact (e.g., between thighs or on belly) that leads to ejaculation. The ruling: qada (make-up) is wajib, kaffarah (expiation) is not.
Contrast with full intercourse (penetration of vagina or anus) which requires both qada and kaffarah.
2
Understand the two concepts: ma'nan and suratan
Intercourse in meaning (ma'nan) refers to the essential reason for invalidation: the ejaculation resulting from sexual activity. Intercourse in form (suratan) refers to the literal physical act: insertion of the private part into the private part.
Hanafi fiqh uses these concepts to calibrate rulings: the former triggers qada, the latter triggers the more severe kaffarah.
3
Apply the distinction to the case
Since ejaculation occurred through sexual contact, the fast is invalidated (ma'nan exists), so qada is required. But the absence of actual penetration (suratan missing) means kaffarah is not required.
The passage explicitly defines farj as the front and back private parts; only penetration of these constitutes suratan.
4
Note the cross-madhhab implication
The Shafi'i school may hold that deliberate ejaculation alone, even without penetration, suffices for kaffarah. The Hanafi position is more lenient in this respect.
This distinction is a point of ikhtilaf; the operative fatwa (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school is as stated.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مادون الفرج میں جماع کیا اور انزال بھی ہو گیا قضا ہے کفارہ نہیں
وَمَنْ جَامَعَ فِيْمَا دُونَ الْفَرُ فَانْزَلَ فَعَلَيْهِ الْقَضَاءُ لِوُجُودِ الْجِمَاعِ مَعْنَى وَلَا كَفَّارَةَ عَلَيْهِ لِإِنْعِدَامِهِ صُورَةً ترجمہ اور جس نے فرج کے علاوہ جماع کیا پھر اس کو انزال ہو گیا تو اس پر قضا واجب ہے کیونکہ معنی جماع پایا گیا اور اس پر کفارہ واجب نہیں ہے کیونکہ صور جماع معدوم ہو گیا۔ تشریح فرج سے مراد قبل اور ڈیر ہے اب مطلب یہ ہوا کہ اگر قبل اور دبر کے علاوہ میں مثلاً رانوں میں یا پیٹ میں بحالت روز وذکر کا استعمال کیا اور انزال ہو گیا تو اس پر قضا واجب ہوگی کفارہ واجب نہ ہوگا۔ قضا تو اس لئے واجب ہوگی کہ معنی جماع پایا گیا اور کفارہ اس لئے واجب نہ ہوگا کہ صورۃ جماع نہیں پایا گیا کیونکہ صورۃ جامع کے لئے ادخال فرج فی الفرج ضروری ہے اور وہ پایا نہیں گیا۔
Intercourse in what is below the private part and he had an emission: qada (make-up) is required, not kaffarah.
And whoever has intercourse in what is below the private part and has an emission, upon him is qada due to the existence of intercourse in meaning, and no kaffarah upon him due to its absence in form. Translation: And whoever has intercourse other than the private part and then has an emission, upon him qada is obligated because the meaning of intercourse is found, and kaffarah is not obligated because the form of intercourse is absent. Explanation: By 'private part' (farj) is meant the front and the back. The meaning is that if he uses his organ in something other than the front and back, for example on the thighs or belly while fasting, and he has an emission, then qada is obligatory, kaffarah is not obligatory. Qada is obligatory because the meaning of intercourse is found; kaffarah is not obligatory because the form of intercourse is not found, because for the form of intercourse, insertion of the private part into the private part is necessary, and that is not found.
Source pages p. 224

Commentary
This is a ruling statement with rational proof. The passage addresses the situation of a person who, while fasting in Ramadan, engages in intercourse-like activity that does not involve actual penetration of the vagina or anus (madun al-faraj). If he inserts his organ between the thighs or against the stomach and has an emission, then the fast is invalidated and he must make it up (qada) because in meaning (ma'nan) this constitutes intercourse: it involves the act of ejaculation through sexual contact, which breaks the fast. However, no expiation (kaffarah) is required because the full form (suratan) of intercourse—actual insertion of the private part into the private part—did not occur. The Hanafi school distinguishes between the essence of intercourse (which is the act causing ejaculation) and its complete form, which is required for kaffarah. The passage specifically defines farj as the private parts (front and back), i.e., the vagina and anus. Only direct insertion into these invalidates the fast with both qada and kaffarah.

Key Terms
فرج (farj): The private parts: specifically the front (vagina) and back (anus).
معنی (ma'nan): In meaning: the essence or legal significance of an act, as opposed to its literal form.
صورۃ (suratan): In form: the literal, physical act as defined legally, e.g., insertion of private part into private part.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A person fasting in Ramadan rubs his organ on his thighs until he ejaculates. What is the ruling?
A) Both qada and kaffarah required.
B) Only qada required, no kaffarah.
C) No qada and no kaffarah.
D) Only kaffarah required, no qada.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes between the meaning (ma'nan) and form (suratan) of intercourse; qada is required for the former, kaffarah only for the latter.
